transcriber’s notes e-text:
 
e-text prepared pelican classics edition leviathan,
 turn prepared first edition. tried to
 follow closely possible original, give flavour of
 text hobbes proof-read, following differences
 unavoidable.
 
hobbes used capitals italics extensively, emphasis, for
 proper names, quotations, sometimes, seems, just because.
 
original extensive margin notes, used show
 introduces definitions words concepts, give in
 short subject paragraph section dealing with, to
 give references quotations, largely exclusively biblical.
 degree, margin notes seem intended serve
 place index, original none. italics.
 
also used italics words languages english, and
 number greek words, greek alphabet, text.
 
deal within limits plain vanilla ascii, done
 following e-text.
 
restricted use full capitalization places where
 hobbes used it, except chapter headings, fully
 capitalized, hobbes used mixture full capitalization and
 italics.
 
clear italics indicate text quoting,
 introduced quotation marks. within quotation marks have
 retained capitalization hobbes used.
 
italics seem used emphasis, proper names, just
 because, capitalized initial letter words. has
 disadvantage distinguished that
 hobbes capitalized plain text, extent italics would
 make text ugly use underscore slash.
 
margin notes either introduce paragraph subject,
 show introduces word definitions, included as
 headers paragraph, words initial capitals,
 shortened line.
 
margin references quotes, included text,
 brackets immediately next quotation. hobbes included
 references main text, left put them, except to
 change square brackets round.
 
greek alphabet, simply substituted nearest ordinary
 letters can, used initial capitals foreign
 language words.
 
neither thomas hobbes typesetters seem many
 inhibitions spelling punctuation. tried reproduce
 exactly, exception introduction quotation marks.
 
preparing text, found much meaning if
 read sub-vocalization, aloud, rather trying read
 silently. hobbes’ use emphasis eccentric punctuation and
 construction seem work.
 


honor’d friend mr. francis godolphin godolphin
 

honor’d sir.
 
worthy brother mr sidney godolphin, lived, pleas’d
 think studies something, otherwise oblige me, know,
 reall testimonies good opinion, great themselves, the
 greater worthinesse person. vertue
 disposeth man, either service god, service
 country, civill society, private friendship, not
 manifestly appear conversation, acquired necessity,
 affected upon occasion, inhaerent, shining generous
 constitution nature. therefore honour gratitude him,
 devotion selfe, humbly dedicate unto my
 discourse common-wealth. know world will receive it,
 may reflect shall seem favour it. a
 way beset contend one side great liberty, and
 side much authority, ’tis hard passe the
 points unwounded. yet, thinks, endeavour advance
 civill power, civill power condemned; nor
 private men, reprehending it, declare think power too
 great. besides, speak men, (in abstract) the
 seat power, (like simple unpartiall creatures the
 roman capitol, noyse defended within it, not
 they, there) offending none, think, those
 without, within (if such) favour them. that
 perhaps may offend, certain texts holy scripture,
 alledged purpose ordinarily use by
 others. done due submission, also (in order to
 subject) necessarily; outworks enemy, from
 whence impugne civill power. notwithstanding this, find
 labour generally decryed, may pleased excuse selfe,
 say man love opinions, think true i
 say, honoured brother, honour you, presum’d on
 that, assume title (without knowledge) being, am,
 
sir,
 
humble, obedient servant, thomas hobbes.
 
paris aprill 15/25 1651.

introduction
 

nature (the art whereby god hath made governes world) the
 art man, many things, also imitated, it
 can make artificial animal. seeing life motion limbs,
 begining whereof principall part within; may not
 say, automata (engines move springs and
 wheeles doth watch) artificiall life? the
 heart, spring; nerves, many strings; the
 joynts, many wheeles, giving motion whole body, as
 intended artificer? art goes yet further, imitating that
 rationall excellent worke nature, man. art created
 great leviathan called common-wealth, state, (in latine
 civitas) artificiall man; though greater stature
 strength naturall, whose protection defence it
 intended; which, soveraignty artificiall soul, as
 giving life motion whole body; magistrates, other
 officers judicature execution, artificiall joynts; reward and
 punishment (by fastned seat soveraignty, every joynt
 member moved performe duty) nerves, the
 body naturall; wealth riches particular
 members, strength; salus populi (the peoples safety) its
 businesse; counsellors, things needfull know,
 suggested unto it, memory; equity lawes, artificiall
 reason will; concord, health; sedition, sicknesse; civill war,
 death. lastly, pacts covenants, parts body
 politique first made, set together, united, resemble that
 fiat, let us make man, pronounced god creation.
 
describe nature artificiall man, will consider
 
first matter thereof, artificer; man.
 
secondly, how, covenants made; rights and
 just power authority soveraigne; preserveth
 dissolveth it.
 
thirdly, christian common-wealth.
 
lastly, kingdome darkness.
 
concerning first, saying much usurped late, that
 wisedome acquired, reading books, men. consequently
 whereunto, persons, part can give proof
 wise, take great delight shew think read
 men, uncharitable censures one another behind backs.
 another saying late understood, might
 learn truly read one another, take pains; that
 is, nosce teipsum, read thy self: meant, now
 used, countenance, either barbarous state men power,
 towards inferiors; encourage men low degree, a
 sawcie behaviour towards betters; teach us, the
 similitude thoughts, passions one man, thoughts,
 passions another, whosoever looketh himselfe, and
 considereth doth, think, opine, reason, hope,
 feare, &c, upon grounds; shall thereby read know,
 thoughts, passions men, upon like
 occasions. say similitude passions, all
 men, desire, feare, hope, &c; similitude objects the
 passions, things desired, feared, hoped, &c: the
 constitution individuall, particular education vary, they
 easie kept knowledge, characters mans
 heart, blotted confounded are, dissembling, lying,
 counterfeiting, erroneous doctrines, legible onely that
 searcheth hearts. though mens actions wee discover their
 designee sometimes; yet without comparing own,
 distinguishing circumstances, case may come to
 altered, decypher without key, part
 deceived, much trust, much diffidence; that
 reads, himselfe good evill man.
 
let one man read another actions never perfectly, it
 serves onely acquaintance, few. is
 govern whole nation, must read himselfe, this, that
 particular man; man-kind; though hard do, harder than
 learn language, science; yet, shall set my
 reading orderly, perspicuously, pains left another, will be
 onely consider, also find himselfe. this
 kind doctrine, admitteth demonstration.
 



part i.
 man
 



chapter i. sense
 

concerning thoughts man, will consider first singly, and
 afterwards trayne, dependance upon one another. singly, they
 every one representation apparence, quality, other
 accident body without us; commonly called object. which
 object worketh eyes, eares, parts mans body; by
 diversity working, produceth diversity apparences.
 
originall all, call sense; (for is
 conception mans mind, hath first, totally, by
 parts, begotten upon organs sense.) rest derived
 originall.
 
know naturall cause sense, necessary the
 business now hand; els-where written large.
 nevertheless, fill part present method, will briefly
 deliver place.
 
cause sense, externall body, object, presseth the
 organ proper sense, either immediatly, tast touch;
 mediately, seeing, hearing, smelling: pressure, by
 mediation nerves, strings, membranes body,
 continued inwards brain, heart, causeth resistance,
 counter-pressure, endeavour heart, deliver self:
 endeavour outward, seemeth matter without. and
 seeming, fancy, men call sense; consisteth, as
 eye, light, colour figured; eare, sound; to
 nostrill, odour; tongue palat, savour; and
 rest body, heat, cold, hardnesse, softnesse, such
 qualities, discern feeling. qualities called
 sensible, object causeth them, many several
 motions matter, presseth organs diversly. neither
 us pressed, anything els, divers motions; (for
 motion, produceth nothing motion.) apparence us is
 fancy, waking, dreaming. pressing, rubbing,
 striking eye, makes us fancy light; pressing eare,
 produceth dinne; bodies also see, hear, produce the
 strong, though unobserved action, colours,
 sounds, bodies, objects cause them, could
 bee severed them, glasses, ecchoes reflection,
 wee see are; know thing see, one place; the
 apparence, another. though certain distance, reall,
 object seem invested fancy begets us; yet still
 object one thing, image fancy another. sense in
 cases, nothing els originall fancy, caused (as said)
 pressure, is, motion, externall things upon our
 eyes, eares, organs thereunto ordained.
 
philosophy-schooles, universities of
 christendome, grounded upon certain texts aristotle, teach another
 doctrine; say, cause vision, thing seen, sendeth
 forth every side visible species(in english) visible shew,
 apparition, aspect, seen; receiving whereof the
 eye, seeing. cause hearing, thing heard,
 sendeth forth audible species, is, audible aspect, audible
 seen; entring eare, maketh hearing. nay the
 cause understanding also, say thing understood sendeth forth
 intelligible species, is, intelligible seen; which
 comming understanding, makes us understand. say this,
 disapproving use universities: speak
 hereafter office common-wealth, must let see on
 occasions way, things amended them; amongst
 frequency insignificant speech one.
 


chapter ii. imagination
 

thing lies still, unlesse somewhat els stirre it, will
 lye still ever, truth man doubts of. a
 thing motion, will eternally motion, unless somewhat els
 stay it, though reason same, (namely, nothing can change
 selfe,) easily assented to. men measure, onely
 men, things, themselves: find
 subject motion pain, lassitude, think every
 thing els growes weary motion, seeks repose accord;
 little considering, whether motion, wherein that
 desire rest find themselves, consisteth. hence is,
 schooles say, heavy bodies fall downwards, appetite
 rest, conserve nature place proper
 them; ascribing appetite, knowledge good their
 conservation, (which man has) things inanimate absurdly.
 
body motion, moveth (unless something els hinder
 it) eternally; whatsoever hindreth it, instant, in
 time, degrees quite extinguish it: wee see water,
 though wind cease, waves give rowling long
 time after; also happeneth motion, made the
 internall parts man, then, sees, dreams, &c. the
 object removed, eye shut, wee still retain image the
 thing seen, though obscure see it. it,
 latines call imagination, image made seeing; apply
 same, though improperly, senses. greeks
 call fancy; signifies apparence, proper one sense,
 another. imagination therefore nothing decaying sense; and
 found men, many living creatures, well sleeping, as
 waking.
 



memory
 
decay sense men waking, decay motion made in
 sense; obscuring it, manner, light sun
 obscureth light starres; starrs less exercise
 vertue visible, day, night.
 amongst many stroaks, eyes, eares, other
 organs receive externall bodies, predominant onely sensible;
 therefore light sun predominant, affected
 action starrs. object removed our
 eyes, though impression made us remain; yet objects more
 present succeeding, working us, imagination past is
 obscured, made weak; voyce man noyse the
 day. whence followeth, longer time is, the
 sight, sense object, weaker imagination. the
 continuall change mans body, destroyes time parts in
 sense moved: distance time, place, hath one
 effect us. distance place, wee
 look at, appears dimme, without distinction smaller parts;
 voyces grow weak, inarticulate: also great distance
 time, imagination past weak; wee lose( example)
 cities wee seen, many particular streets; actions, many
 particular circumstances. decaying sense, wee express
 thing self, (i mean fancy selfe,) wee call imagination, i
 said before; express decay, signifie the
 sense fading, old, past, called memory. imagination
 memory, one thing, divers considerations hath
 divers names.
 
much memory, memory many things, called experience. againe,
 imagination things formerly
 perceived sense, either once, parts severall
 times; former, (which imagining whole object, was
 presented sense) simple imagination; one imagineth a
 man, horse, hath seen before. compounded; as
 sight man one time, horse another, we
 conceive mind centaure. man compoundeth image of
 person, image actions man; a
 man imagins himselfe hercules, alexander, (which happeneth often
 much taken reading romants) compound
 imagination, properly fiction mind. also other
 imaginations rise men, (though waking) great impression
 made sense; gazing upon sun, impression leaves an
 image sun eyes long time after; long
 vehemently attent upon geometricall figures, man shall the
 dark, (though awake) images lines, angles his
 eyes: kind fancy hath particular name; thing that
 doth commonly fall mens discourse.
 



dreams
 
imaginations sleep, call dreams. these
 also (as imaginations) before, either totally, or
 parcells sense. sense, brain, nerves,
 necessary organs sense, benummed sleep, as
 easily moved action externall objects, can
 happen sleep, imagination; therefore dreame, what
 proceeds agitation inward parts mans body; which
 inward parts, connexion brayn, other
 organs, distempered, keep motion; whereby
 imaginations formerly made, appeare man waking;
 saving organs sense now benummed, is
 new object, can master obscure vigorous
 impression, dreame must needs cleare, silence of
 sense, waking thoughts. hence cometh pass, that
 hard matter, many thought impossible distinguish
 exactly sense dreaming. part, consider, that
 dreames, often, constantly think persons,
 places, objects, actions waking; remember long a
 trayne coherent thoughts, dreaming, times; because
 waking often observe absurdity dreames, never dream of
 absurdities waking thoughts; well satisfied, being
 awake, know dreame not; though dreame, think selfe
 awake.
 
seeing dreames caused distemper inward
 parts body; divers distempers must needs cause different dreams.
 hence is, lying cold breedeth dreams feare, raiseth
 thought image fearfull object (the motion the
 brain inner parts, inner parts brain being
 reciprocall:) anger causeth heat parts body,
 awake; sleep, heating parts
 causeth anger, raiseth brain imagination enemy.
 manner; naturall kindness, awake causeth
 desire; desire makes heat certain parts body; so
 also, much heat parts, wee sleep, raiseth the
 brain imagination kindness shewn. summe, dreams are
 reverse waking imaginations; motion awake,
 beginning one end; dream, another.
 



apparitions visions
 
difficult discerning mans dream, waking thoughts,
 then, accident observe slept:
 easie happen man full fearfull thoughts; and
 whose conscience much troubled; sleepeth, without the
 circumstances, going bed, putting clothes, one that
 noddeth chayre. taketh pains, industriously layes
 himselfe sleep, case uncouth exorbitant fancy come unto
 him, easily think dream. read marcus
 brutes, (one life given julius caesar, also
 favorite, notwithstanding murthered him,) phillipi,
 night gave battell augustus caesar, saw fearfull
 apparition, commonly related historians vision: but
 considering circumstances, one may easily judge but
 short dream. sitting tent, pensive troubled the
 horrour rash act, hard him, slumbering the
 cold, dream affrighted him; feare, by
 degrees made wake; also must needs make apparition by
 degrees vanish: assurance slept, have
 cause think dream, thing vision. no
 rare accident: even perfectly awake, be
 timorous, supperstitious, possessed fearfull tales, alone
 dark, subject like fancies, believe see
 spirits dead mens ghosts walking churchyards; whereas is
 either fancy onely, els knavery persons, make
 use superstitious feare, pass disguised night, to
 places known haunt.
 
ignorance distinguish dreams, strong
 fancies, vision sense, arise greatest part the
 religion gentiles time past, worshipped satyres, fawnes,
 nymphs, like; now adayes opinion rude people have
 fayries, ghosts, goblins; power witches. for
 witches, think witch craft reall power; yet
 justly punished, false beliefe have, that
 can mischiefe, joyned purpose they
 can; trade neerer new religion, craft or
 science. fayries, walking ghosts, opinion i
 think purpose, either taught, confuted, keep in
 credit use exorcisme, crosses, holy water, such
 inventions ghostly men. neverthelesse, doubt, god can
 make unnaturall apparitions. often, men need
 feare things, feare stay, change, the
 course nature, also can stay, change, point of
 christian faith. evill men pretext god can thing,
 bold say thing serves turn, though
 think untrue; part wise man, believe no
 further, right reason makes say, appear credible.
 superstitious fear spirits taken away, it,
 prognostiques dreams, false prophecies, many things
 depending thereon, which, crafty ambitious persons abuse the
 simple people, men much fitted civill
 obedience.
 
work schooles; rather nourish
 doctrine. (not knowing imagination, senses are),
 receive, teach: saying, imaginations rise of
 themselves, cause: others rise commonly from
 will; good thoughts blown (inspired) man, by
 god; evill thoughts divell: good thoughts powred
 (infused) man, god; evill ones divell. say
 senses receive species things, deliver the
 common-sense; common sense delivers fancy, and
 fancy memory, memory judgement, like
 handing things one another, many words making nothing
 understood.
 



understanding
 
imagination raysed man (or creature indued with
 faculty imagining) words, voluntary signes, that
 generally call understanding; common man beast. a
 dogge custome will understand call, rating master;
 will many beasts. understanding peculiar to
 man, understanding onely will; conceptions and
 thoughts, sequell contexture names things into
 affirmations, negations, formes speech: kinde
 understanding shall speak hereafter.
 


chapter iii. consequence trayne imaginations
 

consequence, trayne thoughts, understand succession
 one thought another, called (to distinguish from
 discourse words) mentall discourse.
 
man thinketh thing whatsoever, next thought after, is
 altogether casuall seems be. every thought every
 thought succeeds indifferently. wee imagination, whereof
 formerly sense, whole, parts; no
 transition one imagination another, whereof never the
 like senses. reason whereof this. fancies
 motions within us, reliques made sense: those
 motions immediately succeeded one another sense, continue
 also together sense: much former comming to
 take place, praedominant, later followeth, coherence of
 matter moved, manner, water upon plain table drawn
 way one part guided finger. because
 sense, one thing perceived, sometimes one thing,
 sometimes another succeedeth, comes passe time, the
 imagining thing, certainty shall imagine
 next; onely certain, shall something succeeded the
 before, one time another.
 



trayne thoughts unguided
 
trayne thoughts, mentall discourse, two sorts. the
 first unguided, without designee, inconstant; wherein no
 passionate thought, govern direct follow, self,
 end scope desire, passion: case the
 thoughts said wander, seem impertinent one another, as
 dream. commonly thoughts men, onely
 without company, also without care thing; though even then
 thoughts busie times, without harmony; as
 sound lute tune yeeld man; tune,
 one play. yet wild ranging mind,
 man may oft-times perceive way it, dependance one
 thought upon another. discourse present civill warre,
 seem impertinent, ask (as one did) the
 value roman penny? yet cohaerence manifest enough.
 thought warre, introduced thought delivering
 king enemies; thought that, brought thought
 delivering christ; thought 30
 pence, price treason: thence easily followed
 malicious question; moment time; thought
 quick.
 



trayne thoughts regulated
 
second constant; regulated desire, and
 designee. impression made things wee desire, or
 feare, strong, permanent, or, (if cease time,) quick
 return: strong sometimes, hinder break sleep.
 desire, ariseth thought means seen produce the
 like ayme at; thought that, the
 thought means mean; continually, till come some
 beginning within power. end, greatnesse
 impression, comes often mind, case thoughts begin to
 wander, quickly reduced way: observed by
 one seven wise men, made give men praecept, is
 now worne out, respice finem; say, actions,
 look often upon have, thing directs your
 thoughts way attain it.
 



remembrance
 
trayn regulated thoughts two kinds; one, effect
 imagined, wee seek causes, means produce it: this
 common man beast. is, imagining thing
 whatsoever, wee seek possible effects, can be
 produced; say, imagine can it, wee
 it. time seen signe, man
 onely; curiosity hardly incident nature any
 living creature passion sensuall, are
 hunger, thirst, lust, anger. summe, discourse mind,
 governed designee, nothing seeking, faculty
 invention, latines call sagacitas, solertia; hunting
 causes, effect, present past; effects,
 present past cause, sometimes man seeks hath lost;
 place, time, wherein hee misses it, mind runs
 back, place place, time time, find where, when
 it; say, find certain, limited time and
 place, begin method seeking. again, thence, his
 thoughts run places times, find action, or
 occasion might make lose it. call remembrance,
 calling mind: latines call reminiscentia, a
 re-conning former actions.
 
sometimes man knows place determinate, within compasse whereof
 seek; thoughts run parts thereof,
 manner, one sweep room, find jewell; as
 spaniel ranges field, till find sent; man run
 alphabet, start rime.
 



prudence
 
sometime man desires know event action; he
 thinketh like action past, events thereof one after
 another; supposing like events will follow like actions. that
 foresees wil become criminal, re-cons seen follow
 like crime before; order thoughts, crime,
 officer, prison, judge, gallowes. kind
 thoughts, called foresight, prudence, providence; and
 sometimes wisdome; though conjecture, difficulty of
 observing circumstances, fallacious. certain; by
 much one man experience things past, another; by
 much also prudent, expectations seldomer faile
 him. present onely nature; things past being
 memory onely, things come all; future
 fiction mind, applying sequels actions past,
 actions present; certainty done by
 experience; certainty enough. though
 called prudence, event answereth expectation; yet in
 nature, presumption. foresight things to
 come, providence, belongs onely whose will are
 come. onely, supernaturally, proceeds prophecy. best
 prophet naturally best guesser; best guesser, is
 versed studied matters guesses at: hath most
 signes guesse by.
 



signes
 
signe, event antecedent, consequent; contrarily,
 consequent antecedent, like consequences been
 observed, before: oftner observed, lesse
 uncertain signe. therefore experience in
 kind businesse, signes, whereby guesse future
 time, consequently prudent: much prudent
 new kind business, equalled by
 advantage naturall extemporary wit: though perhaps many young
 men think contrary.
 
neverthelesse prudence distinguisheth man beast.
 beasts, year old observe more, pursue which
 good, prudently, child can ten.
 



conjecture time past
 
prudence praesumtion future, contracted the
 experience time past; praesumtion things past taken
 things (not future but) past also. hath seen
 courses degrees, flourishing state hath first come into
 civill warre, ruine; upon sights ruines any
 state, will guesse, like warre, like courses been
 also. conjecture, incertainty almost the
 conjecture future; grounded onely upon experience.
 
act mans mind, can remember, naturally
 planted him, so, need thing, exercise it,
 born man, live use five senses. those
 faculties, shall speak by, seem proper
 man onely, acquired, encreased study industry; of
 men learned instruction, discipline; proceed from
 invention words, speech. besides sense, thoughts, and
 trayne thoughts, mind man motion; though by
 help speech, method, facultyes may improved to
 height, distinguish men living creatures.
 
whatsoever imagine, finite. therefore idea, or
 conception anything call infinite. man can mind an
 image infinite magnitude; conceive ends, bounds of
 thing named; conception thing, own
 inability. therefore name god used, make us
 conceive him; (for incomprehensible; greatnesse, power
 unconceivable;) may honour him. also whatsoever
 (as said before,) conceive, perceived first sense,
 either once, parts; man can thought, representing
 thing, subject sense. man therefore can conceive any
 thing, must conceive place; indued some
 determinate magnitude; may divided parts; any
 thing place, another place time;
 two, things can one, place once:
 none things ever have, can incident sense; are
 absurd speeches, taken upon credit (without signification all,)
 deceived philosophers, deceived, deceiving schoolemen.
 


chapter iv. speech
 



originall speech
 
invention printing, though ingenious, compared invention
 letters, great matter. first found use
 letters, known. first brought greece, men
 say cadmus, sonne agenor, king phaenicia. profitable
 invention continuing memory time past, conjunction of
 mankind, dispersed many, distant regions earth; and
 difficult, proceeding watchfull observation the
 divers motions tongue, palat, lips, organs speech;
 whereby make many differences characters, remember them.
 noble profitable invention other, of
 speech, consisting names apellations, connexion; whereby
 men register thoughts; recall past; also
 declare one another mutuall utility conversation;
 without which, amongst men, neither common-wealth, nor
 society, contract, peace, amongst lyons, bears,
 wolves. first author speech god himselfe, instructed
 adam name creatures presented sight; the
 scripture goeth matter. sufficient
 direct adde names, experience use the
 creatures give occasion; joyn manner by
 degrees, make himselfe understood; succession time,
 much language might gotten, found use for; though so
 copious, orator philosopher need of. find any
 thing scripture, which, directly consequence can
 gathered, adam taught names figures, numbers,
 measures, colours, sounds, fancies, relations; much less names
 words speech, generall, speciall, affirmative, negative,
 interrogative, optative, infinitive, usefull; least of
 all, entity, intentionality, quiddity, significant words of
 school.
 
language gotten, augmented adam posterity,
 lost tower babel, hand god, every man
 stricken rebellion, oblivion former language.
 hereby forced disperse severall parts of
 world, must needs be, diversity tongues now is,
 proceeded degrees them, manner, need (the mother of
 inventions) taught them; tract time grew every more
 copious.
 



use speech
 
generall use speech, transferre mentall discourse, into
 verbal; trayne thoughts, trayne words; that
 two commodities; whereof one is, registring consequences
 thoughts; apt slip memory, put
 us new labour, may recalled, words were
 marked by. first use names, serve markes,
 notes remembrance. another is, many use words,
 signifie (by connexion order,) one another, they
 conceive, think matter; also desire, feare,
 passion for, use called
 signes. speciall uses speech these; first, register, by
 cogitation, wee find cause thing, present past; and
 find things present past may produce, effect: in
 summe, acquiring arts. secondly, shew others knowledge
 attained; is, counsell, teach one another.
 thirdly, make known others wills, purposes, may
 mutuall help one another. fourthly, please delight
 selves, others, playing words, pleasure or
 ornament, innocently.
 



abuses speech
 
uses, also foure correspondent abuses. first,
 men register thoughts wrong, inconstancy the
 signification words; register their
 conceptions, never conceived; deceive themselves.
 secondly, use words metaphorically; is, sense
 ordained for; thereby deceive others. thirdly,
 words declare will, not.
 fourthly, use grieve one another: seeing nature
 hath armed living creatures, teeth, horns, some
 hands, grieve enemy, abuse speech, grieve
 tongue, unlesse one wee obliged govern;
 grieve, correct amend.
 
manner speech serveth remembrance consequence
 causes effects, consisteth imposing names, the
 connexion them.
 



names proper & common universall
 
names, proper, singular one onely thing; peter,
 john, man, tree: common many things; man,
 horse, tree; every though one name, nevertheless the
 name divers particular things; respect together, it
 called universall; nothing world universall
 names; things named, every one individual and
 singular.
 
one universall name imposed many things, similitude in
 quality, accident: whereas proper name bringeth to
 mind one thing onely; universals recall one many.
 
names universall, more, lesse extent; the
 larger comprehending lesse large: equall extent,
 comprehending reciprocally. example, name body is
 larger signification word man, conprehendeth it; the
 names man rationall, equall extent, comprehending mutually
 one another. wee must take notice, name not
 alwayes understood, grammar, one onely word; sometimes by
 circumlocution many words together. words, hee in
 actions observeth lawes country, make one name,
 equivalent one word, just.
 
imposition names, larger, stricter
 signification, turn reckoning consequences things
 imagined mind, reckoning consequences of
 appellations. example, man hath use speech all,
 (such, born remains perfectly deafe dumb,) set
 eyes triangle, two right angles, (such the
 corners square figure,) may meditation compare find, that
 three angles triangle, equall two right angles
 stand it. another triangle shewn different in
 shape former, know without new labour, whether the
 three angles also equall same. hath the
 use words, observes, equality consequent, not
 length sides, particular thing his
 triangle; onely this, sides straight, the
 angles three; all, named triangle;
 will boldly conclude universally, equality angles in
 triangles whatsoever; register invention generall
 termes, every triangle hath three angles equall two right angles.
 thus consequence found one particular, comes registred
 remembred, universall rule; discharges mentall
 reckoning, time place; delivers us labour the
 mind, saving first; makes found true here, and
 now, true times places.
 
use words registring thoughts, nothing so
 evident numbering. naturall foole never learn by
 heart order numerall words, one, two, three, may observe
 every stroak clock, nod it, say one, one, one; can
 never know houre strikes. seems, time when
 names number use; men fayn apply their
 fingers one hands, things desired keep
 account of; thence proceeded, now numerall words
 ten, nation, five, begin
 again. can tell ten, recite order, will
 lose himselfe, know done: much lesse will be
 able add, substract, performe operations of
 arithmetique. without words, possibility of
 reckoning numbers; much lesse magnitudes, swiftnesse, force,
 things, reckonings whereof necessary being, or
 well-being man-kind.
 
two names joyned together consequence, affirmation;
 thus, man living creature; thus, man, a
 living creature, later name living creature, signifie that
 former name man signifieth, affirmation, consequence is
 true; otherwise false. true false attributes speech, not
 things. speech not, neither truth falshood.
 errour may be, wee expect shall be; or
 suspect been: neither case can man charged with
 untruth.
 
seeing truth consisteth right ordering names our
 affirmations, man seeketh precise truth, need remember
 every name uses stands for; place accordingly; els
 will find himselfe entangled words, bird lime-twiggs; the
 struggles, belimed. therefore geometry, (which
 onely science hath pleased god hitherto bestow on
 mankind,) men begin settling significations words; which
 settling significations, call definitions; place the
 beginning reckoning.
 
appears necessary man aspires true
 knowledge, examine definitions former authors; either
 correct them, negligently set down; make them
 himselfe. errours definitions multiply themselves, according
 reckoning proceeds; lead men absurdities, last
 see, avoyd, without reckoning anew beginning;
 lyes foundation errours. whence happens,
 trust books, cast many little
 summs greater, without considering whether little summes
 rightly cast not; last finding errour visible,
 mistrusting first grounds, know way cleere
 themselves; spend time fluttering bookes; birds
 entring chimney, finding inclosed a
 chamber, flitter false light glasse window, want wit
 consider way came in. right definition
 names, lyes first use speech; acquisition of
 science: wrong, definitions’ lyes first abuse; from
 proceed false senslesse tenets; make men that
 take instruction authority books, their
 meditation, much condition ignorant men, as
 men endued true science it. true science,
 erroneous doctrines, ignorance middle. naturall sense and
 imagination, subject absurdity. nature selfe erre:
 men abound copiousnesse language; become wise,
 mad ordinary. possible without letters any
 man become either excellently wise, (unless memory hurt by
 disease, ill constitution organs) excellently foolish. words
 wise mens counters, reckon them: the
 mony fooles, value authority aristotle, a
 cicero, thomas, doctor whatsoever, man.
 



subject names
 
subject names, whatsoever can enter into, considered an
 account; added one another make summe; substracted one
 another, leave remainder. latines called accounts mony
 rationes, accounting, ratiocinatio: bills or
 books account call items, called nomina; is, names: and
 thence seems proceed, extended word ratio, the
 faculty reckoning things. greeks one word
 logos, speech reason; thought no
 speech without reason; reasoning without speech: act of
 reasoning called syllogisme; signifieth summing the
 consequences one saying another. things may
 enter account divers accidents; names (to shew that
 diversity) diversly wrested, diversified. diversity names
 may reduced foure generall heads.
 
first, thing may enter account matter, body; living,
 sensible, rationall, hot, cold, moved, quiet; names the
 word matter, body understood; such, names matter.
 
secondly, may enter account, considered, accident
 quality, conceive it; moved, being
 long, hot, &c; then, name thing selfe,
 little change wresting, wee make name accident, which
 consider; living put account life; moved, motion;
 hot, heat; long, length, like. names, are
 names accidents properties, one matter, body
 distinguished another. called names abstract; because
 severed (not matter, but) account matter.
 
thirdly, bring account, properties bodies,
 whereby make distinction: thing seen us, we
 reckon thing selfe; sight, colour, idea of
 fancy: thing heard, wee reckon not; the
 hearing, sound onely, fancy conception the
 eare: names fancies.
 
fourthly, bring account, consider, give names, names
 themselves, speeches: for, generall, universall, speciall,
 oequivocall, names names. affirmation, interrogation,
 commandement, narration, syllogisme, sermon, oration, many other
 such, names speeches.
 



use names positive
 
variety names positive; put mark
 somewhat nature, may feigned mind man, as
 bodies are, may conceived be; bodies, properties
 are, may feigned be; words speech.
 



negative names uses
 
also names, called negative; notes signifie
 word name thing question; words
 nothing, man, infinite, indocible, three want foure, the
 like; nevertheless use reckoning, correcting of
 reckoning; call mind past cogitations, though not
 names thing; make us refuse admit names not
 rightly used.
 



words insignificant
 
names, insignificant sounds; two
 sorts. one, new, yet meaning explained by
 definition; whereof aboundance coyned schoole-men,
 pusled philosophers.
 
another, men make name two names, whose significations are
 contradictory inconsistent; name, incorporeall body, or
 (which one) incorporeall substance, great number more.
 whensoever affirmation false, two names it
 composed, put together made one, signifie nothing all. for
 example false affirmation say quadrangle round,
 word round quadrangle signifies nothing; meere sound. so
 likewise false, say vertue can powred, blown up
 down; words in-powred vertue, in-blown vertue, absurd
 insignificant, round quadrangle. therefore shall hardly
 meet senselesse insignificant word, made of
 latin greek names. frenchman seldome hears saviour called
 name parole, name verbe often; yet verbe and
 parole differ more, one latin, french.
 



understanding
 
man upon hearing speech, hath thoughts the
 words speech, connexion, ordained constituted
 signifie; said understand it; understanding being
 nothing els, conception caused speech. therefore speech
 peculiar man (as know is,) understanding
 peculiar also. therefore absurd false affirmations,
 case universall, can understanding; though many
 think understand, then, repeat words softly,
 mind.
 
kinds speeches signifie appetites, aversions, passions
 mans mind; use abuse, shall speak have
 spoken passions.
 



inconstant names
 
names things affect us, is, please, and
 displease us, men alike affected thing,
 man times, common discourses men, of
 inconstant signification. seeing names imposed signifie
 conceptions; affections conceptions; we
 conceive things differently, can hardly avoyd different
 naming them. though nature conceive, the
 same; yet diversity reception it, respect different
 constitutions body, prejudices opinion, gives everything a
 tincture different passions. therefore reasoning, man
 bust take heed words; besides signification we
 imagine nature, disposition, interest speaker; such
 names vertues, vices; one man calleth wisdome,
 another calleth feare; one cruelty, another justice;
 one prodigality, another magnanimity; one gravity, another
 stupidity, &c. therefore names can never true grounds any
 ratiocination. can metaphors, tropes speech: these
 less dangerous, profess inconstancy; the
 not.
 


chapter v. reason, science.
 



reason is
 
man reasoneth, hee nothing els conceive summe totall,
 addition parcels; conceive remainder, substraction of
 one summe another: (if done words,) conceiving of
 consequence names parts, name whole;
 names whole one part, name other
 part. though things, (as numbers,) besides adding and
 substracting, men name operations, multiplying dividing;
 yet same; multiplication, addition together of
 things equall; division, substracting one thing, often as
 can. operations incident numbers onely, to
 manner things can added together, taken one of
 another. arithmeticians teach adde substract numbers;
 geometricians teach lines, figures (solid and
 superficiall,) angles, proportions, times, degrees swiftnesse, force,
 power, like; logicians teach consequences
 words; adding together two names, make affirmation; two
 affirmations, make syllogisme; many syllogismes make a
 demonstration; summe, conclusion syllogisme, they
 substract one proposition, finde other. writers politiques,
 adde together pactions, find mens duties; lawyers, lawes and
 facts, find right wrong actions private men.
 summe, matter soever place addition and
 substraction, also place reason; no
 place, reason nothing do.
 



reason defined
 
may define, (that say determine,) that
 is, meant word reason, wee reckon amongst
 faculties mind. reason, sense, nothing but
 reckoning (that is, adding substracting) consequences of
 generall names agreed upon, marking signifying our
 thoughts; say marking them, reckon selves; and
 signifying, demonstrate, approve reckonings men.
 



right reason where
 
arithmetique, unpractised men must, professors themselves
 may often erre, cast false; also subject of
 reasoning, ablest, attentive, practised men, may
 deceive themselves, inferre false conclusions; reason
 selfe always right reason, well arithmetique certain
 infallible art: one mans reason, reason any
 one number men, makes certaintie; account is
 therefore well cast up, great many men unanimously
 approved it. therfore, controversy account,
 parties must accord, set right reason, the
 reason arbitrator, judge, whose sentence will
 stand, controversie must either come blowes, be
 undecided, want right reason constituted nature; is
 also debates kind soever: men think
 wiser others, clamor demand right reason for
 judge; yet seek more, things determined, no
 mens reason own, intolerable society of
 men, play trump turned, use trump every
 occasion, suite whereof hand. do
 nothing els, will every passions, comes to
 bear sway them, taken right reason, own
 controversies: bewraying want right reason, claym they
 lay it.
 



use reason
 
use end reason, finding summe, truth
 one, consequences, remote first definitions, and
 settled significations names; begin these; proceed from
 one consequence another. can certainty last
 conclusion, without certainty affirmations negations,
 grounded, inferred. master family,
 taking account, casteth summs bills expence,
 one sum; regarding bill summed up, those
 give account; payes for; advantages
 himselfe more, allowed account grosse, trusting to
 every accountants skill honesty; also reasoning all
 things, takes conclusions trust authors, and
 doth fetch first items every reckoning, (which are
 significations names settled definitions), loses labour;
 know thing; onely beleeveth.
 



error absurdity
 
man reckons without use words, may done in
 particular things, (as upon sight one thing, wee
 conjecture likely preceded, likely follow upon
 it;) thought likely follow, followes not; that
 thought likely preceded it, hath preceded it, this
 called error; even prudent men subject. but
 reason words generall signification, fall upon a
 generall inference false; though commonly called error,
 indeed absurdity, senseless speech. error a
 deception, presuming somewhat past, come; which,
 though past, come; yet impossibility
 discoverable. make generall assertion, unlesse a
 true one, possibility unconceivable. words whereby we
 conceive nothing sound, call absurd, insignificant,
 non-sense. therefore man talk round
 quadrangle; accidents bread cheese; immaterial substances;
 free subject; free will; free, free being
 hindred opposition, say errour; that
 words without meaning; say, absurd.
 
said before, (in second chapter,) man excell
 animals faculty, conceived thing
 whatsoever, apt enquire consequences it, what
 effects it. now adde degree the
 excellence, can words reduce consequences findes
 generall rules, called theoremes, aphorismes; is, can
 reason, reckon, onely number; things, whereof
 one may added unto, substracted another.
 
priviledge, allayed another; is, the
 priviledge absurdity; living creature subject, man
 onely. men, subject it, professe
 philosophy. true cicero sayth somewhere;
 can nothing absurd, may found books of
 philosophers. reason manifest. one them
 begins ratiocination definitions, explications of
 names use; method hath used onely
 geometry; whose conclusions thereby made indisputable.
 



causes absurditie
 
first cause absurd conclusions ascribe want method;
 begin ratiocination definitions; that
 is, settled significations words: cast
 account, without knowing value numerall words, one, two, and
 three.
 
whereas bodies enter account upon divers considerations,
 (which mentioned precedent chapter;) considerations
 diversly named, divers absurdities proceed confusion, and
 unfit connexion names assertions. therefore
 
second cause absurd assertions, ascribe giving names
 bodies, accidents; accidents, bodies; do, that
 say, faith infused, inspired; nothing can powred, or
 breathed thing, body; that, extension body; that
 phantasmes spirits, &c.
 
third ascribe giving names accidents of
 bodies without us, accidents bodies; that
 say, colour body; sound ayre, &c.
 
fourth, giving names bodies, names, speeches;
 say, things universall; living
 creature genus, generall thing, &c.
 
fifth, giving names accidents, names and
 speeches; say, nature thing its
 definition; mans command will; like.
 
sixth, use metaphors, tropes, rhetoricall
 figures, stead words proper. though lawfull say, (for
 example) common speech, way goeth, leadeth hither, thither,
 proverb sayes (whereas wayes go, proverbs
 speak;) yet reckoning, seeking truth, speeches to
 admitted.
 
seventh, names signifie nothing; taken up, and
 learned rote schooles, hypostatical, transubstantiate,
 consubstantiate, eternal-now, like canting schoole-men.
 
can avoyd things, easie fall any
 absurdity, unlesse length account; wherein may
 perhaps forget went before. men nature reason alike, and
 well, good principles. stupid, to
 mistake geometry, also persist it, another detects his
 error him?
 



science
 
appears reason sense, memory, borne with
 us; gotten experience onely; prudence is; attayned by
 industry; first apt imposing names; secondly getting good
 orderly method proceeding elements, names,
 assertions made connexion one another; to
 syllogismes, connexions one assertion another, till
 come knowledge consequences names appertaining to
 subject hand; it, men call science. whereas
 sense memory knowledge fact, thing past, and
 irrevocable; science knowledge consequences, dependance
 one fact upon another: which, can presently do, we
 know something els will, like, another time;
 see thing comes about, upon causes, by
 manner; like causes come power, wee see to
 make produce like effects.
 
children therefore endued reason all, till have
 attained use speech: called reasonable creatures, the
 possibility apparent use reason time come. and
 part men, though use reasoning little
 way, numbring degree; yet serves little use in
 common life; govern themselves, better, worse,
 according differences experience, quicknesse memory, and
 inclinations severall ends; specially according good evill
 fortune, errors one another. science, certain
 rules actions, farre it, know
 is. geometry thought conjuring: other
 sciences, taught beginnings, some
 progresse them, may see acquired generated,
 point like children, thought generation,
 made believe women, brothers sisters not
 born, found garden.
 
yet science, better, nobler condition
 naturall prudence; men, mis-reasoning, by
 trusting reason wrong, fall upon false absurd generall
 rules. ignorance causes, rules, set men farre
 way, relying false rules, taking causes of
 aspire to, so, rather causes the
 contrary.
 
conclude, light humane minds perspicuous words, by
 exact definitions first snuffed, purged ambiguity; reason is
 pace; encrease science, way; benefit man-kind, the
 end. contrary, metaphors, senslesse ambiguous words,
 like ignes fatui; reasoning upon them, wandering amongst
 innumerable absurdities; end, contention, sedition, or
 contempt.
 



prudence & sapience, difference
 
as, much experience, prudence; so, much science, sapience. for
 though wee usually one name wisedome both; yet
 latines always distinguish prudentia sapientia,
 ascribing former experience, later science. make
 difference appeare cleerly, let us suppose one man endued
 excellent naturall use, dexterity handling armes; and
 another added dexterity, acquired science, where
 can offend, offended adversarie, every possible
 posture, guard: ability former, ability
 later, prudence sapience; usefull; later
 infallible. trusting onely authority books,
 follow blind blindly, like trusting false rules
 master fence, ventures praesumptuously upon adversary, that
 either kills, disgraces him.
 



signes science
 
signes science, some, certain infallible; some,
 uncertain. certain, pretendeth science thing,
 can teach same; say, demonstrate truth thereof
 perspicuously another: uncertain, onely particular events
 answer pretence, upon many occasions prove sayes
 must. signes prudence uncertain; observe by
 experience, remember circumstances may alter successe,
 impossible. businesse, whereof man infallible
 science proceed by; forsake natural judgement, be
 guided generall sentences read authors, subject many
 exceptions, signe folly, generally scorned name of
 pedantry. even men themselves, councells the
 common-wealth, love shew reading politiques history,
 domestique affaires, particular
 interest concerned; prudence enough private
 affaires: publique study reputation owne
 wit, successe anothers businesse.
 


chapter vi. interiour beginnings voluntary motions
 
commonly called passions. speeches are
 expressed.
 



motion vitall animal
 
animals, two sorts motions peculiar them: one called
 vitall; begun generation, continued without interruption through
 whole life; course bloud, pulse, the
 breathing, concoctions, nutrition, excretion, &c; motions
 needs help imagination: animal motion,
 otherwise called voluntary motion; go, speak, move of
 limbes, manner first fancied minds. sense,
 motion organs interiour parts mans body, caused by
 action things see, heare, &c.; fancy the
 reliques motion, remaining sense, already
 sayd first second chapters. going, speaking, and
 like voluntary motions, depend alwayes upon precedent thought of
 whither, way, what; evident, imagination is
 first internall beginning voluntary motion. although
 unstudied men, doe conceive motion there, where
 thing moved invisible; space moved in, (for the
 shortnesse it) insensible; yet doth hinder, such
 motions are. let space never little, moved
 greater space, whereof little one part, must first be
 moved that. small beginnings motion, within body
 man, appear walking, speaking, striking, other
 visible actions, commonly called endeavour.
 



endeavour; appetite; desire; hunger; thirst; aversion
 
endeavour, toward something causes it, called
 appetite, desire; later, generall name; other,
 oftentimes restrayned signifie desire food, namely hunger and
 thirst. endeavour fromward something, generally
 called aversion. words appetite, aversion the
 latines; signifie motions, one approaching,
 retiring. also greek words same, which
 orme aphorme. nature selfe often presse upon men
 truths, afterwards, look somewhat beyond
 nature, stumble at. schooles find meere appetite go,
 move, actuall motion all: motion must
 acknowledge, call metaphoricall motion; absurd
 speech; though words may called metaphoricall; bodies, and
 motions cannot.
 
men desire, also sayd love; hate those
 things, aversion. desire, love, the
 thing; save desire, alwayes signifie absence of
 object; love, commonly presence same. also
 aversion, signifie absence; hate, presence the
 object.
 
appetites, aversions, born men; appetite of
 food, appetite excretion, exoneration, (which may also more
 properly called aversions, somewhat feele bodies;)
 appetites, many. rest, appetites of
 particular things, proceed experience, triall effects
 upon themselves, men. things wee know all, or
 believe be, can desire, tast try.
 aversion wee things, onely know hurt us;
 also know whether will hurt us, not.
 



contempt
 
things neither desire, hate, said contemne:
 contempt nothing els immobility, contumacy heart,
 resisting action certain things; proceeding the
 heart already moved otherwise, either potent objects; from
 want experience them.
 
constitution mans body, continuall mutation;
 impossible things alwayes cause him
 appetites, aversions: much lesse can men consent, in
 desire almost one object.
 



good evill
 
whatsoever object mans appetite desire; is
 it, part calleth good: object hate,
 aversion, evill; contempt, vile, inconsiderable.
 words good, evill, contemptible, ever used with
 relation person useth them: nothing simply and
 absolutely so; common rule good evill, taken from
 nature objects themselves; person man
 (where common-wealth;) or, (in common-wealth,) the
 person representeth it; arbitrator judge, men
 disagreeing shall consent set up, make sentence rule
 thereof.
 



pulchrum turpe; delightfull profitable; unpleasant unprofitable
 
latine tongue two words, whose significations approach to
 good evill; precisely same; are
 pulchrum turpe. whereof former signifies that, some
 apparent signes promiseth good; later, that, promiseth
 evill. tongue generall names expresse them
 by. pulchrum, say things, fayre; beautifull,
 handsome, gallant, honourable, comely, amiable; and
 turpe, foule, deformed, ugly, base, nauseous, like, the
 subject shall require; words, proper places signifie
 nothing els, mine, countenance, promiseth good and
 evill. good three kinds; good promise,
 pulchrum; good effect, end desired, called
 jucundum, delightfull; good means, called utile,
 profitable; many evill: evill, promise, that
 call turpe; evill effect, end, molestum, unpleasant,
 troublesome; evill means, inutile, unprofitable, hurtfull.
 



delight displeasure
 
as, sense, really within us, (as sayd
 before) onely motion, caused action externall objects, in
 apparence; sight, light colour; eare, sound; the
 nostrill, odour, &c: so, action object continued
 eyes, eares, organs heart; real effect
 nothing motion, endeavour; consisteth appetite,
 aversion, to, object moving. apparence, sense
 motion, wee either call delight, trouble mind.
 



pleasure offence
 
motion, called appetite, apparence it
 delight, pleasure, seemeth be, corroboration vitall motion,
 help thereunto; therefore things caused delight, were
 improperly called jucunda, (a juvando,) helping fortifying;
 contrary, molesta, offensive, hindering, troubling the
 motion vitall.
 
pleasure therefore, (or delight,) apparence, sense good;
 molestation displeasure, apparence, sense evill. and
 consequently appetite, desire, love, accompanied some
 delight lesse; hatred, aversion, lesse
 displeasure offence.
 



pleasures sense; pleasures mind; joy paine griefe
 
pleasures, delights, arise sense object
 present; may called pleasures sense, (the word sensuall,
 used onely condemn them, place till
 lawes.) kind onerations exonerations the
 body; also pleasant, sight, hearing, smell,
 tast, touch; others arise expectation, proceeds from
 foresight end, consequence things; whether things in
 sense please displease: pleasures mind of
 draweth consequences; generally called joy. in
 like manner, displeasures, sense, called payne;
 others, expectation consequences, called griefe.
 
simple passions called appetite, desire, love, aversion, hate,
 joy, griefe, names divers considerations diversified.
 first, one succeed another, diversly called from
 opinion men likelihood attaining they
 desire. secondly, object loved hated. thirdly, the
 consideration many together. fourthly, alteration or
 succession selfe.
 

hope-- appetite opinion attaining, called hope.
 
despaire-- same, without opinion, despaire.
 
feare-- aversion, opinion hurt object, feare.
 
courage-- same, hope avoyding hurt resistance,
 courage.
 
anger-- sudden courage, anger.
 
confidence-- constant hope, confidence selves.
 
diffidence-- constant despayre, diffidence selves.
 
indignation-- anger great hurt done another, conceive the
 done injury, indignation.
 
benevolence-- desire good another, benevolence, good will,
 charity. man generally, good nature.
 
covetousnesse-- desire riches, covetousnesse: name used alwayes in
 signification blame; men contending them, displeased
 one anothers attaining them; though desire selfe, to
 blamed, allowed, according means riches are
 sought.
 
ambition-- desire office, precedence, ambition: name used also
 worse sense, reason mentioned.
 
pusillanimity-- desire things conduce little ends;
 fear things little hindrance, pusillanimity.
 
magnanimity-- contempt little helps, hindrances, magnanimity.
 
valour-- magnanimity, danger death, wounds, valour, fortitude.
 
liberality-- magnanimity use riches, liberality
 
miserablenesse-- pusillanimity, wretchednesse,
 miserablenesse; parsimony; liked disliked.
 
kindnesse-- love persons society, kindnesse.
 
naturall lust-- love persons pleasing sense onely, natural
 lust.
 
luxury-- love same, acquired rumination, imagination
 pleasure past, luxury.
 
passion love; jealousie-- love one singularly, desire to
 singularly beloved, passion love. same, fear the
 love mutuall, jealousie.
 
revengefulnesse-- desire, hurt another, make condemn
 fact own, revengefulnesse.
 
curiosity-- desire, know why, how, curiosity; no
 living creature man; man distinguished, onely his
 reason; also singular passion animals; whom
 appetite food, pleasures sense, praedominance,
 take away care knowing causes; lust mind,
 perseverance delight continuall indefatigable
 generation knowledge, exceedeth short vehemence carnall
 pleasure.
 
religion superstition; true religion-- feare power invisible, feigned
 mind, imagined tales publiquely allowed, religion; not
 allowed, superstition. power imagined truly we
 imagine, true religion.
 
panique terrour-- feare, without apprehension why, what,
 panique terror; called fables make pan author of
 them; whereas truth always feareth, first,
 apprehension cause, though rest run away example;
 every one supposing fellow know why. therefore passion
 happens none throng, multitude people.
 
admiration-- joy, apprehension novelty, admiration; proper to
 man, excites appetite knowing cause.
 
glory vaine-glory-- joy, arising imagination man’s power
 ability, exultation mind called glorying:
 which, grounded upon experience former actions, is
 confidence: grounded flattery others, or
 onely supposed himselfe, delight consequences it,
 called vaine-glory: name properly given; a
 well-grounded confidence begetteth attempt; whereas supposing of
 power not, therefore rightly called vaine.
 
dejection-- griefe, opinion want power, called dejection
 mind.
 
vaine-glory consisteth feigning supposing of
 abilities ourselves, know not, incident young
 men, nourished histories fictions gallant persons; and
 corrected often times age, employment.
 
sudden glory laughter-- sudden glory, passion maketh those
 grimaces called laughter; caused either sudden act of
 own, pleaseth them; apprehension some
 deformed thing another, comparison whereof suddenly applaud
 themselves. incident them, conscious the
 fewest abilities themselves; forced keep in
 favour, observing imperfections men.
 therefore much laughter defects others signe of
 pusillanimity. great minds, one proper workes is, help
 free others scorn; compare onely most
 able.
 
sudden dejection weeping-- contrary, sudden dejection the
 passion causeth weeping; caused accidents, as
 suddenly take away vehement hope, prop power: and
 subject it, rely principally helps externall,
 women, children. therefore, weep loss of
 friends; others unkindnesse; others sudden stop made
 thoughts revenge, reconciliation. cases, both
 laughter weeping, sudden motions; custome taking away.
 man laughs old jests; weeps old calamity.
 
shame blushing-- griefe, discovery defect ability
 shame, passion discovereth blushing; and
 consisteth apprehension thing dishonourable; young
 men, signe love good reputation; commendable: in
 old men signe same; comes late, not
 commendable.
 
impudence-- contempt good reputation called impudence.
 
pitty-- griefe, calamity another pitty; ariseth
 imagination like calamity may befall himselfe; and
 therefore called also compassion, phrase present
 time fellow-feeling: therefore calamity arriving from
 great wickedness, best men least pitty; same
 calamity, least pitty, think least obnoxious
 same.
 
cruelty-- contempt, little sense calamity others, that
 men call cruelty; proceeding security fortune.
 for, man take pleasure mens’ great harmes,
 without end own, conceive possible.
 
emulation envy-- griefe, success competitor wealth,
 honour, good, joyned endeavour enforce own
 abilities equal exceed him, called emulation: joyned with
 endeavour supplant hinder competitor, envie.
 
deliberation-- mind man, appetites aversions, hopes
 feares, concerning one thing, arise alternately; and
 divers good evill consequences doing, omitting thing
 propounded, come successively thoughts; sometimes we
 appetite it, sometimes aversion it; sometimes hope to
 able it; sometimes despaire, feare attempt it; whole
 sum desires, aversions, hopes feares, continued till thing be
 either done, thought impossible, call deliberation.
 
therefore things past, deliberation; manifestly
 impossible changed: things known impossible, or
 thought so; men know, think deliberation vaine. but
 things impossible, think possible, may deliberate; not
 knowing vain. called deliberation; a
 putting end liberty doing, omitting, according to
 appetite, aversion.
 
alternate succession appetites, aversions, hopes feares is
 less living creatures man; therefore beasts also
 deliberate.
 
every deliberation sayd end whereof they
 deliberate, either done, thought impossible; till wee
 retain liberty doing, omitting, according appetite, or
 aversion.
 



will
 
deliberation, last appetite, aversion, immediately adhaering
 action, omission thereof, wee call the
 will; act, (not faculty,) willing. beasts have
 deliberation must necessarily also will. definition the
 will, given commonly schooles, rationall appetite,
 good. were, voluntary act
 reason. voluntary act that, proceedeth the
 will, other. stead rationall appetite, shall
 say appetite resulting precedent deliberation, the
 definition given here. will, therefore, the
 last appetite deliberating. though say common discourse, a
 man will thing, neverthelesse forbore to
 do; yet properly inclination, makes action
 voluntary; action depends it, last
 inclination, appetite. intervenient appetites make any
 action voluntary, reason intervenient aversions
 make action involuntary; one action
 voluntary & involuntary.
 
manifest, onely actions beginning
 covetousness, ambition, lust, appetites thing
 propounded; also beginning aversion,
 feare consequences follow omission, voluntary
 actions.
 



formes speech, passion
 
formes speech passions expressed, partly the
 same, partly different those, express thoughts.
 first generally passions may expressed indicatively; as, i
 love, feare, joy, deliberate, will, command: them
 particular expressions themselves, nevertheless not
 affirmations, unless serve make inferences,
 besides passion proceed from. deliberation expressed
 subjunctively; speech proper signifie suppositions, with
 consequences; as, done, will follow; and
 differs language reasoning, save reasoning in
 generall words, deliberation part particulars.
 language desire, aversion, imperative; as, this,
 forbear that; party obliged do, forbear, is
 command; otherwise prayer; els counsell. language vaine-glory,
 indignation, pitty revengefulness, optative: desire to
 know, peculiar expression called interrogative; as, is
 it, shall it, done, so? language the
 passions find none: cursing, swearing, reviling, like, do
 signifie speech; actions tongue accustomed.
 
forms speech, say, expressions, voluntary
 significations passions: certain signes not; because
 may used arbitrarily, whether use them, such
 passions not. best signes passions present, either the
 countenance, motions body, actions, ends, aims, we
 otherwise know man have.
 



good evill apparent
 
deliberation appetites aversions raised by
 foresight good evill consequences, sequels action
 whereof deliberate; good evill effect thereof dependeth the
 foresight long chain consequences, seldome man
 able see end. far man seeth, good
 consequences greater evill, whole chain that
 writers call apparent seeming good. contrarily, the
 evill exceedeth good, whole apparent seeming evill: so
 hath experience, reason, greatest surest
 prospect consequences, deliberates best himself; able, he
 will, give best counsel unto others.
 



felicity
 
continual successe obtaining things man time to
 time desireth, say, continual prospering, men call
 felicity; mean felicity life. thing
 perpetual tranquillity mind, live here; life
 motion, can never without desire, without
 feare, without sense. kind felicity god hath
 ordained devoutly honour him, man shall sooner know,
 enjoy; joys, now incomprehensible, word of
 school-men, beatifical vision, unintelligible.
 



praise magnification
 
form speech whereby men signifie opinion goodnesse
 anything praise. whereby signifie power and
 greatness anything magnifying. whereby signifie
 opinion man’s felicity greeks called
 makarismos, name tongue. thus much is
 sufficient present purpose said passions.
 


chapter vii. ends resolutions discourse
 

discourse, governed desire knowledge, last
 end, either attaining, giving over. chain of
 discourse, wheresoever interrupted, end time.
 



judgement, sentence final; doubt
 
discourse meerly mentall, consisteth thoughts the
 thing will be, will be; been, been,
 alternately. wheresoever break chayn mans
 discourse, leave praesumption will be, or, will
 be; been, or, been. opinion. that
 alternate appetite, deliberating concerning good evil,
 alternate opinion enquiry truth past, and
 future. last appetite deliberation called will, so
 last opinion search truth past, future, called
 judgement, resolute final sentence discourseth.
 whole chain appetites alternate, question good
 bad called deliberation; whole chain opinions alternate,
 question true, false called doubt.
 
discourse whatsoever, can end absolute knowledge fact, past, or
 come. for, knowledge fact, originally, sense; and
 ever after, memory. knowledge consequence, have
 said called science, absolute, conditionall. no
 man can know discourse, this, that, is, been, will
 be; know absolutely: onely, be, is; if
 been, been; shall be, shall be: which
 know conditionally; consequence one thing to
 another; one name thing, another name thing.
 



science opinion conscience
 
therefore, discourse put speech, begins with
 definitions words, proceeds connexion into
 general affirmations, syllogismes, end or
 last sum called conclusion; thought mind it
 signified conditional knowledge, knowledge consequence
 words, commonly called science. first ground of
 discourse definitions, definitions rightly
 joyned together syllogismes, end conclusion again
 opinion, namely truth somewhat said, though sometimes in
 absurd senslesse words, without possibility understood.
 two, men, know one fact, said
 conscious one another; much know it
 together. fittest witnesses facts one
 another, third, was, ever will reputed evill
 act, man speak conscience; corrupt force
 another do: insomuch plea conscience, always
 hearkened unto diligently times. afterwards, men made use
 word metaphorically, knowledge secret
 facts, secret thoughts; therefore rhetorically said that
 conscience thousand witnesses. last all, men, vehemently
 love new opinions, (though never absurd,) and
 obstinately bent maintain them, gave opinions also that
 reverenced name conscience, seem unlawful,
 change speak them; pretend know true,
 know think so.
 



beliefe faith
 
mans discourse beginneth definitions, beginneth either
 contemplation own, still called
 opinion; beginneth saying another, whose ability to
 know truth, whose honesty deceiving, doubteth
 not; discourse much concerning thing, the
 person; resolution called beleefe, faith: faith, the
 man; beleefe, man, truth sayes. so
 beleefe two opinions; one saying man; the
 vertue. faith in, trust to, beleeve man,
 signifie thing; namely, opinion veracity man:
 beleeve said, signifieth onely opinion truth
 saying. wee observe phrase, beleeve in;
 also latine, credo in; greek, pisteno eis, never used
 writings divines. stead them, writings are
 put, beleeve him; faith him; rely him: latin,
 credo illi; fido illi: greek, pisteno anto: this
 singularity ecclesiastical use word hath raised many
 disputes right object christian faith.
 
beleeving in, creed, meant, trust the
 person; confession acknowledgement doctrine. not
 onely christians, manner men believe god, hold
 truth heare say, whether understand it, not;
 faith trust can possibly person
 whatsoever: believe doctrine creed.
 
whence may inferre, wee believe saying whatsoever
 be, true, arguments taken, thing selfe, or
 principles naturall reason, authority, and
 good opinion wee have, hath sayd it; speaker, or
 person believe in, trust in, whose word take, object of
 faith; honour done believing, done onely. and
 consequently, wee believe scriptures word god,
 immediate revelation god himselfe, beleefe, faith,
 trust church; whose word take, acquiesce therein.
 believe prophet relates unto the
 name god, take word prophet, honour him, him
 trust, believe, touching truth relateth, whether he
 true, false prophet. also history.
 believe written historians, the
 glorious acts alexander, caesar; think ghost of
 alexander, caesar, just cause offended; body
 else, historian. livy say gods made cow speak, and
 believe not; wee distrust god therein, livy. is
 evident, whatsoever believe, upon reason, is
 drawn authority men onely, writings; whether be
 sent god not, faith men onely.
 


chapter viii. vertues commonly called intellectual; their
 contrary defects
 



intellectuall vertue defined
 
vertue generally, sorts subjects, somewhat valued
 eminence; consisteth comparison. things
 equally men, nothing prized. vertues
 intellectuall, always understood abilityes mind, men
 praise, value, desire themselves; go commonly under
 name good witte; though word witte, used also, to
 distinguish one certain ability rest.
 



wit, naturall, acquired
 
vertues two sorts; naturall, acquired. naturall, i
 mean not, man hath birth: nothing else
 sense; wherein men differ little one another, brute
 beasts, reckoned amongst vertues. mean, that
 witte, gotten use onely, experience; without method,
 culture, instruction. naturall witte, consisteth principally
 two things; celerity imagining, (that is, swift succession one
 thought another;) steddy direction approved end. the
 contrary slow imagination, maketh defect, fault mind,
 commonly called dulnesse, stupidity, sometimes other
 names signifie slownesse motion, difficulty moved.
 



good wit, fancy; good judgement; discretion
 
difference quicknesse, caused difference mens
 passions; love dislike, one thing, another: and
 therefore mens thoughts run one way, another: held to,
 observe differently things passe imagination.
 whereas succession mens thoughts, nothing to
 observe things think on, either like one
 another, unlike, serve for, they
 serve purpose; observe similitudes, case
 rarely observed others, sayd a
 good wit; which, occasion, meant good fancy. they
 observe differences, dissimilitudes; called
 distinguishing, discerning, judging thing thing; in
 case, discerning easie, said good judgement:
 particularly matter conversation businesse; wherein,
 times, places, persons discerned, vertue called
 discretion. former, is, fancy, without help judgement,
 commended vertue: later judgement, and
 discretion, commended selfe, without help fancy.
 besides discretion times, places, persons, necessary a
 good fancy, required also often application thoughts
 end; say, use made them. done;
 hath vertue, will easily fitted similitudes, that
 will please, onely illustration discourse, adorning it
 new apt metaphors; also, rarity invention.
 without steddinesse, direction end, great fancy one
 kind madnesse; have, entring discourse,
 snatched purpose, every thing comes their
 thought, many, long digressions, parentheses, that
 utterly lose themselves: kind folly, know particular
 name for: cause is, sometimes want experience; whereby
 seemeth man new rare, doth others:
 sometimes pusillanimity; seems great him, other
 men think trifle: whatsoever new, great, therefore
 thought fit told, withdrawes man degrees intended
 way discourse.
 
good poem, whether epique, dramatique; also sonnets,
 epigrams, pieces, judgement fancy required:
 fancy must eminent; please the
 extravagancy; displease indiscretion.
 
good history, judgement must eminent; goodnesse
 consisteth, method, truth, choyse the
 actions profitable known. fancy place, but
 onely adorning stile.
 
orations prayse, invectives, fancy praedominant;
 designe truth, honour dishonour; is
 done noble, vile comparisons. judgement suggest
 circumstances make action laudable, culpable.
 
hortatives, pleadings, truth, disguise serveth best the
 designe hand; judgement, fancy required.
 
demonstration, councell, rigourous search truth,
 judgement all; except sometimes understanding need be
 opened apt similitude; much use fancy.
 metaphors, case utterly excluded. seeing
 openly professe deceipt; admit councell, reasoning,
 manifest folly.
 
discourse whatsoever, defect discretion be
 apparent, extravagant soever fancy be, whole discourse
 will taken signe want wit; will never the
 discretion manifest, though fancy never ordinary.
 
secret thoughts man run things, holy, prophane,
 clean, obscene, grave, light, without shame, blame; verball
 discourse do, farther judgement shall approve the
 time, place, persons. anatomist, physitian may speak, or
 write judgement unclean things; please,
 profit: another man write extravagant, pleasant
 fancies same, man, tumbled dirt,
 come present himselfe good company. ’tis want
 discretion makes difference. again, profest remissnesse
 mind, familiar company, man may play sounds, and
 aequivocal significations words; many times encounters
 extraordinary fancy: sermon, publique, before
 persons unknown, reverence, gingling of
 words will accounted folly: difference onely in
 want discretion. wit wanting, fancy
 wanting, discretion. judgement therefore without fancy is
 wit, fancy without judgement not.
 



prudence
 
thoughts man, designe hand, running a
 multitude things, observes conduce designe; what
 designe may conduce into; observations not
 easie, usuall, wit called prudence; dependeth on
 much experience, memory like things, consequences
 heretofore. much difference men, is
 fancies judgements; experience men equall
 age, much unequall, quantity; lyes different
 occasions; every one private designes. govern well a
 family, kingdome, different degrees prudence; but
 different sorts businesse; draw picture little,
 great, greater life, different degrees art. a
 plain husband-man prudent affaires house, a
 privy counseller affaires another man.
 



craft
 
prudence, adde use unjust, dishonest means, such
 usually prompted men feare, want; crooked
 wisdome, called craft; signe pusillanimity. for
 magnanimity contempt unjust, dishonest helps. which
 latines call versutia, (translated english, shifting,) is
 putting present danger incommodity, engaging into
 greater, man robbs one pay another, shorter
 sighted craft, called versutia, versura, signifies taking
 mony usurie, present payment interest.
 



acquired wit
 
acquired wit, (i mean acquired method instruction,) there
 none reason; grounded right use speech; and
 produceth sciences. reason science, already spoken
 fifth sixth chapters.
 
causes difference witts, passions: and
 difference passions, proceedeth partly different
 constitution body, partly different education. if
 difference proceeded temper brain, organs of
 sense, either exterior interior, lesse difference
 men sight, hearing, senses, fancies,
 discretions. proceeds therefore passions; are
 different, onely difference mens complexions; also
 difference customes, education.
 
passions cause differences wit, are
 principally, lesse desire power, riches, knowledge,
 honour. may reduced first, desire of
 power. riches, knowledge honour severall sorts power.
 



giddinesse madnesse
 
therefore, man great passion things;
 men terme indifferent; though may farre good
 man, free giving offence; yet possibly have
 either great fancy, much judgement. thoughts, the
 desires, scouts, spies, range abroad, find way the
 things desired: stedinesse minds motion, quicknesse
 same, proceeding thence. desire, to
 dead: weak passions, dulnesse; passions
 indifferently every thing, giddinesse, distraction; have
 stronger, vehement passions thing, ordinarily
 seen others, men call madnesse.
 
whereof almost many kinds, passions themselves.
 sometimes extraordinary extravagant passion, proceedeth the
 evill constitution organs body, harme done them; and
 sometimes hurt, indisposition organs, caused the
 vehemence, long continuance passion. cases the
 madnesse one nature.
 
passion, whose violence, continuance maketh madnesse, either
 great vaine-glory; commonly called pride, selfe-conceipt;
 great dejection mind.
 



rage
 
pride, subjecteth man anger, excesse whereof, madnesse
 called rage, fury. thus comes passe excessive desire
 revenge, becomes habituall, hurteth organs, becomes
 rage: excessive love, jealousie, becomes also rage: excessive
 opinion mans selfe, divine inspiration, wisdome,
 learning, forme, like, becomes distraction, giddinesse:
 same, joyned envy, rage: vehement opinion truth any
 thing, contradicted others, rage.
 



melancholy
 
dejection, subjects man causelesse fears; madnesse
 commonly called melancholy, apparent also divers manners; in
 haunting solitudes, graves; superstitious behaviour; in
 fearing one, another particular thing. summe, passions
 produce strange unusuall behaviour, called generall
 name madnesse. severall kinds madnesse, that
 take paines, might enrowle legion. excesses be
 madnesse, doubt passions themselves, tend
 evill, degrees same.
 
(for example,) though effect folly, possessed of
 opinion inspired, visible alwayes one man, any

 many conspire together, rage whole multitude is
 visible enough. argument madnesse can greater, than

 protected, secured injury. be
 madnesse multitude, every particular man. for
 middest sea, though man perceive sound of
 part water next him; yet well assured, part
 contributes much, roaring sea, part, of
 quantity: also, thought wee perceive great unquietnesse,
 one, two men; yet may well assured, singular
 passions, parts seditious roaring troubled nation. and

 taking leave, know were, might another time

 think need expect extravagant action argument his
 madnesse.
 
opinion inspiration, called commonly, private spirit, begins
 often, lucky finding errour generally held by
 others; knowing, remembring, conduct reason,
 came singular truth, (as think it, though many

 speciall grace god almighty, hath revealed same
 supernaturally, spirit.
 
again, madnesse nothing else, much appearing passion,
 may gathered effects wine, with
 evill disposition organs. variety of
 behaviour men drunk much, of
 mad-men: raging, others loving, others laughing, all
 extravagantly, according severall domineering passions:
 effect wine, remove dissimulation; take from

 sober men, walk alone without care employment the
 mind, unwilling vanity extravagance thoughts
 time publiquely seen: confession, that
 passions unguided, part meere madnesse.
 
opinions world, antient later ages, concerning
 cause madnesse, two. some, deriving the
 passions; some, daemons, spirits, either good, bad, which
 thought might enter man, possesse him, move organs
 strange, uncouth manner, mad-men use do. former

 sometimes daemoniacks, (that is, possessed spirits;) sometimes

great conflux people abdera, city the

insignificant speech
 
yet another fault discourses men; may also

chapter ix. severall subjects knowledge
 

knowledge two kinds; whereof one knowledge fact: the
 knowledge consequence one affirmation another. the
 former nothing else, sense memory, absolute knowledge;
 see fact doing, remember done: the
