chapter xiv. first second naturall lawes, contracts
 



right nature what
 
right nature, writers commonly call jus naturale, the
 liberty man hath, use power, will himselfe, for
 preservation nature; say, life;
 consequently, thing, judgement, and
 reason, hee shall conceive aptest means thereunto.
 



liberty what
 
liberty, understood, according proper signification the
 word, absence externall impediments: impediments, may oft
 take away part mans power hee would; hinder
 using power left him, according judgement, and
 reason shall dictate him.
 



law nature what
 
law nature, (lex naturalis,) precept, generall rule,
 found reason, man forbidden do, that, which
 destructive life, taketh away means preserving the
 same; omit, that, thinketh may best preserved.
 though speak subject, use confound jus, and
 lex, right law; yet distinguished; right,
 consisteth liberty do, forbeare; whereas law, determineth,
 bindeth one them: law, right, differ much,
 obligation, liberty; one matter are
 inconsistent.
 



naturally every man right everything
 
condition man, (as hath declared the
 precedent chapter) condition warre every one every
 one; case every one governed reason; there
 nothing can make use of, may help unto him, in
 preserving life enemyes; followeth, a
 condition, every man right every thing; even one anothers
 body. therefore, long naturall right every man to
 every thing endureth, can security man, (how strong
 wise soever be,) living time, nature ordinarily
 alloweth men live.
 



fundamental law nature
 
consequently precept, generall rule reason, "that
 every man, endeavour peace, farre hope of
 obtaining it; obtain it, may seek, use,
 helps, advantages warre." first branch, rule,
 containeth first, fundamentall law nature; is, "to seek
 peace, follow it." second, summe right nature;
 is, "by means can, defend selves."
 



second law nature
 
fundamentall law nature, men commanded to
 endeavour peace, derived second law; "that man willing,
 others too, farre-forth, peace, defence of
 himselfe shall think necessary, lay right all
 things; contented much liberty men, as
 allow men himselfe." long every man
 holdeth right, thing liketh; long men in
 condition warre. men will lay right,
 well he; reason one, devest himselfe
 his: expose himselfe prey, (which man bound
 to) rather dispose himselfe peace. law the
 gospell; "whatsoever require others you, do
 ye them." law men, "quod tibi feiri non vis, alteri
 ne feceris."
 



lay right
 
lay downe mans right thing, devest himselfe the
 liberty, hindring another benefit right the
 same. renounceth, passeth away right, giveth to
 man right before; nothing
 every man right nature: onely standeth of
 way, may enjoy originall right, without hindrance
 him; without hindrance another. effect which
 redoundeth one man, another mans defect right, much
 diminution impediments use right originall.
 



renouncing (or) transferring right what; obligation duty justice
 
right layd aside, either simply renouncing it; transferring
 another. simply renouncing; cares the
 benefit thereof redoundeth. transferring; intendeth the
 benefit thereof certain person, persons. man hath
 either manner abandoned, granted away right; said
 obliged, bound, hinder those, right is
 granted, abandoned, benefit it: ought, it
 duty, make voyd voluntary act own: such
 hindrance injustice, injury, sine jure; right being
 renounced, transferred. injury, injustice, in
 controversies world, somewhat like that, the
 disputations scholers called absurdity. called
 absurdity, contradict one maintained beginning: in
 world, called injustice, injury, voluntarily undo that,
 beginning voluntarily done. way man
 either simply renounceth, transferreth right, declaration,
 signification, voluntary sufficient signe, signes,
 doth renounce, transferre; hath renounced, or
 transferred same, accepteth it. signes are
 either words onely, actions onely; (as happeneth often)
 words actions. bonds, men are
 bound, obliged: bonds, strength, own
 nature, (for nothing easily broken mans word,) from
 feare evill consequence upon rupture.
 



rights alienable
 
whensoever man transferreth right, renounceth it; either
 consideration right reciprocally transferred himselfe; or
 good hopeth thereby. voluntary act:
 voluntary acts every man, object good to
 himselfe. therefore rights, man can be
 understood words, signes, abandoned, or
 transferred. first man lay right resisting them,
 assault force, take away life; be
 understood ayme thereby, good himselfe. may be
 sayd wounds, chayns, imprisonment; is
 benefit consequent patience; patience of
 suffering another wounded, imprisoned: also man
 tell, seeth men proceed violence, whether
 intend death not. lastly motive, end which
 renouncing, transferring right introduced, nothing
 else security mans person, life, means of
 preserving life, weary it. therefore man by
 words, signes, seem despoyle himselfe end, which
 signes intended; understood meant
 it, will; ignorant words
 actions interpreted.
 



contract what
 
mutuall transferring right, men call contract.
 
difference, transferring right thing; and
 transferring, tradition, is, delivery thing selfe. for
 thing may delivered together translation right;
 buying selling ready mony; exchange goods, or
 lands: may delivered time after.
 



covenant what
 
again, one contractors, may deliver thing contracted on
 part, leave perform part determinate
 time after, mean time trusted; contract on
 part, called pact, covenant: parts may contract now,
 performe hereafter: cases, performe time
 come, trusted, performance called keeping promise, or
 faith; fayling performance (if voluntary) violation of
 faith.
 



free-gift
 
transferring right, mutuall; one parties
 transferreth, hope gain thereby friendship, service from
 another, friends; hope gain reputation of
 charity, magnanimity; deliver mind pain of
 compassion; hope reward heaven; contract, but
 gift, freegift, grace: words signifie one thing.
 



signes contract expresse
 
signes contract, either expresse, inference. expresse, are
 words spoken understanding signifie; words
 either time present, past; as, give, grant, have
 given, granted, will yours: future;
 as, will give, will grant; words future, called
 promise.
 



signes contract inference
 
signes inference, sometimes consequence words; sometimes
 consequence silence; sometimes consequence actions;
 sometimes consequence forbearing action: generally signe
 inference, contract, whatsoever sufficiently argues the
 will contractor.
 



free gift passeth words present past
 
words alone, time come, contain bare promise,
 insufficient signe free-gift therefore obligatory.
 time come, as, morrow will give, they
 signe given yet, consequently right not
 transferred, remaineth till transferre act. but
 words time present, past, as, "i given, do
 give delivered morrow," morrows right given away
 day; vertue words, though no
 argument will. great difference the
 signification words, volos hoc tuum esse cras, cros dabo;
 "i will thine morrow," and, "i will
 give thee morrow:" word will, former manner
 speech, signifies act will present; later, it
 signifies promise act will come: therefore the
 former words, present, transferre future right; the
 later, future, transferre nothing. other
 signes will transferre right, besides words; then, though
 gift free, yet may right understood passe words of
 future: man propound prize comes first the
 end race, gift free; though words the
 future, yet right passeth: words be
 understood, let runne.
 
signes contract words past, present, future in
 contracts, right passeth, onely words time
 present, past; also future; all
 contract mutuall translation, change right; therefore he
 promiseth onely, hath already received benefit for
 promiseth, understood intended right
 passe: unlesse content words so
 understood, performed part first. and
 cause, buying, selling, acts contract, a
 promise equivalent covenant; therefore obligatory.
 



merit what
 
performeth first case contract, said merit
 receive performance other; hath
 due. also prize propounded many, given
 onely winneth; mony thrown amongst many, enjoyed
 catch it; though free gift; yet win, or
 catch, merit, due. right is
 transferred propounding prize, throwing the
 mony; though determined whom, event the
 contention. two sorts merit, this
 difference, contract, merit vertue power, the
 contractors need; case free gift, enabled to
 merit onely benignity giver; contract, merit the
 contractors hand hee depart right; case of
 gift, merit giver part right; that
 parted it, mine, rather anothers.
 think meaning distinction schooles,
 meritum congrui, meritum condigni. god almighty, having
 promised paradise men (hoodwinkt carnall desires,) that
 can walk world according precepts, limits
 prescribed him; say, shall walk, shall merit paradise
 ex congruo. man can demand right it, own
 righteousnesse, power himselfe, free grace of
 god onely; say, man can merit paradise ex condigno. say,
 think meaning distinction; disputers not
 agree upon signification termes art, longer it
 serves turn; will affirme thing meaning:
 onely say; gift given indefinitely, prize be
 contended for, winneth meriteth, may claime prize as
 due.
 



covenants mutuall trust, invalid
 
covenant made, wherein neither parties performe
 presently, trust one another; condition meer nature,
 (which condition warre every man every man,) upon
 reasonable suspition, voyd; common power set
 bothe, right force sufficient compell performance;
 voyd. performeth first, assurance other
 will performe after; bonds words weak bridle
 mens ambition, avarice, anger, passions, without feare of
 coerceive power; condition meer nature, all
 men equall, judges justnesse fears cannot
 possibly supposed. therefore performeth first, does
 betray himselfe enemy; contrary right (he can never
 abandon) defending life, means living.
 
civill estate, power set constrain
 otherwise violate faith, feare more
 reasonable; cause, covenant perform
 first, obliged do.
 
cause feare, maketh covenant invalid, must be
 alwayes something arising covenant made; new fact,
 signe will performe; else make the
 covenant voyd. hinder man promising,
 admitted hindrance performing.
 



right end, containeth right means
 
transferreth right, transferreth means enjoying it,
 farre lyeth power. selleth land, understood
 transferre herbage, whatsoever growes upon it; can he
 sells mill turn away stream drives it. that
 give man right government soveraignty, understood
 give right levying mony maintain souldiers; of
 appointing magistrates administration justice.
 



covenant beasts
 
make covenant bruit beasts, impossible; not
 understanding speech, understand not, accept any
 translation right; can translate right another; and
 without mutuall acceptation, covenant.
 



god without speciall revelation
 
make covenant god, impossible, mediation such
 god speaketh to, either revelation supernaturall, his
 lieutenants govern him, name; otherwise we
 know whether covenants accepted, not. therefore they
 vow thing contrary law nature, vow vain; being
 thing unjust pay vow. thing commanded the
 law nature, vow, law binds them.
 



covenant, possible future
 
matter, subject covenant, alwayes something falleth
 deliberation; (for covenant, act will; to
 say act, last act, deliberation;) therefore alwayes
 understood something come; judged possible him
 covenanteth, performe.
 
therefore, promise known impossible, no
 covenant. prove impossible afterwards, was
 thought possible, covenant valid, bindeth, (though the
 thing selfe,) yet value; or, also impossible, to
 unfeigned endeavour performing much possible; to
 man can obliged.
 



covenants made voyd
 
men freed covenants two wayes; performing; being
 forgiven. performance, naturall end obligation; and
 forgivenesse, restitution liberty; retransferring of
 right, obligation consisted.
 



covenants extorted feare valide
 
covenants entred fear, condition meer nature, are
 obligatory. example, covenant pay ransome, service for
 life, enemy; bound it. contract, wherein
 one receiveth benefit life; receive mony,
 service it; consequently, law (as the
 condition, meer nature) forbiddeth performance, covenant
 valid. therefore prisoners warre, trusted payment of
 ransome, obliged pay it; weaker prince, make a
 disadvantageous peace stronger, feare; bound keep
 it; unlesse (as hath sayd before) ariseth new, just
 cause feare, renew war. even common-wealths, be
 forced redeem selfe theefe promising mony, am
 bound pay it, till civill law discharge me. whatsoever may
 lawfully without obligation, may lawfully covenant do
 feare: lawfully covenant, lawfully break.
 



former covenant one, makes voyd later another
 
former covenant, makes voyd later. man hath passed away
 right one man day, hath passe morrow another:
 therefore later promise passeth right, null.
 



mans covenant defend himselfe, voyd
 
covenant defend selfe force, force, alwayes voyd.
 (as shewed before) man can transferre, lay his
 right save himselfe death, wounds, imprisonment, (the
 avoyding whereof onely end laying right,)
 therefore promise resisting force, covenant
 transferreth right; obliging. though man may covenant
 thus, "unlesse so, so, kill me;" covenant thus "unless
 so, so, will resist you, come kill me." for
 man nature chooseth lesser evill, danger death in
 resisting; rather greater, certain present death
 resisting. granted true men, in
 lead criminals execution, prison, armed men,
 notwithstanding criminals consented law, which
 condemned.
 



man obliged accuse himselfe
 
covenant accuse ones selfe, without assurance pardon, is
 likewise invalide. condition nature, every man is
 judge, place accusation: civill state, the
 accusation followed punishment; force, man is
 obliged resist. also true, accusation of
 those, whose condemnation man falls misery; father,
 wife, benefactor. testimony accuser, not
 willingly given, praesumed corrupted nature; therefore
 received: mans testimony credited,
 bound give it. also accusations upon torture, to
 reputed testimonies. torture used means of
 conjecture, light, examination, search truth;
 case confessed, tendeth ease is
 tortured; informing torturers: therefore ought
 credit sufficient testimony: whether deliver
 himselfe true, false accusation, right of
 preserving life.
 



end oath; forme oath
 
force words, (as formerly noted) weak hold
 men performance covenants; mans nature, but
 two imaginable helps strengthen it. either feare
 consequence breaking word; glory, pride in
 appearing need breake it. later generosity too
 rarely found presumed on, especially pursuers wealth,
 command, sensuall pleasure; greatest part mankind.
 passion reckoned upon, fear; whereof two very
 generall objects: one, power spirits invisible; other, the
 power men shall therein offend. two, though the
 former greater power, yet feare later commonly
 greater feare. feare former every man, own
 religion: hath place nature man civill society.
 later hath so; least place enough, keep men their
 promises; condition meer nature, inequality of
 power discerned, event battell. the
 time civill society, interruption thereof warre, there
 nothing can strengthen covenant peace agreed on, the
 temptations avarice, ambition, lust, strong desire, the
 feare invisible power, every one worship god; and
 feare revenger perfidy. therefore can done
 two men subject civill power, put one another
 swear god feareth: swearing oath, forme of
 speech, added promise; promiseth, signifieth, that
 unlesse performe, renounceth mercy god, calleth to
 vengeance himselfe. heathen forme, "let jupiter
 kill else, kill beast." forme, "i shall thus,
 thus, help god." this, rites ceremonies,
 every one useth religion, feare breaking
 faith might greater.
 



oath, god
 
appears, oath taken according forme, or
 rite, his, sweareth, vain; oath: no
 swearing thing swearer thinks god. though men
 sometimes used swear kings, feare, flattery; yet
 thereby understood, attributed divine
 honour. swearing unnecessarily god, prophaning his
 name: swearing things, men common discourse, is
 swearing, impious custome, gotten much vehemence of
 talking.
 



oath addes nothing obligation
 
appears also, oath addes nothing obligation. a
 covenant, lawfull, binds sight god, without oath,
 much it; unlawfull, bindeth all; though be
 confirmed oath.
 


chapter xv. lawes nature
 



third law nature, justice
 
law nature, obliged transferre to
 another, rights, retained, hinder peace mankind,
 followeth third; this, men performe their
 covenants made: without which, covenants vain, empty
 words; right men things remaining, wee still
 condition warre.
 



justice injustice what
 
law nature, consisteth fountain originall of
 justice. covenant hath preceded, hath right been
 transferred, every man right every thing; consequently,
 action can unjust. covenant made, break it
 unjust: definition injustice, not
 performance covenant. whatsoever unjust, just.
 
justice propriety begin constitution common-wealth
 covenants mutuall trust, feare not
 performance either part, (as hath said former chapter,)
 invalid; though originall justice making covenants;
 yet injustice actually can none, till cause feare
 taken away; men naturall condition warre,
 done. therefore names just, unjust can have
 place, must coercive power, compell men equally to
 performance covenants, terrour punishment,
 greater benefit expect breach covenant;
 make good propriety, mutuall contract men acquire,
 recompence universall right abandon: power there
 none erection common-wealth. also be
 gathered ordinary definition justice schooles: for
 say, "justice constant will giving every man his
 own." therefore own, is, propriety, there
 injustice; coerceive power erected, is,
 common-wealth, propriety; men having
 right things: therefore common-wealth, there
 nothing unjust. nature justice, consisteth keeping
 valid covenants: validity covenants begins with
 constitution civill power, sufficient compell men keep
 them: also propriety begins.
 



justice contrary reason
 
foole hath sayd heart, thing justice;
 sometimes also tongue; seriously alleaging, every mans
 conservation, contentment, committed care, there
 reason, every man might thought conduced
 thereunto; therefore also make, make; keep, keep
 covenants, reason, conduced ones benefit.
 therein deny, covenants; are
 sometimes broken, sometimes kept; breach may
 called injustice, observance justice: he
 questioneth, whether injustice, taking away feare god, (for the
 foole hath said heart god,) may sometimes
 stand reason, dictateth every man good; and
 particularly then, conduceth benefit, shall put a
 man condition, neglect onely dispraise, revilings,
 also power men. kingdome god gotten by
 violence; gotten unjust violence? it
 reason get it, impossible receive hurt by
 it? reason, justice; else
 justice approved good. reasoning this,
 succesfull wickednesse hath obtained name vertue; that
 things disallowed violation faith; yet have
 allowed it, getting kingdome. heathen
 believed, saturn deposed jupiter, believed
 neverthelesse jupiter avenger injustice: somewhat
 like piece law cokes commentaries litleton; he
 sayes, right heire crown attainted treason; yet the
 crown shall descend him, eo instante atteynder voyd; from
 instances man will prone inferre; heire
 apparent kingdome, shall kill possession, though his
 father; may call injustice, name will; yet
 can never reason, seeing voluntary actions of
 men tend benefit themselves; actions most
 reasonable, conduce ends. specious reasoning is
 nevertheless false.
 
question promises mutuall, security
 performance either side; civill power erected
 parties promising; promises covenants: but
 either one parties performed already; there
 power make performe; question whether be
 reason, is, benefit performe,
 not. say reason. manifestation
 whereof, consider; first, man doth thing, which
 notwithstanding thing can foreseen, reckoned on, tendeth to
 destruction, howsoever accident expect,
 arriving may turne benefit; yet events make it
 reasonably wisely done. secondly, condition warre,
 wherein every man every man, want common power keep them
 awe, enemy, man can hope strength,
 wit, defend himselfe destruction, without help
 confederates; every one expects defence the
 confederation, one else does: therefore declares
 thinks reason deceive help him, can reason expect
 means safety, can single
 power. therefore breaketh covenant, consequently
 declareth thinks may reason so, received
 society, unite peace defence, but
 errour receive him; received, be
 retayned it, without seeing danger errour; errours
 man reasonably reckon upon means security; and
 therefore left, cast society, perisheth; he
 live society, errours men, not
 foresee, reckon upon; consequently reason his
 preservation; so, men contribute destruction,
 forbear onely ignorance good themselves.
 
instance gaining secure perpetuall felicity of
 heaven, way; frivolous: one way imaginable;
 breaking, keeping covenant.
 
instance attaining soveraignty rebellion; is
 manifest, though event follow, yet reasonably
 expected, rather contrary; gaining so,
 others taught gain like manner, attempt thereof
 reason. justice therefore, say, keeping of
 covenant, rule reason, forbidden thing
 destructive life; consequently law nature.
 
proceed further; will law nature,
 rules conduce preservation mans life on
 earth; attaining eternall felicity death; to
 think breach covenant may conduce; consequently
 just reasonable; (such think work merit
 kill, depose, rebell against, soveraigne power constituted
 consent.) naturall
 knowledge mans estate death; much lesse reward is
 given breach faith; onely beliefe grounded upon
 mens saying, know supernaturally, know
 those, knew them, knew others, knew supernaturally;
 breach faith called precept reason, nature.
 



covenants discharged vice person made
 
others, allow law nature, keeping faith, do
 neverthelesse make exception certain persons; heretiques, and
 use performe covenant others: also is
 reason. fault man, sufficient discharge
 covenant made; reason sufficient to
 hindred making it.
 



justice men, justice actions what
 
names just, unjust, attributed men, signifie
 one thing; attributed actions, another. they
 attributed men, signifie conformity, inconformity of
 manners, reason. attributed actions, they
 signifie conformity, inconformity reason, manners, or
 manner life, particular actions. just man therefore, he
 taketh care can, actions may just: and
 unjust man, neglecteth it. men often
 language stiled names righteous, unrighteous; then
 just, unjust; though meaning same. therefore righteous
 man, lose title, one, unjust actions, that
 proceed sudden passion, mistake things, persons: does
 unrighteous man, lose character, actions, does,
 forbeares do, feare: will framed the
 justice, apparant benefit do. which
 gives humane actions relish justice, certain noblenesse
 gallantnesse courage, (rarely found,) man scorns to
 beholding contentment life, fraud, breach of
 promise. justice manners, meant, where
 justice called vertue; injustice vice.
 
justice actions denominates men, just, guiltlesse;
 injustice same, (which also called injury,) gives them
 name guilty.
 



justice manners, justice actions
 
again, injustice manners, disposition, aptitude to
 injurie; injustice proceed act; without
 supposing individuall person injured. injustice an
 action, (that say injury,) supposeth individuall person
 injured; namely him, covenant made: therefore many
 times injury received one man, dammage redoundeth
 another. master commandeth servant give mony a
 stranger; done, injury done master, whom
 covenanted obey; dammage redoundeth the
 stranger, obligation; therefore injure
 him. also common-wealths, private men may remit one another
 debts; robberies violences, whereby are
 endammaged; detaining debt, injury themselves;
 robbery violence, injuries person the
 common-wealth.
 



nothing done man, consent can injury
 
whatsoever done man, conformable will signified to
 doer, injury him. doeth it, hath passed
 away originall right please, antecedent
 covenant, breach covenant; therefore injury done
 him. have; will done signified, a
 release covenant; injury done him.
 



justice commutative, distributive
 
justice actions, writers divided commutative, and
 distributive; former say consisteth proportion
 arithmeticall; later proportion geometricall. commutative
 therefore, place equality value things contracted
 for; distributive, distribution equall benefit, men of
 equall merit. injustice sell dearer buy; to
 give man merits. value things contracted
 for, measured appetite contractors: therefore the
 just value, contented give. merit (besides
 covenant, performance one part, meriteth
 performance part, falls justice commutative,
 distributive,) due justice; rewarded grace
 onely. therefore distinction, sense wherein useth to
 expounded, right. speak properly, commutative justice,
 justice contractor; is, performance covenant,
 buying, selling; hiring, letting hire; lending, and
 borrowing; exchanging, bartering, acts contract.
 
distributive justice, justice arbitrator; say,
 act defining just. wherein, (being trusted that
 make arbitrator,) performe trust, said distribute
 every man own: indeed just distribution, may
 called (though improperly) distributive justice; properly
 equity; also law nature, shall shewn due place.
 



fourth law nature, gratitude
 
justice dependeth antecedent covenant; gratitude depend
 antecedent grace; say, antecedent free-gift: the
 fourth law nature; may conceived forme, "that man
 receiveth benefit another meer grace, endeavour he
 giveth it, reasonable cause repent good
 will." man giveth, intention good himselfe;
 gift voluntary; voluntary acts, object to
 every man good; men see shall frustrated,
 will beginning benevolence, trust; consequently of
 mutuall help; reconciliation one man another; therefore
 remain still condition war; contrary to
 first fundamentall law nature, commandeth men seek
 peace. breach law, called ingratitude; hath same
 relation grace, injustice hath obligation covenant.
 



fifth, mutuall accommodation, compleasance
 
fifth law nature, compleasance; say, "that every
 man strive accommodate himselfe rest." understanding
 whereof, may consider, mens aptnesse society;
 diversity nature, rising diversity affections; not
 unlike see stones brought together building an
 aedifice. stone asperity, irregularity of
 figure, takes room others, selfe fills; for
 hardnesse, easily made plain, thereby hindereth the
 building, builders cast away unprofitable, troublesome:
 also, man asperity nature, will strive retain those
 things himselfe superfluous, others necessary; and
 stubbornness passions, corrected, be
 left, cast society, combersome thereunto. seeing every
 man, onely right, also necessity nature, supposed
 endeavour can, obtain necessary his
 conservation; shall oppose himselfe it, things
 superfluous, guilty warre thereupon follow; and
 therefore doth that, contrary fundamentall law of
 nature, commandeth seek peace. observers law,
 may called sociable, (the latines call commodi;) contrary,
 stubborn, insociable, froward, intractable.
 



sixth, facility pardon
 
sixth law nature this, "that upon caution future time,
 man pardon offences past repenting, desire
 it." pardon, nothing granting peace; though granted
 persevere hostility, peace, feare; yet
 granted give caution future time, signe an
 aversion peace; therefore contrary law nature.
 



seventh, revenges, men respect onely future good
 
seventh is, " revenges, (that is, retribution evil for
 evil,) men look greatnesse evill past, the
 greatnesse good follow." whereby forbidden inflict
 punishment designe, correction offender,
 direction others. law consequent next before
 it, commandeth pardon, upon security future time. besides,
 revenge without respect example, profit come, a
 triumph, glorying hurt another, tending end; (for the
 end alwayes somewhat come;) glorying end, vain-glory,
 contrary reason; hurt without reason, tendeth the
 introduction warre; law nature; is
 commonly stiled name cruelty.
 



eighth, contumely
 
signes hatred, contempt, provoke fight;
 insomuch men choose rather hazard life, be
 revenged; may eighth place, law nature set this
 precept, "that man deed, word, countenance, gesture, declare
 hatred, contempt another." breach law, commonly
 called contumely.
 



ninth, pride
 
question better man, place condition of
 meer nature; where, (as shewn before,) men equall. the
 inequallity now is, introduced lawes civill. know
 aristotle first booke politiques, foundation of
 doctrine, maketh men nature, worthy command, meaning
 wiser sort (such thought himselfe philosophy;)
 others serve, (meaning strong bodies, not
 philosophers he;) master servant introduced by
 consent men, difference wit; against
 reason; also experience. foolish,
 rather governe themselves, governed others:
 wise conceit, contend force, who
 distrust owne wisdome, alwaies, often, almost any
 time, get victory. nature therefore made men equall, that
 equalitie acknowledged; nature made men unequall;
 yet men think equall, will enter into
 conditions peace, upon equall termes, equalitie must be
 admitted. therefore ninth law nature, put this, "that
 every man acknowledge equall nature." breach of
 precept pride.
 



tenth arrogance
 
law, dependeth another, "that entrance conditions of
 peace, man require reserve himselfe right, not
 content reserved every one rest." necessary
 men seek peace, lay certaine rights nature; that
 say, libertie list: necessarie
 mans life, retaine some; right governe owne bodies;
 enjoy aire, water, motion, waies go place place; all
 things else without man live, live well. in
 case, making peace, men require themselves, that
 granted others, contrary
 precedent law, commandeth acknowledgement naturall
 equalitie, therefore also law nature. observers
 law, call modest, breakers arrogant men.
 greeks call violation law pleonexia; is, desire
 share.
 



eleventh equity
 
also "if man trusted judge man man," precept
 law nature, "that deale equally them." without
 that, controversies men determined warre.
 therefore partiall judgment, doth lies, to
 deterre men use judges, arbitrators; consequently,
 (against fundamentall lawe nature) cause warre.
 
observance law, equall distribution man, of
 reason belongeth him, called equity, (as have
 sayd before) distributive justice: violation, acception persons,
 prosopolepsia.
 



twelfth, equall use things common
 
followeth another law, "that things be
 divided, enjoyed common, can be; quantity the
 thing permit, without stint; otherwise proportionably number of
 right." otherwise distribution unequall, and
 contrary equitie.
 



thirteenth, lot
 
things be, can neither divided, enjoyed in
 common. then, law nature, prescribeth equity, requireth,
 "that entire right; else, (making use alternate,) first
 possession, determined lot." equall distribution, of
 law nature; means equall distribution be
 imagined.
 



fourteenth, primogeniture, first seising
 
lots two sorts, arbitrary, naturall. arbitrary, is
 agreed competitors; naturall, either
 primogeniture, (which greek calls kleronomia, signifies, given
 lot;) first seisure.
 
therefore things enjoyed common, nor
 divided, adjudged first possessor; cases
 first-borne, acquired lot.
 



fifteenth, mediators
 
also law nature, "that men mediate peace, allowed
 safe conduct." law commandeth peace, end, commandeth
 intercession, means; intercession means safe
 conduct.
 



sixteenth, submission arbitrement
 
because, though men never willing observe lawes,
 may neverthelesse arise questions concerning mans action; first,
 whether done, done; secondly (if done) whether against
 law, law; former whereof, called a
 question fact; later question right; therefore unlesse the
 parties question, covenant mutually stand sentence
 another, farre peace ever. other, whose
 sentence submit, called arbitrator. therefore of
 law nature, "that controversie, submit their
 right judgement arbitrator."
 



seventeenth, man judge
 
seeing every man presumed things order own
 benefit, man fit arbitrator cause: were
 never fit; yet equity allowing party equall benefit, one
 admitted judge, admitted also; & the
 controversie, is, cause war, remains, law of
 nature.
 



eighteenth, man judge, cause partiality
 
reason man cause received for
 arbitrator, greater profit, honour, pleasure apparently
 ariseth victory one party, other: hath
 taken (though unavoydable bribe, yet) bribe; man can be
 obliged trust him. thus also controversie, condition
 war remaineth, contrary law nature.
 



nineteenth, witnesse
 
controversie fact, judge give credit
 one, other, (if arguments) must give
 credit third; third fourth; more: else the
 question undecided, left force, contrary law nature.
 
lawes nature, dictating peace, means the
 conservation men multitudes; onely concern doctrine
 civill society. things tending destruction of
 particular men; drunkenness, parts intemperance;
 may therefore also reckoned amongst things law
 nature hath forbidden; necessary mentioned, are
 pertinent enough place.
 



rule, laws nature may easily examined
 
though may seem subtile deduction lawes nature,
 taken notice men; whereof part busie in
 getting food, rest negligent understand; yet leave
 men unexcusable, contracted one easie sum,
 intelligible even meanest capacity; is, "do to
 another, thou wouldest done thy selfe;" sheweth
 him, learning lawes nature, but,
 weighing actions men own, seem too
 heavy, put part ballance, into
 place, passions, selfe-love, may adde nothing to
 weight; none lawes nature will
 appear unto reasonable.
 



lawes nature oblige conscience alwayes,
 
effect onely security lawes nature
 oblige foro interno; say, bind desire they
 take place: foro externo; is, putting them
 act, alwayes. modest, tractable, and
 performe promises, time, place, man els
 so, make himselfe prey others, procure his
 certain ruine, contrary ground lawes nature, which
 tend natures preservation. again, shall observe same
 lawes towards him, observes himselfe, seeketh peace, but
 war; & consequently destruction nature violence.
 
whatsoever lawes bind foro interno, may broken, onely by
 fact contrary law also fact according it, case a
 man think contrary. though action case, according
 law; obligation foro interno, breach.
 



laws nature eternal;
 
lawes nature immutable eternall, injustice,
 ingratitude, arrogance, pride, iniquity, acception persons, the
 rest, can never made lawfull. can never warre shall
 preserve life, peace destroy it.
 



yet easie
 
lawes, oblige onely desire, endeavour, i
 mean unfeigned constant endeavour, easie observed. for
 require nothing endeavour; endeavoureth their
 performance, fulfilleth them; fulfilleth law, just.
 



science lawes, true morall philosophy
 
science them, true onely moral philosophy. for
 morall philosophy nothing else science good, and
 evill, conversation, society mankind. good, evill,
 names signifie appetites, aversions; different
 tempers, customes, doctrines men, different: divers men,
 differ onely judgement, senses pleasant,
 unpleasant tast, smell, hearing, touch, sight; also
 conformable, disagreeable reason, actions of
 common life. nay, man, divers times, differs himselfe;
 one time praiseth, is, calleth good, another time
 dispraiseth, calleth evil: whence arise disputes,
 controversies, last war. therefore long man the
 condition meer nature, (which condition war,) private
 appetite measure good, evill: consequently men
 agree this, peace good, therefore also way, or
 means peace, (as shewed before) justice, gratitude,
 modesty, equity, mercy, & rest laws nature, good; that
 say, morall vertues; contrarie vices, evill. now the
 science vertue vice, morall philosophie; therfore true
 doctrine lawes nature, true morall philosophie. the
 writers morall philosophie, though acknowledge vertues
 vices; yet seeing wherein consisted goodnesse; that
 come praised, meanes peaceable, sociable, and
 comfortable living; place mediocrity passions: not
 cause, degree daring, made fortitude; cause,
 quantity gift, made liberality.
 
dictates reason, men use call name lawes; but
 improperly: conclusions, theoremes concerning what
 conduceth conservation defence themselves; whereas law,
 properly word him, right hath command others. but
 yet consider theoremes, delivered word of
 god, right commandeth things; properly called
 lawes.
 


chapter xvi. persons, authors, things personated
 


person what
 
person, "whose words actions considered, either his
 own, representing words actions man, any
 thing attributed, whether truly fiction."
 



person naturall, artificiall
 
considered owne, called naturall
 person: considered representing words and
 actions other, feigned artificiall person.
 



word person, whence
 
word person latine: instead whereof greeks prosopon,
 signifies face, persona latine signifies disguise,
 outward appearance man, counterfeited stage; somtimes
 particularly part it, disguiseth face, mask
 visard: stage, hath translated representer
 speech action, well tribunalls, theaters. a
 person, actor is, stage common
 conversation; personate, act, represent himselfe, an
 other; acteth another, said beare person, or
 act name; (in sence cicero useth saies, "unus
 sustineo tres personas; mei, adversarii, & judicis, beare three
 persons; own, adversaries, judges;") called in
 diverse occasions, diversly; representer, representative, a
 lieutenant, vicar, attorney, deputy, procurator, actor, and
 like.
 



actor, author; authority
 
persons artificiall, words actions owned by
 represent. person actor; that
 owneth words actions, author: case the
 actor acteth authority. speaking goods and
 possessions, called owner, latine dominus, greeke
 kurios; speaking actions, called author. right of
 possession, called dominion; right action, is
 called authority. authority, alwayes understood right
 act: done authority, done commission, licence
 whose right is.
 



covenants authority, bind author
 
hence followeth, actor maketh covenant by
 authority, bindeth thereby author, lesse made
 himselfe; lesse subjecteth consequences the
 same. therfore hath said formerly, (chap. 14) the
 nature covenants man man naturall capacity,
 true also made actors, representers, or
 procurators, authority them, far-forth their
 commission, farther.
 
therefore maketh covenant actor, representer,
 knowing authority hath, doth perill. man
 obliged covenant, whereof author; consequently by
 covenant made against, beside authority gave.
 



actor
 
actor doth thing law nature command of
 author, obliged former covenant obey him, he, but
 author breaketh law nature: though action against
 law nature; yet his: contrarily; refuse do
 it, law nature, forbiddeth breach covenant.
 



authority shewne
 
maketh covenant author, mediation the
 actor, knowing authority hath, onely takes word;
 case authority made manifest unto upon demand, is
 longer obliged: covenant made author, valid,
 without counter-assurance. covenanteth, knew
 hand expect assurance, actors word;
 covenant valid; actor case maketh
 himselfe author. therefore, authority evident,
 covenant obligeth author, actor; authority
 feigned, obligeth actor onely; author but
 himselfe.
 



things personated, inanimate
 
things, uncapable represented by
 fiction. inanimate things, church, hospital, bridge, may
 personated rector, master, overseer. things inanimate,
 authors, therefore give authority actors: yet the
 actors may authority procure maintenance, given by
 owners, governours things. therefore,
 things personated, state civill
 government.
 



irrational
 
likewise children, fooles, mad-men use reason, may
 personated guardians, curators; can authors (during
 time) action done them, longer (when shall
 recover use reason) shall judge reasonable.
 yet folly, hath right governing them, may give
 authority guardian. place state
 civill, estate, dominion persons.
 



false gods
 
idol, meer figment brain, may personated; the
 gods heathen; officers state appointed, were
 personated, held possessions, goods, rights, men
 time time dedicated, consecrated unto them. idols cannot
 authors: idol nothing. authority proceeded the
 state: therefore introduction civill government, gods
 heathen personated.
 



true god
 
true god may personated. was; first, moses; governed
 israelites, (that his, gods people,) own
 name, hoc dicit moses; gods name, hoc dicit dominus.
 secondly, man, blessed saviour jesus
 christ, came reduce jewes, induce nations the
 kingdome father; himselfe, sent father.
 thirdly, holy ghost, comforter, speaking, working
 apostles: holy ghost, comforter came of
 himselfe; sent, proceeded both.
 



multitude men, one person
 
multitude men, made one person, one man, or
 one person, represented; done consent of
 every one multitude particular. unity the
 representer, unity represented, maketh person
 one. representer beareth person, one
 person: unity, otherwise understood multitude.
 



every one author
 
multitude naturally one, many; cannot
 understood one; many authors, every thing their
 representative faith, doth name; every man giving their
 common representer, authority himselfe particular; owning
 actions representer doth, case give authority
 without stint: otherwise, limit what, farre
 shall represent them, none owneth more, gave him
 commission act.
 



actor may many men made one plurality voyces
 
representative consist many men, voyce greater
 number, must considered voyce all. lesser
 number pronounce (for example) affirmative, greater in
 negative, will negatives enough destroy
 affirmatives; thereby excesse negatives, standing
 uncontradicted, onely voyce representative hath.
 



representatives, number even, unprofitable
 
representative even number, especially number is
 great, whereby contradictory voyces oftentimes equall, is
 therefore oftentimes mute, uncapable action. yet cases
 contradictory voyces equall number, may determine question; in
 condemning, absolving, equality votes, even condemne
 not, absolve; contrary condemne, absolve
 not. cause heard; condemne, absolve; on
 contrary, say absolving, condemning, true. the
 like deliberation executing presently, deferring
 till another time; voyces equall, decreeing
 execution, decree dilation.
 



negative voyce
 
number odde, three, more, (men, assemblies;)
 whereof every one negative voice, authority take away the
 effect affirmative voices rest, number no
 representative; diversity opinions, interests of
 men, becomes oftentimes, cases greatest consequence, a
 mute person, unapt, may things else, government of
 multitude, especially time warre.
 
authors two sorts. first simply called; have
 defined him, owneth action another simply.
 second he, owneth action, covenant another
 conditionally; say, undertaketh it, the
 doth not, at, certain time. authors
 conditionall, generally called suretyes, latine fidejussores, and
 sponsores; particularly debt, praedes; appearance before
 judge, magistrate, vades.
 




part ii.
 common-wealth
 



chapter xvii. causes, generation, definition a
 common-wealth
 



end common-wealth, particular security
 
finall cause, end, designe men, (who naturally love liberty,
 dominion others,) introduction restraint upon
 themselves, (in wee see live common-wealths,) the
 foresight preservation, contented life
 thereby; say, getting miserable
 condition warre, necessarily consequent (as hath shewn)
 naturall passions men, visible power keep
 awe, tye feare punishment performance of
 covenants, observation lawes nature set in
 fourteenth fifteenth chapters.
 



law nature:
 
lawes nature (as justice, equity, modesty, mercy, (in
 summe) others, wee done to,) themselves, without
 terrour power, cause observed, contrary to
 naturall passions, carry us partiality, pride, revenge, and
 like. covenants, without sword, words, no
 strength secure man all. therefore notwithstanding lawes of
 nature, (which every one hath kept, will keep
 them, can safely,) power erected, not
 great enough security; every man will may lawfully rely on
 strength art, caution men. all
 places, men lived small families, robbe spoyle one
 another, trade, farre reputed the
 law nature, greater spoyles gained, greater was
 honour; men observed lawes therein, lawes of
 honour; is, abstain cruelty, leaving men lives,
 instruments husbandry. small familyes then; now
 cities kingdomes greater families (for own
 security) enlarge dominions, upon pretences danger, and
 fear invasion, assistance may given invaders, endeavour
 much can, subdue, weaken neighbours, open
 force, secret arts, want caution, justly; are
 remembred ages honour.
 



conjunction men familyes
 
joyning together small number men, gives them
 security; small numbers, small additions one side
 other, make advantage strength great, sufficient
 carry victory; therefore gives encouragement invasion.
 multitude sufficient confide security, not
 determined certain number, comparison enemy we
 feare; sufficient, odds enemy so
 visible conspicuous moment, determine event warre, to
 move attempt.
 



great multitude, unlesse directed one judgement
 
never great multitude; yet actions be
 directed according particular judgements, particular
 appetites, can expect thereby defence, protection, neither
 common enemy, injuries one another. for
 distracted opinions concerning best use application
 strength, help, hinder one another; reduce
 strength mutuall opposition nothing: whereby are
 easily, onely subdued agree together; also
 common enemy, make warre upon other, for
 particular interests. suppose great multitude of
 men consent observation justice, lawes nature,
 without common power keep awe; might well suppose
 man-kind same; neither need to
 civill government, common-wealth all; would
 peace without subjection.
 



continually
 
enough security, men desire last all
 time life, governed, directed one
 judgement, limited time; one battell, one warre. for
 though obtain victory unanimous endeavour a
 forraign enemy; yet afterwards, either common enemy,
 one part held enemy, another part held for
 friend, must needs difference interests dissolve,
 fall warre amongst themselves.
 



certain creatures without reason, speech,
 



neverthelesse live society, without coercive power
 
true, certain living creatures, bees, ants, live
 sociably one another, (which therefore aristotle numbred
 amongst politicall creatures;) yet direction, than
 particular judgements appetites; speech, whereby one of
 can signifie another, thinks expedient common
 benefit: therefore man may perhaps desire know, man-kind
 same. answer,
 
first, men continually competition honour dignity,
 creatures not; consequently amongst men there
 ariseth ground, envy hatred, finally warre; amongst
 so.
 
secondly, amongst creatures, common good differeth not
 private; nature enclined private, they
 procure thereby common benefit. man, whose joy consisteth
 comparing himselfe men, can relish nothing is
 eminent.
 
thirdly, creatures, (as man) use reason,
 see, think see fault, administration their
 common businesse: whereas amongst men, many, thinke
 wiser, abler govern publique, better the
 rest; strive reforme innovate, one way, another
 way; thereby bring distraction civill warre.
 
fourthly, creatures, though use voice, in
 making knowne one another desires, affections; yet
 want art words, men can represent others,
 good, likenesse evill; evill, the
 likenesse good; augment, diminish apparent greatnesse of
 good evill; discontenting men, troubling peace their
 pleasure.
 
fiftly, irrationall creatures distinguish betweene injury, and
 dammage; therefore long ease, offended
 fellowes: whereas man troublesome, is
 ease: loves shew wisdome, and
 controule actions governe common-wealth.
 
lastly, agreement creatures naturall; men, is
 covenant only, artificiall: therefore wonder
 somewhat else required (besides covenant) make their
 agreement constant lasting; common power, keep in
 awe, direct actions common benefit.
 



generation common-wealth
 
way erect common power, may able defend them
 invasion forraigners, injuries one another, and
 thereby secure sort, owne industrie,
 fruites earth, may nourish live
 contentedly; is, conferre power strength upon one
 man, upon one assembly men, may reduce wills,
 plurality voices, unto one will: much say, to
 appoint one man, assembly men, beare person; every
 one owne, acknowledge himselfe author whatsoever he
 beareth person, shall act, cause acted, those
 things concerne common peace safetie; therein to
 submit wills, every one will, judgements, his
 judgment. consent, concord; reall unitie of
 all, one person, made covenant every man with
 every man, manner, every man say every man, "i
 authorise give right governing selfe, man, to
 assembly men, condition, thou give thy right
 him, authorise actions like manner." done, the
 multitude united one person, called common-wealth, latine
 civitas. generation great leviathan, rather (to
 speake reverently) mortall god, wee owe the
 immortall god, peace defence. authoritie, given him
 every particular man common-wealth, hath use so
 much power strength conferred him, terror thereof, is
 inabled forme wills all, peace home, mutuall
 ayd enemies abroad.
 



definition common-wealth
 
consisteth essence common-wealth; (to
 define it,) "one person, whose acts great multitude, mutuall
 covenants one another, made every one author,
 end may use strength means all, shall
 think expedient, peace common defence."
 



soveraigne, subject, what
 
carryeth person, called soveraigne, said have
 soveraigne power; every one besides, subject.
 
attaining soveraigne power, two wayes. one, by
 naturall force; man maketh children, submit themselves,
 children government, able destroy if
 refuse, warre subdueth enemies will, giving them
 lives condition. other, men agree amongst
 themselves, submit man, assembly men, voluntarily, on
 confidence protected others. later, may be
 called politicall common-wealth, common-wealth institution; and
 former, common-wealth acquisition. first, shall speak of
 common-wealth institution.
 


chapter xviii. rights soveraignes institution
 



act instituting common-wealth, what
 
common-wealth said instituted, multitude men do
 agree, covenant, every one every one, whatsoever man,
 assembly men, shall given major part, right
 present person all, (that say, their
 representative;) every one, well voted it, that
 voted it, shall authorise actions judgements, of
 man, assembly men, manner, his
 own, end, live peaceably amongst themselves, protected
 men.
 



consequences institution, are
 



1. subjects change forme government
 



institution common-wealth derived rights, and
 facultyes him, them, soveraigne power conferred by
 consent people assembled.
 
first, covenant, understood, not
 obliged former covenant thing repugnant hereunto. and
 consequently already instituted common-wealth, being
 thereby bound covenant, actions, judgements one,
 lawfully make new covenant, amongst themselves, obedient
 other, thing whatsoever, without permission. and
 therefore, subjects monarch, without leave
 cast monarchy, return confusion disunited multitude;
 transferre person beareth it, another man,
 assembly men: bound, every man every man,
 own, reputed author all, already their
 soveraigne, shall do, judge fit done: one man
 dissenting, rest break covenant made man,
 injustice: also every man given soveraignty
 beareth person; therefore depose him,
 take own, injustice.
 besides, attempteth depose soveraign, killed, or
 punished attempt, author punishment,
 institution, author soveraign shall do: and
 injustice man thing, may be
 punished authority, also upon title, unjust.
 whereas men pretended disobedience their
 soveraign, new covenant, made, men, god; also
 unjust: covenant god, mediation some
 body representeth gods person; none doth gods lieutenant,
 hath soveraignty god. pretence covenant with
 god, evident lye, even pretenders consciences, that
 onely act unjust, also vile, unmanly
 disposition.
 



2. soveraigne power forfeited
 
secondly, right bearing person all, given
 make soveraigne, covenant onely one another, and
 them; can happen breach covenant the
 part soveraigne; consequently none subjects, any
 pretence forfeiture, can freed subjection. which
 made soveraigne maketh covenant subjects beforehand, is
 manifest; either must make whole multitude, as
 one party covenant; must make severall covenant with
 every man. whole, one party, impossible; as
 yet one person: make many severall covenants
 men, covenants hath soveraignty voyd,
 act soever can pretended one breach
 thereof, act himselfe, rest, done
 person, right every one particular.
 besides, one, them, pretend breach covenant
 made soveraigne institution; others, one of
 subjects, himselfe alone, pretend breach,
 case, judge decide controversie: returns
 therefore sword again; every man recovereth right of
 protecting himselfe strength, contrary designe they
 institution. therefore vain grant soveraignty by
 way precedent covenant. opinion monarch receiveth his
 power covenant, say condition, proceedeth want
 understanding easie truth, covenants words, and
 breath, force oblige, contain, constrain, protect man,
 publique sword; is, untyed hands
 man, assembly men hath soveraignty, whose
 actions avouched all, performed strength them
 all, united. assembly men made soveraigne; then
 man imagineth covenant past institution; for
 man dull say, example, people rome, made
 covenant romans, hold soveraignty such
 conditions; performed, romans might lawfully depose the
 roman people. men see reason alike monarchy, and
 popular government, proceedeth ambition some, that
 kinder government assembly, whereof may hope to
 participate, monarchy, despair enjoy.
 



3. man can without injustice protest institution the
 soveraigne declared major part.
 
thirdly, major part hath consenting voices declared a
 soveraigne; dissented must now consent rest; is,
 contented avow actions shall do, else justly be
 destroyed rest. voluntarily entered the
 congregation assembled, sufficiently declared
 thereby will (and therefore tacitely covenanted) stand what
 major part ordayne: therefore refuse stand
 thereto, make protestation decrees, does
 contrary covenant, therfore unjustly. whether of
 congregation, not; whether consent asked, not, he
 must either submit decrees, left condition of
 warre before; wherein might without injustice destroyed
 man whatsoever.
 



4. soveraigns actions justly accused subject
 
fourthly, every subject institution author the
 actions, judgements soveraigne instituted; followes, that
 whatsoever doth, can injury subjects; nor
 accused injustice. doth any
 thing authority another, doth therein injury whose
 authority acteth: institution common-wealth, every
 particular man author soveraigne doth; consequently
 complaineth injury soveraigne, complaineth that
 whereof himselfe author; therefore accuse man
 himselfe; himselfe injury; injury ones
 selfe, impossible. true soveraigne
 power, may commit iniquity; injustice, injury proper
 signification.
 



5. soever soveraigne doth, unpunishable subject
 
fiftly, consequently sayd last, man hath
 soveraigne power can justly put death, otherwise manner
 subjects punished. seeing every subject author the
 actions soveraigne; punisheth another, actions
 committed himselfe.
 



6. soveraigne judge necessary peace and
 defence subjects
 
end institution, peace defence of
 all; whosoever right end, right means;
 belongeth right, whatsoever man, assembly hath the
 soveraignty, judge meanes peace defence;
 also hindrances, disturbances same; do
 whatsoever shall think necessary done, beforehand, the
 preserving peace security, prevention discord home and
 hostility abroad; and, peace security lost, the
 recovery same. therefore,
 



judge doctrines fit taught them
 
sixtly, annexed soveraignty, judge opinions
 doctrines averse, conducing peace; consequently,
 occasions, farre, what, men trusted withall,
 speaking multitudes people; shall examine doctrines
 bookes published. actions men proceed
 opinions; wel governing opinions, consisteth
 well governing mens actions, order peace, and
 concord. though matter doctrine, nothing regarded
 truth; yet repugnant regulating by
 peace. doctrine repugnant peace, can true, peace
 concord can law nature. true, in
 common-wealth, negligence, unskilfullnesse of
 governours, teachers, false doctrines time generally
 received; contrary truths may generally offensive; yet most
 sudden, rough busling new truth, can be, never
 breake peace, onely somtimes awake warre. men that
 remissely governed, dare take armes, defend, or
 introduce opinion, still warre; condition peace,
 cessation armes feare one another; live
 were, procincts battaile continually. belongeth
 therefore hath soveraign power, judge, or
 constitute judges opinions doctrines, thing necessary to
 peace, thereby prevent discord civill warre.
 



7. right making rules, whereby subject may every man know
 owne, subject can without injustice take it
 him
 
seventhly, annexed soveraigntie, whole power of
 prescribing rules, whereby every man may know, goods may
 enjoy actions may doe, without molested of
 fellow subjects: men call propriety. before
 constitution soveraign power (as hath already shewn) men had
 right things; necessarily causeth warre: therefore this
 proprietie, necessary peace, depending soveraign power,
 act power, order publique peace. rules of
 propriety (or meum tuum) good, evill, lawfull unlawfull
 actions subjects, civill lawes, say, the
 lawes commonwealth particular; though name civill law
 now restrained antient civill lawes city rome; which
 head great part world, lawes time were
 parts civill law.
 



8. also belongeth right judicature decision of
 controversies:
 
eightly, annexed soveraigntie, right judicature; that
 say, hearing deciding controversies, may arise
 concerning law, either civill, naturall, concerning fact. for
 without decision controversies, protection one
 subject, injuries another; lawes concerning meum and
 tuum vaine; every man remaineth, naturall and
 necessary appetite conservation, right protecting
 himselfe private strength, condition warre; and
 contrary end every common-wealth instituted.
 



9. making war, peace, shall think best:
 
ninthly, annexed soveraignty, right making warre, and
 peace nations, common-wealths; say, of
 judging publique good, great forces to
 assembled, armed, payd end; levy mony upon the
 subjects, defray expenses thereof. power the
 people defended, consisteth armies; strength
 army, union strength one command; which
 command soveraign instituted, therefore hath; command
 militia, without institution, maketh hath it
 soveraign. therefore whosoever made generall army, that
 hath soveraign power alwayes generallissimo.
 



10. choosing counsellours, ministers, peace, and
 warre:
 
tenthly, annexed soveraignty, choosing all
 councellours, ministers, magistrates, officers, peace, and
 war. seeing soveraign charged end, the
 common peace defence; understood power use such
 means, shall think fit discharge.
 



11. rewarding, punishing, (where no
 former law hath determined measure it) arbitrary:
 
eleventhly, soveraign committed power rewarding
 riches, honour; punishing corporall, pecuniary
 punishment, ignominy every subject according lawe hath
 formerly made; law made, according shall judge
 conduce encouraging men serve common-wealth, or
 deterring dis-service same.
 



12. honour order
 
lastly, considering values men naturally apt set upon
 themselves; respect look others; little they
 value men; whence continually arise amongst them, emulation,
 quarrells, factions, last warre, destroying one
 another, diminution strength common enemy; it
 necessary lawes honour, publique rate the
 worth men deserved, able deserve well the
 common-wealth; force hands other, to
 put lawes execution. hath already shown, not
 onely whole militia, forces common-wealth; also the
 judicature controversies, annexed soveraignty. the
 soveraign therefore belongeth also give titles honour; to
 appoint order place, dignity, man shall hold; what
 signes respect, publique private meetings, shall give to
 one another.
 



rights indivisible
 
rights, make essence soveraignty; which
 markes, whereby man may discern man, assembly
 men, soveraign power placed, resideth. are
 incommunicable, inseparable. power coyn mony; dispose of
 estate persons infant heires; praeemption in
 markets; statute praerogatives, may transferred the
 soveraign; yet power protect subject retained. if
 transferre militia, retains judicature vain, want
 execution lawes; grant away power raising
 mony; militia vain: give away government of
 doctrines, men will frighted rebellion feare of
 spirits. consider one said rights, shall
 presently see, holding rest, will produce no
 effect, conservation peace justice, end all
 common-wealths instituted. division it, whereof is
 said, "a kingdome divided selfe stand:" unlesse this
 division precede, division opposite armies can never happen. if
 first opinion received greatest part of
 england, powers divided king, lords,
 house commons, people never divided, and
 fallen civill warre; first disagreed
 politiques; dissenters liberty of
 religion; instructed men point soveraign right,
 now (in england,) see, rights
 inseparable, will generally acknowledged, next
 return peace; continue, till miseries forgotten; and
 longer, except vulgar better taught hetherto
 been.
 



can grant passe away without direct renouncing the

essentiall inseparable rights, follows

power honour subjects vanisheth presence power
 soveraign
 
great authority indivisible, inseparably annexed the

power, also honour soveraign, be

 greatest part submitting readily, lesse

 him, unlimited power hands. and

 make necessary governours draw can

chapter xix. severall kinds common-wealth institution,
 succession soveraigne power
 



different formes common-wealths three
 
difference common-wealths, consisteth difference the
 soveraign, person representative every one the
 multitude. soveraignty either one man, an
 assembly one; assembly either every man hath
 right enter, every one, certain men distinguished the
 rest; manifest, can three kinds common-wealth. for
 representative must needs one man, more: more, it
 assembly all, part. representative one
 man, common-wealth monarchy: assembly that
 will come together, democracy, popular common-wealth:
 assembly part onely, called aristocracy.
 kind common-wealth can none: either one, or
 more, must soveraign power (which shewn be
 indivisible) entire.
 



tyranny oligarchy, different names monarchy, aristocracy
 
names government, histories, books of
 policy; tyranny, oligarchy: names other
 formes government, formes misliked. that
 discontented monarchy, call tyranny; are
 displeased aristocracy, called oligarchy: also, which
 find grieved democracy, call anarchy, (which
 signifies want government;) yet think man believes, that
 want government, new kind government: same
 reason believe, government one kind, when
 like it, another, mislike it, oppressed the
 governours.
 



subordinate representatives dangerous
 
manifest, men absolute liberty, may, they
 please, give authority one man, represent every one; as
 well give authority assembly men whatsoever; and
 consequently may subject themselves, think good, monarch,
 absolutely, representative. therefore, is
 already erected soveraign power, can representative
 people, onely certain particular ends, the
 soveraign limited. erect two soveraigns; every
 man person represented two actors, opposing one
 another, must needs divide power, (if men will live peace)
 indivisible, thereby reduce multitude condition of
 warre, contrary end soveraignty instituted. and
 therefore absurd, think soveraign assembly, inviting
 people dominion, send deputies, power
 make known advise, desires, therefore hold such
 deputies, rather themselves, absolute representative of
 people: absurd also, think monarchy. and
 know manifest truth, late little
 observed; monarchy, soveraignty descent
 600 years, alone called soveraign, title majesty from
 every one subjects, unquestionably taken them
 king; notwithstanding never considered their
 representative; name without contradiction passing title
 men, command sent people carry
 petitions, give (if permitted it) advise. which
 may serve admonition, true, absolute
 representative people, instruct men nature that
 office, take heed admit generall
 representation upon occasion whatsoever, mean discharge
 truth committed them.
 



comparison monarchy, soveraign assemblyes
 
difference three kindes common-wealth, consisteth
 difference power; difference convenience, or
 aptitude produce peace, security people; end
 instituted. compare monarchy two, may
 observe; first, whosoever beareth person people, or
 one assembly bears it, beareth also naturall
 person. though carefull politique person procure
 common interest; yet more, lesse carefull procure the
 private good himselfe, family, kindred friends; the
 part, publique interest chance crosse private, he
 preferrs private: passions men, commonly potent
 reason. whence follows, publique and
 private interest closely united, publique most
 advanced. now monarchy, private interest the
 publique. riches, power, honour monarch arise onely from
 riches, strength reputation subjects. king can
 rich, glorious, secure; whose subjects either poore, or
 contemptible, weak want, dissention, maintain a
 war enemies: whereas democracy, aristocracy, the
 publique prosperity conferres much private fortune one
 corrupt, ambitious, doth many times perfidious advice, a
 treacherous action, civill warre.
 
secondly, monarch receiveth counsell whom, when, he
 pleaseth; consequently may heare opinion men versed the
 matter deliberates, rank quality soever, and
 long time action, much secrecy, will.
 soveraigne assembly need counsell, none admitted
 right thereto beginning; the
 part beene versed acquisition
 wealth knowledge; give advice long
 discourses, may, commonly excite men action, but
 governe it. understanding flame the
 passions, never enlightned, dazled: place, time,
 wherein assemblie can receive counsell secrecie, of
 owne multitude.
 
thirdly, resolutions monarch, subject other
 inconstancy, humane nature; assemblies, besides that
 nature, ariseth inconstancy number. absence
 few, resolution taken, continue firme,
 (which may happen security, negligence, private impediments,) or
 diligent appearance contrary opinion, undoes day,
 concluded yesterday.
 
fourthly, monarch disagree himselfe, envy, or
 interest; assembly may; height, may produce
 civill warre.
 
fifthly, monarchy inconvenience; subject,
 power one man, enriching favourite flatterer,
 may deprived possesseth; confesse great and
 inevitable inconvenience. may well happen, the
 soveraigne power assembly: power same; and
 subject evill counsell, seduced orators, as
 monarch flatterers; becoming one others flatterers, serve
 one anothers covetousnesse ambition turnes. whereas the
 favorites assembly, many; kindred much numerous,
 monarch. besides, favourite monarch, which
 well succour friends, hurt enemies: orators,
 say, favourites soveraigne assemblies, though have
 great power hurt, little save. accuse, requires lesse
 eloquence (such mans nature) excuse; condemnation, than
 absolution resembles justice.
 
sixtly, inconvenience monarchie, soveraigntie
 may descend upon infant, one discerne good and
 evill: consisteth this, use power, must the
 hand another man, assembly men, governe by
 right, name; curators, protectors person,
 authority. say inconvenience, putting use of
 soveraign power, hand man, assembly men; is
 say government inconvenient, confusion, and
 civill warre. therefore danger can pretended, must
 arise contention those, office great
 honour, profit, may become competitors. make appear, that
 inconvenience, proceedeth forme government call
 monarchy, consider, precedent monarch, hath appointed
 shall tuition infant successor, either expressely
 testament, tacitly, controlling custome that
 case received: inconvenience (if happen) be
 attributed, monarchy, ambition, injustice of
 subjects; kinds government, people are
 well instructed duty, rights soveraignty, is
 same. else precedent monarch, hath taken order for
 tuition; law nature hath provided sufficient
 rule, tuition shall him, hath nature most
 interest preservation authority infant, whom
 least benefit can accrue death, diminution. seeing every
 man nature seeketh benefit, promotion; put infant
 power those, can promote destruction,
 dammage, tuition, trechery. sufficient provision
 taken, just quarrell, government a
 child, contention arise disturbance publique peace,
 attributed forme monarchy, ambition
 subjects, ignorance duty. side, is
 great common-wealth, soveraignty whereof great assembly,
 not, consultations peace, warre, making of
 lawes, condition, government child. for
 child wants judgement dissent counsell given him, and
 thereby necessitated take advise them, him, he
 committed: assembly wanteth liberty, dissent the
 counsell major part, good, bad. child need
 tutor, protector, preserve person, authority: also
 (in great common-wealths,) soveraign assembly, great dangers
 troubles, need custodes libertatis; dictators, or
 protectors authoritie; much temporary monarchs;
 time, may commit entire exercise power;
 (at end time) oftner deprived thereof, than
 infant kings, protectors, regents, tutors.
 
though kinds soveraigntie be, now shewn, three;
 say, monarchie, one man it; democracie, where
 generall assembly subjects hath it; aristocracie, is
 assembly certain persons nominated, otherwise distinguished
 rest: yet shall consider particular common-wealthes
 been, world, will perhaps easily reduce
 three, may thereby inclined think other
 formes, arising mingled together. example, elective
 kingdomes; kings soveraigne power put hands
 time; kingdomes, wherein king hath power limited: which
 governments, nevertheless writers called monarchie. likewise
 popular, aristocraticall common-wealth, subdue enemies
 countrie, govern same, president, procurator, or
 magistrate; may seeme perhaps first sight, a
 democraticall, aristocraticall government. so. for
 elective kings, soveraignes, ministers soveraigne;
 limited kings soveraignes, ministers the
 soveraigne power: provinces subjection a
 democracie, aristocracie another common-wealth, democratically, or
 aristocratically governed, monarchically.
 
first, concerning elective king, whose power limited to
 life, many places christendome day; to
 certaine yeares moneths, dictators power amongst romans;
 right appoint successor, elective but
 hereditary. power elect successor, there
 man, assembly known, decease may elect
 new, else common-wealth dieth, dissolveth him, and
 returneth condition warre. known power
 give soveraigntie death, known also the
 soveraigntie before: none right give which
 right possesse, keep themselves, think
 good. none can give soveraigntie, the
 decease first elected; power, nay is
 obliged law nature, provide, establishing successor,
 keep trusted government, relapsing
 miserable condition civill warre. consequently was,
 elected, soveraign absolute.
 
secondly, king whose power limited, superiour him, or
 power limit it; superiour, is
 supreme; say soveraign. soveraignty therefore
 alwaies assembly right limit him; and
 consequence government monarchy, either democracy, or
 aristocracy; old time sparta; kings priviledge
 lead armies; soveraignty ephori.
 
thirdly, whereas heretofore roman people, governed land judea
 (for example) president; yet judea therefore democracy;
 governed assembly, which, of
 them, right enter; aristocracy; were
 governed assembly, which, man enter their
 election: governed one person, though the
 people rome assembly people, democracy; yet to
 people judea, right participating the
 government, monarch. though people governed
 assembly, chosen number, the
 government called democracy, aristocracy; yet are
 governed assembly, choosing, ’tis monarchy; not
 one man, another man; one people, another people.
 



right succession
 
formes government, matter mortall, not
 onely monarchs, also whole assemblies dy, necessary the
 conservation peace men, order taken for
 artificiall man, order also taken, artificiall
 eternity life; without which, men governed assembly,
 return condition warre every age; they
 governed one man, soon governour dyeth. this
 artificiall eternity, men call right succession.
 
perfect forme government, disposing the
 succession present soveraign. other
 particular man, private assembly, person subject, may
 assumed soveraign pleasure; consequently right
 himselfe. particular man, left new
 choyce; common-wealth dissolved; right him
 can get it; contrary intention institute
 common-wealth, perpetuall, temporary security.
 
democracy, whole assembly faile, unlesse multitude
 governed faile. therefore questions right of
 succession, forme government place all.
 
aristocracy, assembly dyeth, election of
 another room belongeth assembly, soveraign, to
 belongeth choosing counsellours, officers. that
 representative doth, actor, every one subjects doth,
 author. though soveraign assembly, may give power others,
 elect new men, supply court; yet still their
 authority, election made; may (when the
 publique shall require it) recalled.
 
present monarch hath right dispose succession greatest
 difficultie right succession, monarchy: the
 difficulty ariseth this, first sight, manifest
 appoint successor; many times, he
 hath appointed. cases, required exact
 ratiocination, every man accustomed use. question,
 shall appoint successor, monarch hath soveraign
 authority; say, (for elective kings princes the
 soveraign power propriety, use only,) consider, that
 either possession, right dispose succession,
 else right dissolved multitude. death
 hath soveraign power propriety, leaves multitude

chapter xxi. liberty subjects
 



liberty what
 
liberty, freedome, signifieth (properly) absence opposition;
 (by opposition, mean externall impediments motion;) may
 applyed lesse irrational, inanimate creatures, to
 rationall. whatsoever tyed, environed, move,
 within certain space, space determined opposition
 externall body, say hath liberty go further. and
 living creatures, whilest imprisoned, restrained,
 walls, chayns; water whilest kept banks,
 vessels, otherwise spread selfe larger space, we
 use say, liberty, move manner, without
 externall impediments would. impediment of
 motion, constitution thing selfe, use to
 say, wants liberty; power move; stone lyeth
 still, man fastned bed sicknesse.
 



free
 
according proper, generally received meaning the
 word, free-man, "he, things, strength
 wit able do, hindred doe will
 to." words free, liberty, applyed thing but

 doe.

liberty necessity consistent: water, hath not

 see connexion causes, necessity all

 will, accompanied necessity that
 god will, & more, lesse. though men may many things,

 will cause. will assure necessity mans
 will, consequently mans will dependeth, liberty
 men contradiction, impediment omnipotence and
 liberty god. shall suffice, (as matter hand) of

 own, anothers sword, nature applyeth obedience it, and
 endeavour maintaine it. though soveraignty, intention
 make it, immortall; yet nature, not
 subject violent death, forreign war; also through
 ignorance, passions men, hath it, very
 institution, many seeds naturall mortality, intestine discord.
 



case captivity
 
subject taken prisoner war; person, means of
 life within guards enemy, hath life corporall
 libertie given him, condition subject victor, hath
 libertie accept condition; accepted it, subject
 took him; way preserve himselfe.
 case same, deteined termes, a
 forreign country. man held prison, bonds, not
 trusted libertie bodie; understood be
 bound covenant subjection; therefore may, can, make his
 escape means whatsoever.
 



case soveraign cast government heyrs
 
monarch shall relinquish soveraignty, himself, and
 heires; subjects returne absolute libertie nature;
 because, though nature may declare sons, the
 nerest kin; yet dependeth will, (as hath said
 precedent chapter,) shall heyr. therefore will
 heyre, soveraignty, subjection. case the
 same, dye without known kindred, without declaration of
 heyre. can heire known, consequently no
 subjection due.
 



case banishment
 
soveraign banish subject; banishment, not
 subject. sent message, hath leave travell, is
 still subject; is, contract soveraigns, vertue
 covenant subjection. whosoever entreth anothers
 dominion, subject lawes thereof; unless a
 privilege amity soveraigns, speciall licence.
 



case soveraign render subject another
 
monarch subdued war, render subject victor; his
 subjects delivered former obligation, become obliged
 victor. held prisoner, liberty
 body; understood given away right of
 soveraigntie; therefore subjects obliged yield obedience
 magistrates formerly placed, governing name,
 his. for, right remaining, question the
 administration; say, magistrates officers; which,
 means name, supposed approve those, he
 formerly appointed.

bodies politique government province, colony, town
 
variety bodies politique, almost infinite; are

 word province signifies charge, care businesse, he

bodies politique ordering trade
 
bodie politique, well ordering forraigne traffique, the
 commodious representative assembly members; that
 say, one, every one adventureth mony, may be
 present deliberations, resolutions body, they
 will themselves. proof whereof, consider end, for
 men merchants, may buy sell, export, import

 bind one corporation. true, few
 merchants, merchandise buy home, can fraight a

 therefore need joyn together one society; every man

 adventure; take own; sell transports, imports, at
 prices thinks fit. body politique, being
 common representative oblige law, that
 common subjects. end incorporating,
 make gaine greater; done two wayes; sole
 buying, sole selling, home, abroad. grant
 company merchants corporation, body politique, to
 grant double monopoly, whereof one sole buyers; another
 sole sellers. company incorporate any
 particular forraign country, export commodities vendible
 country; sole buying home, sole selling abroad.
 home one buyer, abroad one selleth:
 gainfull merchant, thereby buy home
 lower, sell abroad higher rates: abroad one
 buyer forraign merchandise, one sels home; both
 againe gainfull adventurers.
 
double monopoly one part disadvantageous people at
 home, forraigners. home sole exportation
 set price please husbandry handy-works of
 people; sole importation, price please all
 forraign commodities people need of; ill the
 people. contrary, sole selling native commodities

 raise price those, abate price these, to
 disadvantage forraigner: one selleth, the
 merchandise dearer; one buyeth cheaper: such
 corporations therefore monopolies; though would
 profitable common-wealth, bound one body
 forraigne markets liberty home, every man buy, and
 sell price could.

irregular systemes, nature, leagues, sometimes meer

 designe understood occasion.
 
leagues subjects, (because leagues commonly made mutuall

 means soveraign power, unnecessary maintaining of

 publique, unjustly concealed.
