chapter xxiii. publique ministers soveraign power
 

last chapter spoken similar parts a
 common-wealth; shall speak parts organicall, are
 publique ministers.
 



publique minister who
 
publique minister, he, soveraign, (whether monarch,
 assembly,) employed affaires, authority to
 represent employment, person common-wealth. and
 whereas every man, assembly hath soveraignty, representeth
 two persons, (as common phrase is) two capacities, one
 naturall, another politique, (as monarch, hath person not
 onely common-wealth, also man; soveraign assembly
 hath person onely common-wealth, also the
 assembly); servants naturall capacity,
 publique ministers; onely serve the
 administration publique businesse. therefore neither ushers,
 sergeants, officers waite assembly, for
 purpose, commodity men assembled, an
 aristocracy, democracy; stewards, chamberlains, cofferers, any
 officers houshold monarch, publique ministers a
 monarchy.
 



ministers generall administration
 
publique ministers, charge committed general
 administration, either whole dominion, part thereof.
 whole, protector, regent, may bee committed by
 predecessor infant king, minority, whole
 administration kingdome. case, every subject far
 obliged obedience, ordinances shall make, commands
 shall give kings name, inconsistent his
 soveraigne power. part, province; either monarch, or
 soveraign assembly, shall give generall charge thereof a
 governour, lieutenant, praefect, vice-roy: case also,
 every one province, obliged shall doe name
 soveraign, incompatible soveraigns right.
 protectors, vice-roys, governours, right, but
 depends soveraigns will; commission can given
 them, can interpreted declaration will transferre the
 soveraignty, without expresse perspicuous words purpose. and
 kind publique ministers resembleth nerves, tendons that
 move severall limbs body naturall.
 



speciall administration, oeconomy
 
others speciall administration; say, charges some
 speciall businesse, either home, abroad: home, first, for
 oeconomy common-wealth, authority concerning the
 treasure, tributes, impositions, rents, fines, whatsoever publique
 revenue, collect, receive, issue, take accounts thereof,
 publique ministers: ministers, serve person
 representative, can doe nothing command, without his
 authority: publique, serve politicall capacity.
 
secondly, authority concerning militia; the
 custody armes, forts, ports; levy, pay, conduct souldiers; or
 provide necessary thing use war, either land or
 sea, publique ministers. souldier without command, though he
 fight common-wealth, therefore represent person of
 it; none represent to. every one hath
 command, represents commandeth.
 



instruction people
 
also authority teach, enable others teach
 people duty soveraign power, instruct the
 knowledge just, unjust, thereby render apt
 live godlinesse, peace among themselves, resist the
 publique enemy, publique ministers: ministers, doe it
 authority, anothers; publique, they
 doe (or doe it) authority, soveraign.
 monarch, soveraign assembly hath immediate authority
 god, teach instruct people; man the
 soveraign, receiveth power dei gratia simply; say, from
 favour none god: other, receive favour
 providence god, soveraigns; monarchy dei gratia
 & regis; dei providentia & voluntate regis.
 



judicature
 
also jurisdiction given, publique ministers. in
 seats justice represent person soveraign; and
 sentence, sentence; (as hath declared) all
 judicature essentially annexed soveraignty; therefore all
 judges ministers him, soveraign
 power. controversies two sorts, namely fact, of
 law; judgements, fact, law: consequently in
 controversie, may two judges, one fact, another of
 law.
 
controversies, may arise controversie between
 party judged, judge; subjects to
 soveraign, equity judged men agreed consent
 both; man can judge cause. soveraign
 already agreed judge both, therefore either to
 heare cause, determine himself, appoint judge as
 shall agree on. agreement understood be
 made divers wayes; first, defendant allowed
 except judges, whose interest maketh suspect
 them, (for complaynant hath already chosen judge,)
 excepteth against, judges agrees on.
 secondly, appeale judge, can appeale further;
 appeale choice. thirdly, appeale soveraign
 himself, himself, delegates parties shall
 agree on, give sentence; sentence finall: defendant is
 judged judges, say, himself.
 
properties just rationall judicature considered, cannot
 forbeare observe excellent constitution courts justice,
 established common, also publique pleas england. by
 common pleas, meane those, complaynant defendant
 subjects: publique, (which also called pleas the
 crown) those, complaynant soveraign. whereas there
 two orders men, whereof one lords, commons; the
 lords priviledge, judges capitall crimes,
 none lords; them, many present; being
 ever acknowledged priviledge favour, judges none but
 desired. controversies, every
 subject (as also civill controversies lords) judges, men
 country matter controversie lay; he
 might make exceptions, till last twelve men without exception
 agreed on, judged twelve. having
 judges, nothing alledged party, the
 sentence finall, publique persons, authority
 soveraign power, either instruct, judge people,
 members common-wealth, may fitly compared the
 organs voice body naturall.

counsellers without employment advise publique
 ministers
 
neither counsellor, councell state, consider with

chapter xxiv. nutrition, procreation common-wealth
 


nourishment common-wealth consisteth commodities
 
land
 
nutrition common-wealth consisteth, plenty, and
 distribution materials conducing life: concoction, or
 preparation; (when concocted) conveyance it, convenient
 conduits, publique use.
 
plenty matter, thing limited nature, those
 commodities, (the two breasts common mother) land,
 sea, god usually either freely giveth, labour selleth to
 man-kind.
 
matter nutriment, consisting animals, vegetals, and
 minerals, god hath freely layd us, neer face of
 earth; needeth labour, industry
 receiving them. insomuch plenty dependeth (next gods favour)
 meerly labour industry men.
 
matter, commonly called commodities, partly native, partly
 forraign: native, within territory of
 common-wealth; forraign, imported without. and
 territory dominion one common-wealth,
 (except vast extent,) produceth things needfull
 maintenance, motion whole body; produce
 something necessary; superfluous commodities had
 within, become superfluous, supply wants home, by
 importation may abroad, either exchange, or
 just warre, labour: mans labour also, commodity
 exchangeable benefit, well thing: have
 common-wealths territory, hath served
 habitation, neverthelesse, onely maintained, also
 encreased power, partly labour trading one place to
 another, partly selling manifactures, whereof materials
 brought places.
 



right distribution them
 
distribution materials nourishment, the
 constitution mine, thine, his, say, one word
 propriety; belongeth kinds common-wealth soveraign
 power. common-wealth, is, (as hath been
 already shewn) perpetuall warre every man neighbour;
 therefore every thing getteth it, keepeth by
 force; neither propriety community; uncertainty. which
 evident, even cicero, (a passionate defender liberty,) in
 publique pleading, attributeth propriety law civil, "let
 civill law," saith he, "be abandoned, negligently
 guarded, (not say oppressed,) nothing, man can
 sure receive ancestor, leave children." and
 again; "take away civill law, man knows own, and
 another mans." seeing therefore introduction propriety is
 effect common-wealth; can nothing person that
 represents it, act onely soveraign; consisteth in
 lawes, none can make soveraign power. and
 well knew old, called nomos, (that say,
 distribution,) call law; defined justice, distributing
 every man own.
 



private estates land proceed originally arbitrary
 distribution soveraign
 
distribution, first law, division land it
 selfe: wherein soveraign assigneth every man portion, according
 he, according subject, number them, shall
 judge agreeable equity, common good. children israel,
 common-wealth wildernesse; wanted commodities
 earth, till masters land promise; which
 afterward divided amongst them, discretion, but
 discretion eleazar priest, joshua generall: who
 twelve tribes, making thirteen subdivision of
 tribe joseph; made neverthelesse twelve portions land;
 ordained tribe levi land; assigned tenth
 part whole fruits; division therefore arbitrary. and
 though people comming possession land warre, not
 alwaies exterminate antient inhabitants, (as jewes,) but
 leave many, most, estates; yet manifest
 hold afterwards, victors distribution; people
 england held william conquerour.
 



propriety subject excludes dominion soveraign, but
 onely another subject
 
whence may collect, propriety subject hath in
 lands, consisteth right exclude subjects the
 use them; exclude soveraign, assembly, or
 monarch. seeing soveraign, say, common-wealth
 (whose person representeth,) understood nothing order
 common peace security, distribution lands, be
 understood done order same: consequently, whatsoever
 distribution shall make prejudice thereof, contrary the
 will every subject, committed peace, safety his
 discretion, conscience; therefore will every one of
 them, reputed voyd. true, soveraign monarch, or
 greater part soveraign assembly, may ordain many
 things pursuit passions, contrary consciences,
 breach trust, law nature; not
 enough authorise subject, either make warre upon, much
 accuse injustice, way speak evill soveraign;
 authorised actions, bestowing the
 soveraign power, made own. cases commands
 soveraigns contrary equity, law nature, be
 considered hereafter another place.
 



publique dieted
 
distribution land, common-wealth selfe, may be
 conceived portion, possesse, improve by
 representative; portion may made sufficient, to
 susteine whole expence common peace, defence necessarily
 required: true, representative
 conceived free humane passions, infirmities. nature
 men is, setting forth publique land, any

places matter traffique depend, distribution, on

laws transferring property belong also soveraign
 
further, seeing enough sustentation common-wealth,

 taking hire,) bee made; words, signes they

mony bloud common-wealth
 
concoction, understand reducing commodities, are
 presently consumed, reserved nourishment time come, to
 thing equal value, withall portably, hinder
 motion men place place; end man may in

 nothing else gold, silver, mony. gold silver, being

 commodious measure value things else nations; and
 mony (of matter soever coyned soveraign common-wealth,)
 sufficient measure value things else, the
 subjects common-wealth. means measures, all

 way, every member body man.
 
silver gold, value matter self;

 unable endure change ayr, hath effect home only; where

conduits way mony publique use
 
conduits, wayes conveyed publique use, are
 two sorts; one, conveyeth publique coffers; other,
 issueth againe publique payments. first

 maintains resemblance naturall; whose veins receiving the

 made vitall, heart arteries sends again, to

children common-wealth colonies
 
procreation, children common-wealth, call

 country, either formerly voyd inhabitants, made voyd then, by

 remain united metropolis, colonies people of
 rome; common-wealths themselves, provinces, and

 plant.
 


chapter xxv. counsell
 



counsell what
 
fallacious judge nature things, ordinary
 inconstant use words, appeareth nothing more, the
 confusion counsels, commands, arising imperative manner
 speaking both, many occasions besides. the
 words "doe this," words onely commandeth; but
 also giveth counsell; exhorteth; yet
 few, see not, different things;
 distinguish them, perceive it
 speaketh, speech directed, upon what
 occasion. finding phrases mens writings, not
 able, willing enter consideration circumstances,
 mistake sometimes precepts counsellours, precepts
 command; sometimes contrary; according best
 agreeth conclusions inferre, actions
 approve. avoyd mistakes, render termes
 commanding, counselling, exhorting, proper distinct
 significations, define thus.
 



differences command counsell
 
command is, man saith, "doe this," "doe not," without
 expecting reason will sayes it. it
 followeth manifestly, commandeth, pretendeth thereby his
 benefit: reason command will onely, and
 proper object every mans will, good himselfe.
 
counsell, man saith, "doe" "doe this," deduceth
 reasons benefit arriveth he
 saith it. evident, giveth counsell,
 pretendeth onely (whatsoever intendeth) good him, he
 giveth it.
 
therefore counsell command, one great difference is, that
 command directed mans benefit; counsell benefit
 another man. ariseth another difference, man
 may obliged commanded; hath covenanted
 obey: obliged counselled, the
 hurt following it, own; covenant follow
 it, counsell turned nature command. third
 difference is, man can pretend right of
 another mans counsell; pretend benefit to
 himselfe; demand right counsell another, argues will know
 designes, gain good himselfe; (as said
 before) every mans will proper object.
 
also incident nature counsell; whatsoever be,
 asketh it, equity accuse, punish it: ask
 counsell another, permit give counsell shall
 think best; consequently, giveth counsell soveraign,
 (whether monarch, assembly) asketh it, equity
 punished it, whether conformable opinion of
 most, not, proposition debate. the
 sense assembly can taken notice of, debate be
 ended, neither ask, take counsell; the
 sense assembly, resolution debate, end all
 deliberation. generally demandeth counsell, author it;
 therefore punish it; soveraign cannot, man
 else can. one subject giveth counsell another, any
 thing contrary lawes, whether counsell proceed from
 evill intention, ignorance onely, punishable the
 common-wealth; ignorance law, good excuse, where
 every man bound take notice lawes subject.
 



exhortation dehortation what
 
exhortation, dehortation, counsell, accompanied signes in
 giveth it, vehement desire followed; say it
 briefly, counsell vehemently pressed. exhorteth, doth
 deduce consequences adviseth done, tye
 himselfe therein rigour true reasoning; encourages he
 counselleth, action: dehorteth, deterreth it. and
 therefore speeches, regard common passions,
 opinions men, deducing reasons; make use of
 similitudes, metaphors, examples, tooles oratory, to
 perswade hearers utility, honour, justice following
 advise.
 
whence may inferred, first, exhortation dehortation,
 directed good giveth counsell, that
 asketh it, contrary duty counsellour; (by the
 definition counsell) regard, benefits, his
 adviseth. directeth counsell own
 benefit, manifest enough, long vehement urging, by
 artificial giving thereof; required him, and
 consequently proceeding occasions, directed principally
 benefit, accidentarily good is
 counselled, all.
 
secondly, use exhortation dehortation lyeth onely, where
 man speak multitude; speech addressed
 one, may interrupt him, examine reasons rigorously,
 can done multitude; many enter into
 dispute, dialogue speaketh indifferently them
 once. thirdly, exhort dehort, are
 required give counsell, corrupt counsellours, were
 bribed interest. though counsell give never
 good; yet gives it, good counsellour, he
 giveth just sentence reward, just judge. a
 man may lawfully command, father family, leader an
 army, exhortations dehortations, onely lawfull, but
 also necessary, laudable: counsells, but
 commands; execution soure labour; sometimes
 necessity, alwayes humanity requireth sweetned the
 delivery, encouragement, tune phrase counsell,
 rather harsher language command.
 
examples difference command counsell, may take
 formes speech expresse holy scripture. "have no
 gods me; make thy selfe graven image; take gods name
 vain; sanctifie sabbath; honour thy parents; kill not; steale
 not," &c. commands; reason obey
 them, drawn will god king, obliged to
 obey. words, "sell thou hast; give poore; and
 follow me," counsell; reason do
 so, drawn benefit; this, shall have
 "treasure heaven." words, "go village against
 you, shall find asse tyed, colt; loose her, bring
 me," command: reason fact drawn from
 will master: words, "repent, baptized in
 name jesus," counsell; reason so
 do, tendeth benefit god almighty, shall still king
 manner soever rebell; selves, other
 means avoyding punishment hanging us sins.
 



differences fit unfit counsellours
 
difference counsell command, hath now deduced from
 nature counsell, consisting deducing benefit, or
 hurt may arise counselled, necessary
 probable consequences action propoundeth; may also the
 differences apt, inept counsellours derived the
 same. experience, memory consequences like
 actions formerly observed, counsell speech whereby that
 experience made known another; vertues, defects of
 counsell, vertues, defects intellectuall:
 person common-wealth, counsellours serve the

 great importance; is, naturall man receiveth his

 without passion, interest own; whereas give
 counsell representative person common-wealth, may have,
 often particular ends, passions, render their

 may set first condition good counsellour, his

secondly, office counsellour, action comes
 deliberation, make manifest consequences it, such

 (such fetched onely examples, authority books, are

 metaphoricall speeches, tending stirring passion, (because

thirdly, ability counselling proceedeth experience,
 long study; man presumed experience those

 point come different education, one kind study, or

 hath experience particular kind businesse, has

fourthly, able give counsell common-wealth, businesse

 shall think fit. may see, called to

fifthly, supposing number counsellors equall, man better
 counselled hearing apart, assembly; many

 hands, feet, moved sense, the
 eloquence another, feare displeasing spoken,
 whole assembly, contradiction; feare appearing

 one may examine (when need) truth, probability of

 (in every difficult question) man rather astonied, dazled
 variety discourse upon it, informed course he
 take. besides, assembly many, called

 easily avoided. fourthly, deliberations kept secret,
 (whereof many occasions publique businesse,) counsells

 great assemblies necessitated commit affaires lesser

 confidence.
 
conclude, far approves taking counsell
 great assembly counsellours, wisheth for, accept
 pains, question marrying children,
 disposing lands, governing household, managing his
 private estate, especially amongst wish not
 prosperity? man doth businesse help many and
 prudent counsellours, every one consulting apart proper
 element, best, useth able seconds tennis play,
 placed proper stations. next best, useth own
 judgement only; second all. carried
 businesse framed counsell, move
 plurality consenting opinions, execution whereof is
 commonly (out envy, interest) retarded part dissenting,
 worst all, like one carried ball, though
 good players, yet wheele-barrough, frame, heavy it
 self, retarded also inconcurrent judgements, endeavours
 drive it; much more, set
 hands it; all, one, amongst
 them, desire lose. though true, many eys
 see one; yet understood many counsellours;
 only, finall resolution one man. otherwise,
 many eyes see thing divers lines, apt to
 look asquint towards private benefit; desire to
 misse marke, though look two eyes, yet never
 ayme one; therefore great popular common-wealth was

 counsell few; mutuall feare equall factions; and
 open consultations assembly. little

chapter xxvi. civill lawes
 



civill law what
 
civill lawes, understand lawes, men therefore bound to
 observe, members, this, common-wealth
 particular, common-wealth. knowledge particular
 lawes belongeth them, professe study lawes their
 severall countries; knowledge civill law generall, any
 man. antient law rome called civil law, word
 civitas, signifies common-wealth; countries, which
 roman empire, governed law, retaine
 still part thereof think fit, call part civill
 law, distinguish rest civill lawes. that
 intend speak here; designe shew what
 law here, there; law; plato, aristotle, cicero,
 divers others done, without taking upon profession of
 study law.
 
first manifest, law generall, counsell, but
 command; command man man; him, whose
 command addressed one formerly obliged obey him. for
 civill law, addeth name person commanding, is
 persona civitatis, person common-wealth.
 
considered, define civill law manner. "civill law, to
 every subject, rules, common-wealth hath commanded him,
 word, writing, sufficient sign will, make use
 of, distinction right, wrong; say, is
 contrary, contrary rule."
 
definition, nothing first sight
 evident. every man seeth, lawes addressed the
 subjects generall; particular provinces; particular
 vocations; particular men; therefore lawes, every
 command directed; none else. also,
 lawes rules just, unjust; nothing reputed
 unjust, contrary law. likewise, none can
 make lawes common-wealth; subjection the
 common-wealth only: commands, signified sufficient
 signs; man knows otherwise obey them. and
 therefore, whatsoever can definition necessary consequence
 deduced, acknowledged truth. now deduce it
 followeth.
 



soveraign legislator
 
1. legislator common-wealths, soveraign, he
 one man, monarchy, one assembly men, democracy,
 aristocracy. legislator, maketh law. the
 common-wealth only, praescribes, commandeth observation those
 rules, call law: therefore common-wealth legislator.
 common-wealth person, capacity doe thing,
 representative, (that is, soveraign;) therefore the
 soveraign sole legislator. reason, none can abrogate
 law made, soveraign; law abrogated, by
 another law, forbiddeth put execution.
 



subject civill law
 
2. soveraign common-wealth, assembly, one man, is
 subject civill lawes. power make, repeale
 lawes, may pleaseth, free himselfe subjection,
 repealing lawes trouble him, making new; and
 consequently free before. free, can free when
 will: possible person bound himselfe;
 can bind, can release; therefore bound to
 himselfe onely, bound.
 



use, law vertue time, soveraigns consent
 
3. long use obtaineth authority law, the
 length time maketh authority, will soveraign
 signified silence, (for silence sometimes argument of
 consent;) longer law, soveraign shall silent
 therein. therefore soveraign shall question right
 grounded, upon present will, upon lawes formerly
 made; length time shal bring prejudice right; the
 question shal judged equity. many unjust actions, unjust
 sentences, go uncontrolled longer time, man can remember.
 lawyers account customes law, reasonable, and
 evill customes abolished; judgement is
 reasonable, abolished, belongeth maketh
 law, soveraign assembly, monarch.
 



law nature, civill law contain other
 
4. law nature, civill law, contain other, are
 equall extent. lawes nature, consist equity,
 justice, gratitude, morall vertues depending, the
 condition meer nature (as said end 15th
 chapter,) properly lawes, qualities dispose men to
 peace, obedience. common-wealth settled, are
 actually lawes, before; commands the
 common-wealth; therefore also civill lawes: soveraign
 power obliges men obey them. differences private
 men, declare, equity, justice, morall
 vertue, make binding, need ordinances of
 soveraign power, punishments ordained shall break
 them; ordinances therefore part civill law. law of
 nature therefore part civill law common-wealths of
 world. reciprocally also, civill law part dictates
 nature. justice, say, performance covenant, and
 giving every man own, dictate law nature. but
 every subject common-wealth, hath covenanted obey civill
 law, (either one another, assemble make common
 representative, representative selfe one one, when
 subdued sword promise obedience, may receive
 life;) therefore obedience civill law part also the
 law nature. civill, naturall law different kinds, but
 different parts law; whereof one part written, called
 civill, unwritten, naturall. right nature, that
 is, naturall liberty man, may civill law abridged,
 restrained: nay, end making lawes, other, such
 restraint; without possibly peace. law
 brought world nothing else, limit naturall
 liberty particular men, manner, might hurt, but
 assist one another, joyn together common enemy.
 



provinciall lawes made custome, soveraign power
 
5. soveraign one common-wealth, subdue people have
 lived written lawes, afterwards govern the
 lawes, governed before; yet lawes the
 civill lawes victor, vanquished common-wealth, for
 legislator he, whose authority lawes first made,
 whose authority now continue lawes. therefore
 divers provinces, within dominion common-wealth,

 antiently lawes written, otherwise made known, constitutions,
 statutes soveraigns; now lawes, vertue of
 praescription time, constitutions present
 soveraigns. unwritten law, provinces dominion,
 shall generally observed, iniquity appear use thereof;
 law can law nature, equally obliging all
 man-kind.
 



foolish opinions lawyers concerning making lawes
 
6. seeing lawes, written, unwritten, authority,

 common-wealths soveraign assembly; man may wonder from

7. law can never reason, lawyers agreed; and

unwritten lawes lawes nature
 
first, law obliges subjects without

publique registers
 
question injury, crime, upon written law; every

interpretation law dependeth soveraign power
 
legislator known; lawes, either writing, the
 light nature, sufficiently published; wanteth yet another
 materiall circumstance make obligatory. the
 letter, intendment, meaning; say, authentique
 interpretation law (which sense legislator,) in
 nature law consisteth; therefore interpretation

 subject oweth obedience) shall appoint. else, craft an
 interpreter, law made beare sense, contrary of
 soveraign; means interpreter becomes legislator.
 



lawes need interpretation
 
laws, written, unwritten, need interpretation.
 unwritten law nature, though easy such, without
 partiality, passion, make use naturall reason, and
 therefore leaves violators thereof without excuse; yet considering
 few, perhaps none, cases blinded by
 self love, passion, now become laws most
 obscure; consequently greatest need able interpreters.
 written laws, short, easily mis-interpreted, the
 divers significations word, two; long, obscure
 diverse significations many words: much written
 law, delivered few, many words, can well understood, without a
 perfect understanding finall causes, law was
 made; knowledge finall causes legislator. him
 therefore can knot law, insoluble; either by
 finding ends, undoe by; else making ends he
 will, (as alexander sword gordian knot,) the
 legislative power; interpreter can doe.
 



authenticall interpretation law writers
 
interpretation lawes nature, common-wealth, dependeth
 books morall philosophy. authority writers, without

divisions law
 
difference division lawes, made divers
 manners, according different methods, men have
 written them. thing dependeth nature, on
 scope writer; subservient every mans proper method.
 institutions justinian, find seven sorts civill lawes.
 
1. edicts, constitutions, epistles prince, is, of
 emperour; whole power people him. like
 these, proclamations kings england.
 
2. decrees whole people rome (comprehending senate,)
 put question senate. lawes, at

 emperours abrogated, remained lawes by
 authority imperiall. lawes bind, understood be
 lawes authority power repeale them. somewhat like to

3. decrees common people (excluding senate,) they
 put question tribune people. them
 abrogated emperours, remained lawes authority
 imperiall. like these, orders house commons in
 england.
 
4. senatus consulta, orders senate; people
 rome grew numerous, inconvenient assemble them; it
 thought fit emperour, men consult senate in
 stead people: resemblance acts of
 counsell.
 
5. edicts praetors, (in cases) aediles: as
 chiefe justices courts england.
 
6. responsa prudentum; sentences, opinions those
 lawyers, emperour gave authority interpret law, and
 give answer matter law demanded advice;
 answers, judges giving judgement obliged the
 constitutions emperour observe; like reports
 cases judged, judges law england bound to
 observe them. judges common law england, not
 properly judges, juris consulti; judges, either
 lords, twelve men country, point law ask
 advice.
 
7. also, unwritten customes, (which nature imitation
 law,) tacite consent emperour, case not
 contrary law nature, lawes.
 
another division lawes, naturall positive. naturall are
 lawes eternity; called onely
 naturall, also morall lawes; consisting morall vertues, as

 chapters.
 
positive, eternity; been

another division law
 
again, positive lawes humane, divine; humane
 positive lawes, distributive, penal. distributive are
 determine rights subjects, declaring every man
 is, acquireth holdeth propriety lands,
 goods, right liberty action; speak all
 subjects. penal those, declare, penalty shall be
 inflicted violate law; speak ministers
 officers ordained execution. though every one be
 informed punishments ordained beforehand transgression;
 neverthelesse command addressed delinquent, (who
 supposed will faithfully punish himselfe,) publique
 ministers appointed see penalty executed. penal lawes
 part written together lawes distributive; and
 sometimes called judgements. lawes generall judgements,
 sentences legislator; also every particular judgement, a
 law him, whose case judged.
 



divine positive law made known law
 
divine positive lawes (for naturall lawes eternall, and
 universall, divine,) those, commandements of
 god, (not eternity, universally addressed men, but
 onely certain people, certain persons,) declared for
 such, god hath authorised declare them. this
 authority man declare positive lawes god, can
 known? god may command man supernaturall way, deliver
 lawes men. essence law, who
 obliged, assured authority declareth
 it, naturally take notice god, can man
 without supernaturall revelation assured revelation received
 declarer? can bound obey them? first
 question, man can assured revelation another, without
 revelation particularly himselfe, evidently impossible:
 though man may induced believe revelation, the
 miracles see doe, seeing extraordinary sanctity of
 life, seeing extraordinary wisedome, extraordinary
 felicity actions, marks gods extraordinary
 favour; yet assured evidence speciall revelation.
 miracles marvellous workes: marvellous one,
 may another. sanctity may feigned; visible
 felicities world, often work god naturall,
 ordinary causes. therefore man can infallibly know by
 naturall reason, another supernaturall revelation gods
 will; beliefe; every one (as signs thereof shall appear
 greater, lesser) firmer, weaker belief.
 
second, can bound obey them; hard.
 law declared, law nature (which is
 undoubtedly gods law) undertake obey it, bound his
 act; bound say obey it, bound believe it: mens
 beliefe, interiour cogitations, subject commands,
 operation god, ordinary, extraordinary. faith of
 supernaturall law, fulfilling, assenting the
 same; duty exhibite god, gift god
 freely giveth pleaseth; also unbelief breach
 lawes; rejection all, except lawes
 naturall. say, will made yet cleerer, the
 examples, testimonies concerning point holy scripture. the
 covenant god made abraham (in supernaturall manner) thus,
 (gen. 17. 10) "this covenant thou shalt observe between
 thee thy seed thee." abrahams seed this
 revelation, yet being; yet party covenant,
 bound obey abraham declare gods law;
 be, vertue obedience owed to
 parents; (if subject earthly power, as
 case abraham) soveraign power children,
 servants. againe, god saith abraham, "in thee shall all
 nations earth blessed: know thou wilt command thy
 children, thy house thee keep way lord, to
 observe righteousnesse judgement," manifest, obedience of
 family, revelation, depended former obligation
 obey soveraign. mount sinai moses went god; the
 people forbidden approach paine death; yet bound
 obey moses declared gods law. upon ground,
 submission own, "speak thou us, will
 heare thee; let god speak us, lest dye?" two
 places sufficiently appeareth, common-wealth, subject
 certain assured revelation particularly himself
 concerning will god, obey such, command of
 common-wealth: men liberty, take gods
 commandements, dreams, fancies, dreams and
 fancies private men; scarce two men agree upon gods

 nature,) subjects bound obey divine law, is
 declared so, lawes common-wealth. also is
 evident mans reason; whatsoever law of

 tis propounded name god. besides, place in

 declared common-wealth. christian states punish
 revolt christian religion, states, those
 set religion forbidden. whatsoever not

another division lawes

fundamentall law every common-wealth that, taken

 whose foundation destroyed. therefore fundamentall law that,

difference law right
 
find words lex civilis, jus civile, say, law and
 right civil, promiscuously used thing, even most

 nature gave us. nature gave right every man secure himselfe

chapter xxvii. crimes, excuses, extenuations
 


sinne what
 
sinne, onely transgression law, also contempt of
 legislator. contempt, breach lawes once.
 therefore may consist, onely commission fact, in
 speaking words lawes forbidden, omission of
 law commandeth, also intention, purpose to
 transgresse. purpose breake law, degree of
 contempt him, belongeth see executed. be
 delighted imagination onely, possessed another mans
 goods, servants, wife, without intention take him
 force, fraud, breach law, sayth, "thou shalt not
 covet:" pleasure man imagining, dreaming of
 death him, whose life expecteth nothing dammage, and
 displeasure, sinne; resolving put act execution,
 tendeth thereto. pleased fiction that, which
 please man reall, passion adhaerent the
 nature man, every living creature, make a
 sinne, make sinne man. consideration this,
 made think severe, themselves, others, that
 maintain, first motions mind, (though checked the
 fear god) sinnes. confesse safer erre hand,
 other.
 



crime what
 
crime, sinne, consisting committing (by deed, word)
 law forbiddeth, omission hath
 commanded. every crime sinne; every sinne crime.
 intend steale, kill, sinne, though never appeare in
 word, fact: god seeth thoughts man, can lay to
 charge: till appear thing done, said, which
 intention may crime; distinction greeks observed in
 word amartema, egklema, aitia; wherof former, (which is
 translated sinne,) signifieth swarving law whatsoever; but
 two later, (which translated crime,) signifie sinne onely,
 whereof one man may accuse another. intentions, never
 appear outward act, place humane accusation. in
 like manner latines peccatum, sinne, signifie manner
 deviation law; crimen, (which word derive from
 cerno, signifies perceive,) mean onely sinnes, my
 made appear judge; therfore meer intentions.
 



civill law is, crime
 
relation sinne law, crime civill
 law, may inferred, first, law ceaseth, sinne ceaseth.
 law nature eternall, violation covenants,
 ingratitude, arrogance, facts contrary morall vertue, can
 never cease sinne. secondly, civill law ceasing, crimes
 cease: law remaining, nature, there
 place accusation; every man judge, accused
 onely conscience, cleared uprightnesse own
 intention. therefore intention right, fact sinne:
 otherwise, fact sinne; crime. thirdly, the
 soveraign power ceaseth, crime also ceaseth: such
 power, protection law; therefore
 every one may protect power: man the
 institution soveraign power can supposed give away right
 preserving body; safety whereof soveraignty was
 ordained. understood onely those, not
 contributed taking away power protected
 them: crime beginning.
 



ignorance law nature excuseth man
 
source every crime, defect understanding; some
 errour reasoning, sudden force passions. defect in
 understanding, ignorance; reasoning, erroneous opinion. again,
 ignorance three sort; law, soveraign, the
 penalty. ignorance law nature excuseth man; every
 man hath attained use reason, supposed know, he
 another, done himselfe.
 therefore place soever man shall come, thing
 contrary law, crime. man come indies
 hither, perswade men receive new religion, teach them
 thing tendeth disobedience lawes country,
 though never well perswaded truth teacheth,
 commits crime, may justly punished same, onely
 doctrine false, also he
 approve another, namely, comming hence, should
 endeavour alter religion there. ignorance civill law,
 shall excuse man strange country, till declared him;
 because, till civill law binding.
 



ignorance civill law excuseth sometimes
 
like manner, civill law mans country, not
 sufficiently declared, may know will; action
 law nature; ignorance good excuse: other
 cases ignorance civill law, excuseth not.
 



ignorance soveraign excuseth not
 
ignorance soveraign power, place mans ordinary
 residence, excuseth not; take notice the
 power, hath protected there.
 



ignorance penalty excuseth not
 
ignorance penalty, law declared, excuseth man:
 breaking law, without fear penalty follow, were
 law, vain words, undergoeth penalty, though know not
 is; because, whosoever voluntarily doth action, accepteth
 known consequences it; punishment known consequence
 violation lawes, every common-wealth; punishment,
 determined already law, subject that; not,
 subject arbitrary punishment. reason, he
 injury, without limitation will,
 suffer punishment without limitation, will
 whose law thereby violated.
 



punishments declared fact, excuse greater punishments
 it
 
penalty, either annexed crime law selfe,
 hath usually inflicted like cases; delinquent

 men compare benefit injustice, harm

 law formerly determined, others punished

nothing can made crime law made fact
 
law, made fact done, can make crime: the

 fact done; yet doth fact, lyable the
 penalty ordained after, case lesser penalty made known
 before, neither writing, example, reason immediatly

false principles right wrong causes crime
 
defect reasoning, (that say, errour,) men prone
 violate lawes, three wayes. first, presumption false
 principles; men observed places, and
 ages, unjust actions authorised, force, and
 victories committed them; potent men,
 breaking cob-web lawes country, weaker sort,
 failed enterprises, esteemed the
 onely criminals; thereupon taken principles, grounds of
 reasoning, "that justice vain word: whatsoever man
 can get industry, hazard, own: practice
 nations unjust: examples former times good
 arguments like again;" many kind: which
 granted, act selfe can crime, must made so
 (not law, but) successe commit it; the
 fact vertuous, vicious, fortune pleaseth; what
 marius makes crime, sylla shall make meritorious, caesar (the same
 lawes standing) turn crime, perpetuall disturbance
 peace common-wealth.
 



false teachers mis-interpreting law nature secondly, false
 teachers, either mis-interpret law nature, making thereby
 repugnant law civill; teaching lawes, doctrines of
 own, traditions former times, inconsistent the
 duty subject.
 



false inferences true principles, teachers
 
thirdly, erroneous inferences true principles; happens
 commonly men hasty, praecipitate concluding, and
 resolving do; they, great opinion
 understanding, believe things nature
 require time study, onely common experience, good
 naturall wit; whereof man thinks himselfe unprovided: whereas the
 knowledge, right wrong, lesse difficult, no

 reasoning, none can excuse (though may

passions;
 
passions frequently causes crime, one,
 vain-glory, foolish over-rating worth; if

 naturall quality, depending will that
 soveraign authority. whence proceedeth presumption that
 punishments ordained lawes, extended generally all

presumption riches
 
therefore happeneth commonly, value the

friends
 
multitude potent kindred; popular men, that

wisedome
 
great, false opinion wisedome,
 take upon reprehend actions, call question the

 eyes.
 
generally vain-glorious men, (unlesse withall timorous,)
 subject anger; prone others interpret for

hatred, lust, ambition, covetousnesse, causes crime
 
passions, hate, lust, ambition, covetousnesse, what
 crimes apt produce, obvious every mans experience
 understanding, needeth nothing said them, saving

 living creatures, effects hindred,
 extraordinary use reason, constant severity punishing

 unavoydable molestation; whereby either mans patience must be

 molesteth him; former difficult; later many times
 impossible, without violation law. ambition, and
 covetousnesse passions also perpetually incumbent, and
 pressing; whereas reason perpetually present, resist them:
 therefore whensoever hope impunity appears, effects
 proceed. lust, wants lasting, hath the
 vehemence, sufficeth weigh apprehension easie,
 uncertain punishments.
 



fear sometimes cause crime, danger neither present,
 corporeall
 
passions, enclineth men least break lawes, is

 feare.
 
every fear justifies action produceth, fear onely

crimes equall
 
different sources crimes, appeares already, all
 crimes (as stoicks old time maintained) same
 allay. place, excuse, seemed
 crime, proved none all; also extenuation, which

totall excuses
 
totally excuseth fact, takes away nature of
 crime, can none that, time, taketh away the
 obligation law. fact committed law,
 committed obliged law, can a
 crime.
 
want means know law, totally excuseth: law whereof
 man means enforme himself, obligatory. want

 known reason pretends to: children, and

man captive, power enemy, (and in
 power enemy, person, means living, is
 so,) without fault, obligation law ceaseth;
 must obey enemy, dye; consequently obedience
 crime: man obliged (when protection law
 faileth,) protect himself, best means can.
 
man terrour present death, compelled doe fact
 law, totally excused; law can oblige a
 man abandon preservation. supposing law were
 obligatory; yet man reason thus, "if doe not, die
 presently; doe it, die afterwards; therefore it, there
 time life gained;" nature therefore compells fact.
 
man destitute food, thing necessary life,
 preserve himselfe way, fact against
 law; great famine take food force, stealth,
 obtaine mony charity; defence life,
 snatch away another mans sword, totally excused, reason
 next alledged.
 



excuses author
 
again, facts done law, authority another, are
 authority excused author; man to
 accuse fact another, instrument: it

 hence followeth man, assembly, hath the
 soveraign power, commandeth man contrary a

 besides, soveraign commandeth thing done against

man, assembly, hath soveraign power, disclaime

 erected consent, defence;
 liberty inconsistent it, granted through

degrees crime taken divers scales, measured, first, by
 malignity source, cause: secondly, contagion the
 example: thirdly, mischiefe effect; fourthly, the

fact done law, proceed presumption of

 crime proceeding false perswasion lawfull: that
 committeth conscience, presumeth force, or
 power, encourages commit again: that
 doth errour, errour shewn him, conformable the
 law.
 



evill teachers, extenuate
 
hee, whose errour proceeds authority teacher, an
 interpreter law publiquely authorised, faulty, he
 whose errour proceedeth peremptory pursute principles,
 reasoning: taught one teacheth publique
 authority, common-wealth teacheth, hath resemblance law,
 till authority controuleth it; crimes contain
 denyall soveraign power, evident
 law, excuseth totally: whereas groundeth actions, his
 private judgement, according rectitude, errour thereof,
 stand, fall.
 



examples impunity, extenuate
 
fact, constantly punished men, as
 greater crime, may precedent examples of
 impunity. examples, many hopes impunity given by
 soveraign himselfe: furnishes man such
 hope, presumption mercy, encourageth offend, hath his
 part offence; reasonably charge offender the
 whole.
 



praemeditation, aggravateth
 
crime arising sudden passion, great, same
 ariseth long meditation: former case place
 extenuation, common infirmity humane nature: that
 doth praemeditation, used circumspection, cast eye,
 law, punishment, consequence thereof humane
 society; committing crime, hee hath contemned, and
 postposed appetite. suddennesse passion
 sufficient totall excuse: time first
 knowing law, commission fact, shall taken for
 time deliberation; meditation law, to
 rectifie irregularity passions.
 
law publiquely, assiduity, people
 read, interpreted; fact done it, greater crime,
 men left without instruction, enquire with
 difficulty, uncertainty, interruption callings, and
 informed private men: case, part fault is
 discharged upon common infirmity; former apparent
 negligence, without contempt soveraign power.
 



tacite approbation soveraign, extenuates
 
facts law expresly condemneth, law-maker by
 manifest signes will tacitly approveth, lesse crimes,
 facts, condemned law, lawmaker. for
 seeing will law-maker law, appear case two
 contradictory lawes; totally excuse, men bound to
 take notice soveraigns approbation, arguments, are
 expressed command. punishments consequent,
 onely transgression law, also observing
 it, part cause transgression, therefore cannot
 reasonably impute whole crime delinquent. example, the
 law condemneth duells; punishment made capitall: contrary
 part, refuseth duell, subject contempt scorne, without
 remedy; sometimes soveraign himselfe thought unworthy to
 charge, preferment warre: thereupon accept duell,
 considering men lawfully endeavour obtain good opinion
 soveraign power, reason be
 rigorously punished; seeing part fault may discharged the
 punisher; say, wishing liberty private revenges,
 kind disobedience; care governours, not
 countenance thing obliquely, directly forbid. the
 examples princes, see them, are, ever been,
 potent govern actions, lawes themselves. and
 though duty do, do, say; yet
 will duty never performed, till please god give men an
 extraordinary, supernaturall grace follow precept.
 



comparison crimes effects
 
again, compare crimes mischiefe effects, first,
 fact, redounds dammage many, greater, than
 redounds hurt few. therefore, fact hurteth,
 onely present, also, (by example) future, a
 greater crime, hurt onely present: former,
 fertile crime, multiplyes hurt many; later is
 barren. maintain doctrines contrary religion established in
 common-wealth, greater fault, authorised preacher, than
 private person: also it, live prophanely, incontinently,
 irreligious act whatsoever. likewise professor the
 law, maintain point, act, tendeth weakning
 soveraign power, greater crime, another man: also in
 man hath reputation wisedome, counsells are
 followed, actions imitated many, fact law, is
 greater crime, fact another: men onely
 commit crime, teach law men. generally all
 crimes greater, scandall give; say, by
 becoming stumbling-blocks weak, look much upon the
 way go in, upon light men carry them.
 



laesae majestas
 
also facts hostility present state common-wealth,
 greater crimes, acts done private men; for
 dammage extends selfe all: betraying the
 strengths, revealing secrets common-wealth enemy;
 also attempts upon representative common-wealth, a
 monarch, assembly; endeavours word, deed diminish
 authority same, either present time, succession:
 crimes latines understand crimina laesae majestatis, and
 consist designe, act, contrary fundamentall law.
 



bribery false testimony
 
likewise crimes, render judgements effect, greater
 crimes, injuries done one, persons; receive
 mony give false judgement, testimony, greater crime, than
 otherwise deceive man like, greater summe; not
 onely wrong, falls judgements; judgements
 rendered uselesse, occasion ministred force, private
 revenges.
 



depeculation
 
also robbery, depeculation publique treasure, revenues,
 greater crime, robbing, defrauding private man;
 robbe publique, robbe many once.
 



counterfeiting authority
 
also counterfeit usurpation publique ministery, the
 counterfeiting publique seales, publique coine, than
 counterfeiting private mans person, seale; fraud
 thereof, extendeth dammage many.
 



crimes private men compared
 
facts law, done private men, greater crime, is
 that, dammage common opinion men, sensible.
 therefore
 
kill law, greater crime, injury, life
 preserved.

 goods.

woman married, woman married.
 
things commonly valued; though men more,

 particular, generall inclination mankind.
 
therefore offence men take, contumely, words, or

 reproached, hath neglected lawes greeks,

also crime private man, much aggravated person,

 (though surrendred power civill law,) had

many cases aggravation, extenuation might added: by

publique crimes what
 
lastly, almost crimes injury done, onely
 private man, also common-wealth; crime, when
 accusation name common-wealth, called publique
 crime; name private man, private crime; the

 crown; private pleas. accusation murder, accuser

chapter xxviii. punishments, rewards
 



definition punishment
 
"a punishment, evill inflicted publique authority, that
 hath done, omitted judged authority be
 transgression law; end will men may thereby
 better disposed obedience."
 



right punish whence derived
 
inferre thing definition, question to
 answered, much importance; is, door right, or
 authority punishing case, came in. has
 said before, man supposed bound covenant, resist
 violence; consequently intended, gave right
 another lay violent hands upon person. making a
 common-wealth, every man giveth away right defending another; but
 defending himselfe. also obligeth himselfe, assist that
 hath soveraignty, punishing another; himselfe
 not. covenant assist soveraign, hurt another,
 unlesse covenanteth right doe himselfe, not
 give right punish. manifest therefore right
 common-wealth (that is, he, represent it) hath to
 punish, grounded concession, gift subjects.
 also shewed formerly, institution of
 common-wealth, every man right every thing, do
 whatsoever thought necessary preservation; subduing,
 hurting, killing man order thereunto. the
 foundation right punishing, exercised every
 common-wealth. subjects give soveraign right;
 onely laying theirs, strengthned use own, he
 think fit, preservation all: not
 given, left him, onely; (excepting limits set
 naturall law) entire, condition meer nature, and
 warre every one neighbour.
 



private injuries, revenges punishments
 
definition punishment, inferre, first, neither
 private revenges, injuries private men, can properly stiled
 punishment; proceed publique authority.
 



denyall preferment
 
secondly, neglected, unpreferred publique
 favour, punishment; new evill thereby man
 inflicted; onely left estate before.
 



pain inflicted without publique hearing
 
thirdly, evill inflicted publique authority, without
 precedent publique condemnation, stiled name of
 punishment; hostile act; fact man
 punished, first judged publique authority, a
 transgression law.
 



pain inflicted usurped power
 
fourthly, evill inflicted usurped power, judges
 without authority soveraign, punishment; act of
 hostility; acts power usurped, author, the
 person condemned; therefore acts publique authority.
 



pain inflicted without respect future good
 
fifthly, evill inflicted without intention, or
 possibility disposing delinquent, (by example) men,
 obey lawes, punishment; act hostility; because
 without end, hurt done contained name.
 



naturall evill consequences, punishments
 
sixthly, whereas certain actions, annexed nature, divers
 hurtfull consequences; man assaulting another, himselfe
 slain, wounded; falleth sicknesse of
 unlawfull act; hurt, though respect god, the
 author nature, may said inflicted, therefore a
 punishment divine; yet contaned name punishment in
 respect men, inflicted authority man.
 



hurt inflicted, lesse benefit transgressing, not
 punishment
 
seventhly, harm inflicted lesse benefit, or
 contentment naturally followeth crime committed, harm is
 within definition; rather price, redemption, than
 punishment crime: nature punishment, to
 end, disposing men obey law; end (if it
 lesse benefit transgression) attaineth not, but
 worketh contrary effect.
 



punishment annexed law, greater hurt not
 punishment, hostility
 
eighthly, punishment determined prescribed law it
 selfe, crime committed, greater punishment
 inflicted, excesse punishment, act hostility. for
 seeing aym punishment revenge, terrour; the
 terrour great punishment unknown, taken away declaration
 lesse, unexpected addition part punishment.
 punishment determined law, there
 whatsoever inflicted, hath nature punishment. that
 goes violation law, wherein penalty determined,
 expecteth indeterminate, say, arbitrary punishment.
 



hurt inflicted fact done law, punishment
 
ninthly, harme inflicted fact done law that
 forbad it, punishment, act hostility: the
 law, transgression law: punishment supposeth a
 fact judged, transgression law; therefore
 harme inflicted law made, punishment, act of
 hostility.
 



representative common-wealth unpunishable
 
tenthly, hurt inflicted representative common-wealth, is
 punishment, act hostility: nature
 punishment, inflicted publique authority, the
 authority representative self.
 



hurt revolted subjects done right war, way of
 punishment
 
lastly, harme inflicted upon one declared enemy, fals not
 name punishment: seeing either never
 subject law, therefore transgresse it; been
 subject it, professing longer so, consequence deny
 can transgresse it, harmes can done them, must be
 taken acts hostility. declared hostility, infliction of
 evill lawfull. whence followeth, subject shall
 fact, word, wittingly, deliberatly deny authority of
 representative common-wealth, (whatsoever penalty hath
 formerly ordained treason,) may lawfully made suffer
 whatsoever representative will: denying subjection, denyes
 punishment law hath ordained; therefore suffers
 enemy common-wealth; is, according will of
 representative. punishments set law, to
 subjects, enemies; they, their
 act subjects, deliberately revolting, deny soveraign power.
 
first, generall distribution punishments, into
 divine, humane. former shall occasion, speak, a
 convenient place hereafter.
 
humane, punishments inflicted commandement
 man; either corporall, pecuniary, ignominy, or
 imprisonment, exile, mixt these.
 



punishments corporall
 
corporall punishment that, inflicted body directly,
 according intention inflicteth it: are
 stripes, wounds, deprivation pleasures body, as
 lawfully enjoyed.
 



capitall
 
these, capitall, lesse capitall. capitall, is
 infliction death; either simply, torment. lesse
 capitall, stripes, wounds, chains, corporall
 paine, nature mortall. upon infliction of
 punishment death follow intention inflicter, the
 punishment bee esteemed capitall, though harme prove
 mortall accident foreseen; case death not
 inflicted, hastened.
 
pecuniary punishment, consisteth the
 deprivation summe mony, also lands, goods
 usually bought sold mony. case law, that
 ordaineth punishment, made design gather mony, from
 shall transgresse same, properly punishment,
 price priviledge, exemption law, doth not
 absolutely forbid fact, able pay
 mony: except law naturall, part religion; in
 case exemption law, transgression of
 it. law exacteth pecuniary mulct, take the
 name god vaine, payment mulct, price a
 dispensation sweare, punishment transgression law
 undispensable. like manner law impose summe mony be
 payd, injured; satisfaction the
 hurt done him; extinguisheth accusation party injured,
 crime offender.
 



ignominy
 
ignominy, infliction evill, made dishonorable;
 deprivation good, made honourable the
 common-wealth. things honorable nature; the
 effects courage, magnanimity, strength, wisdome, abilities
 body mind: others made honorable common-wealth; badges,
 titles, offices, singular marke soveraigns favour.
 former, (though may faile nature, accident,) be
 taken away law; therefore losse punishment.
 later, may taken away publique authority made
 honorable, properly punishments: degrading men
 condemned, badges, titles, offices; declaring them
 uncapable like time come.
 



imprisonment
 
imprisonment, man publique authority deprived of
 liberty; may happen two divers ends; whereof one safe
 custody man accused; inflicting paine man
 condemned. former punishment; man supposed
 punisht, judicially heard, declared guilty.
 therefore whatsoever hurt man made suffer bonds, or
 restraint, cause heard, is
 necessary assure custody, law nature. the
 later punishment, evill, inflicted publique authority,
 somewhat authority judged transgression
 law. word imprisonment, comprehend restraint of
 motion, caused externall obstacle, house, called
 generall name prison; iland, men said to
 confined it; place men set worke, old time
 men condemned quarries, times gallies; or
 chaine, impediment.
 



exile
 
exile, (banishment) man crime, condemned depart
 dominion common-wealth, certaine part
 thereof; prefixed time, ever, return it:
 seemeth nature, without circumstances, be
 punishment; rather escape, publique commandement to
 avoid punishment flight. cicero sayes, never such
 punishment ordained city rome; cals refuge men in
 danger. man banished, neverthelesse permitted enjoy
 goods, revenue lands, meer change ayr no
 punishment; tend benefit common-wealth, for
 punishments ordained, (that say, forming of
 mens wils observation law;) many times dammage
 common-wealth. banished man, lawfull enemy the
 common-wealth banished him; member the
 same. withall deprived lands, goods, then
 punishment lyeth exile, reckoned amongst
 punishments pecuniary.
 



punishment innocent subjects contrary law nature
 
punishments innocent subjects, great little, are
 law nature; punishment transgression of
 law, therefore can punishment innocent. it
 therefore violation, first, law nature, forbiddeth
 men, revenges, look thing future good:
 can arrive good common-wealth, punishing the
 innocent. secondly, that, forbiddeth ingratitude: seeing
 soveraign power, originally given consent every one of
 subjects, end long obedient, be
 protected thereby; punishment innocent, rendring of
 evill good. thirdly, law commandeth equity; that
 say, equall distribution justice; punishing the
 innocent observed.
 



harme done innocents war, so
 
infliction evill soever, innocent man, not
 subject, benefit common-wealth, without
 violation former covenant, breach law nature.
 men subjects, either enemies, else have
 ceased so, precedent covenants. enemies,
 common-wealth judgeth capable hurt, lawfull by
 originall right nature make warre; wherein sword judgeth
 not, doth victor make distinction nocent innocent, to
 time past; respect mercy, conduceth to
 good people. upon ground is, also
 subjects, deliberatly deny authority common-wealth
 established, vengeance lawfully extended, onely the
 fathers, also third fourth generation yet being,
 consequently innocent fact, afflicted:
 nature offence, consisteth renouncing of
 subjection; relapse condition warre, commonly
 called rebellion; offend, suffer subjects, but
 enemies. rebellion, warre renewed.
 



reward, either salary, grace
 
reward, either gift, contract. contract, is
 called salary, wages; benefit due service performed, or
 promised. gift, benefit proceeding grace them
 bestow it, encourage, enable men service. and
 therefore soveraign common-wealth appointeth salary
 publique office, receiveth it, bound justice
 performe office; otherwise, bound onely honour, to
 acknowledgement, endeavour requitall. though men no
 lawfull remedy, commanded quit private businesse,
 serve publique, without reward, salary; yet not
 bound thereto, law nature, institution the
 common-wealth, unlesse service otherwise done; it
 supposed soveraign may make use means, insomuch as
 common souldier, may demand wages warrefare, a
 debt.
 



benefits bestowed fear, rewards
 
benefits soveraign bestoweth subject, fear some
 power, ability hath hurt common-wealth, not
 properly rewards; salaryes; this
 case contract supposed, every man obliged already the
 common-wealth disservice: graces; extorted
 feare, incident soveraign power: but
 rather sacrifices, soveraign (considered naturall
 person, person common-wealth) makes, the
 appeasing discontent thinks potent himselfe; and
 encourage obedience, contrary, continuance, and
 increasing extortion.
 



salaries certain casuall
 
whereas salaries certain, proceed publique
 treasure; others uncertain, casuall, proceeding the
 execution office salary ordained; later
 cases hurtfull common-wealth; case of
 judicature. benefit judges, ministers a
 court justice, ariseth multitude causes brought
 cognisance, must needs follow two inconveniences: one,
 nourishing sutes; sutes, greater benefit: and
 another depends that, contention jurisdiction;
 court drawing selfe, many causes can. in
 offices execution inconveniences; their
 employment encreased endeavour own. thus
 much shall suffice nature punishment, reward; are,
 were, nerves tendons, move limbes joynts a
 common-wealth.
 
hitherto set forth nature man, (whose pride other
 passions compelled submit himselfe government;) together
 great power governour, compared leviathan,
 taking comparison two last verses one and
 fortieth job; god set forth great power of
 leviathan, called king proud. "there nothing," saith he,
 "on earth, compared him. made afraid. hee
 seeth every high thing him; king children of
 pride." mortall, subject decay, other
 earthly creatures are; heaven, (though not
 earth) stand fear of, whose lawes to
 obey; shall next following chapters speak diseases, and
 causes mortality; lawes nature bound to
 obey.
 


chapter xxix. things weaken, tend dissolution of
 common-wealth
 

dissolution common-wealths proceedeth imperfect institution
 
though nothing can immortall, mortals make; yet, men the
 use reason pretend to, common-wealths might secured, at
 least, perishing internall diseases. nature their
 institution, designed live, long man-kind, as
 lawes nature, justice selfe, gives life.
 therefore come dissolved, externall violence, but
 intestine disorder, fault men, matter; but
 makers, orderers them. men, become
 last weary irregular justling, hewing one another, desire
 hearts, conforme one firme lasting
 edifice; want, art making fit laws, square
 actions by, also humility, patience, suffer rude
 combersome points present greatnesse taken off, they
 without help able architect, compiled, any
 crasie building, hardly lasting time,
 must assuredly fall upon heads posterity.
 
amongst infirmities therefore common-wealth, will reckon in
 first place, arise imperfect institution,
 resemble diseases naturall body, proceed a
 defectuous procreation.
 



want absolute power
 
which, one, "that man obtain kingdome, sometimes
 content lesse power, peace, defence the
 common-wealth necessarily required." whence commeth passe,
 exercise power layd by, publique safety
 resumed, hath resemblance unjust act; disposeth
 great numbers men (when occasion presented) rebell; the
 manner bodies children, gotten diseased parents, are
 subject either untimely death, purge ill quality, derived
 vicious conception, breaking biles scabbs.
 kings deny necessary power, not
 alwayes (though sometimes) ignorance necessary the
 office undertake; many times hope recover same
 pleasure: wherein reason well; as
 will hold promises, shall maintained by
 forraign common-wealths; order good subjects
 let slip occasions weaken estate neighbours. was
 thomas beckett archbishop canterbury, supported henry
 second, pope; subjection ecclesiastiques the
 common-wealth, dispensed william conqueror at
 reception, took oath, infringe liberty the
 church. barons, whose power william rufus (to
 help transferring succession elder brother,
 himselfe,) encreased degree, inconsistent soveraign
 power, maintained rebellion king john, french.
 happen monarchy onely. whereas stile the
 antient roman common-wealth, was, senate, people rome;
 neither senate, people pretended whole power; first
 caused seditions, tiberius gracchus, caius gracchus, lucius
 saturnius, others; afterwards warres senate and
 people, marius sylla; pompey caesar,
 extinction democraty, setting monarchy.
 
people athens bound one onely action; which
 was, man pain death propound renewing the
 warre island salamis; yet thereby, solon not
 caused given mad, afterwards gesture habit
 mad-man, verse, propounded people flocked
 him, enemy perpetually readinesse, even the
 gates citie; dammage, shifts, common-wealths
 forced to, power never little limited.
 



private judgement good evill
 
second place, observe diseases common-wealth, that
 proceed poyson seditious doctrines; whereof one is, "that
 every private man judge good evill actions." true in
 condition meer nature, civill lawes; also
 civill government, cases determined the
 law. otherwise, manifest, measure good evill
 actions, civill law; judge legislator, alwayes
 representative common-wealth. false doctrine, men are
 disposed debate themselves, dispute commands the
 common-wealth; afterwards obey, disobey them, their
 private judgements shall think fit. whereby common-wealth is
 distracted weakened.
 



erroneous conscience
 
another doctrine repugnant civill society, is, "whatsoever a
 man conscience, sinne;" dependeth the
 presumption making judge good evill. mans
 conscience, judgement thing; judgement,
 also conscience may erroneous. therefore, though is
 subject civill law, sinneth conscience,
 rule follow reason; yet is
 lives common-wealth; law the
 publique conscience, hath already undertaken guided.
 otherwise diversity, private consciences, which
 private opinions, common-wealth must needs distracted,
 man dare obey soveraign power, farther shall seem
 good eyes.
 



pretence inspiration
 
hath also commonly taught, "that faith sanctity, to
 attained study reason, supernaturall inspiration, or
 infusion," granted, see man render reason
 faith; every christian also prophet; or
 man take law country, rather own
 inspiration, rule action. thus wee fall into
 fault taking upon us judge good evill; make
 judges it, private men pretend supernaturally inspired,
 dissolution civill government. faith comes hearing,
 hearing accidents, guide us presence them
 speak us; accidents contrived god almighty; and
 yet supernaturall, onely, great number that
 concurre every effect, unobservable. faith, sanctity, indeed
 frequent; yet miracles, brought passe
 education, discipline, correction, naturall wayes, which
 god worketh elect, time thinketh fit. and
 three opinions, pernicious peace government, this
 part world, proceeded chiefly tongues, pens of
 unlearned divines; joyning words holy scripture together,
 otherwise agreeable reason, can, make men
 think, sanctity naturall reason, stand together.
 



subjecting soveraign power civill lawes
 
fourth opinion, repugnant nature common-wealth, this,
 "that hath soveraign power, subject civill lawes."
 true, soveraigns subjects lawes nature;
 lawes divine, man, common-wealth
 abrogated. lawes soveraign himselfe, is,
 common-wealth maketh, subject. subject to
 lawes, subject common-wealth, soveraign
 representative, himselfe; subjection, but
 freedome lawes. errour, setteth lawes
 soveraign, setteth also judge him, power to
 punish him; make new soveraign; same
 reason third, punish second; continually without end, to
 confusion, dissolution common-wealth.
 



attributing absolute propriety subjects
 
fifth doctrine, tendeth dissolution common-wealth,
 is, "that every private man absolute propriety goods;
 such, excludeth right soveraign." every man indeed a
 propriety excludes right every subject: it
 onely soveraign power; without protection whereof, every
 man equall right same. right the
 soveraign also excluded, performe office put
 into; is, defend forraign enemies, and
 injuries one another; consequently longer a
 common-wealth.
 
propriety subjects, exclude right the
 soveraign representative goods; much lesse offices
 judicature, execution, represent soveraign
 himselfe.
 



dividing soveraign power
 
sixth doctrine, plainly, directly essence
 common-wealth; ’tis this, "that soveraign power may be
 divided." divide power common-wealth, but
 dissolve it; powers divided mutually destroy other. for
 doctrines, men chiefly beholding those, making
 profession lawes, endeavour make depend upon own
 learning, upon legislative power.
 



imitation neighbour nations
 
false doctrine, also often-times example different
 government neighbouring nation, disposeth men alteration of
 forme already setled. people jewes stirred to
 reject god, call upon prophet samuel, king after
 manner nations; also lesser cities greece, were
 continually disturbed, seditions aristocraticall, and
 democraticall factions; one part almost every common-wealth, desiring
 imitate lacedaemonians; other, athenians. doubt
 not, many men, contented see late troubles in
 england, imitation low countries; supposing there
 needed grow rich, change, done, forme
 government. constitution mans nature, selfe
 subject desire novelty: therefore provoked same,
 neighbourhood also enriched it, is
 almost impossible them, content solicite
 change; love first beginnings, though grieved
 continuance disorder; like hot blouds, gotten
 itch, tear nayles, till can endure
 smart longer.
 



imitation greeks, romans
 
rebellion particular monarchy; one most
 frequent causes it, reading books policy, and
 histories antient greeks, romans; which, young men,
 others unprovided antidote solid reason,
 receiving strong, delightfull impression, great exploits
 warre, atchieved conductors armies, receive withall
 pleasing idea, done besides; imagine great
 prosperity, proceeded aemulation particular men,
 vertue popular form government: considering
 frequent seditions, civill warres, produced imperfection
 policy. reading, say, books, men have
 undertaken kill kings, greek latine writers,
 books, discourses policy, make lawfull, laudable,
 man do; provided it, call tyrant. for
 say regicide, is, killing king, tyrannicide, that
 is, killing tyrant lawfull. books, live
 monarch conceive opinion, subjects popular
 common-wealth enjoy liberty; monarchy slaves.
 say, live monarchy conceive opinion; not
 live popular government; find matter.
 summe, imagine, anything can prejudiciall a
 monarchy, allowing books publikely read, without
 present applying correctives discreet masters, fit to
 take away venime; venime will doubt compare to
 biting mad dogge, disease physicians call
 hydrophobia, fear water. bitten, a
 continuall torment thirst, yet abhorreth water; such
 estate, poyson endeavoured convert dogge:
 monarchy bitten quick, democraticall
 writers, continually snarle estate; wanteth nothing
 strong monarch, neverthelesse certain
 tyrannophobia, feare strongly governed, him,
 abhorre.
 
doctors, hold three soules man;
 also think may soules, (that is, more
 soveraigns,) one, common-wealth; set supremacy
 soveraignty; canons lawes; ghostly authority
 civill; working mens minds, words distinctions,
 signifie nothing, bewray (by obscurity)
 walketh (as think invisibly) another kingdome, it
 kingdome fayries, dark. now seeing manifest, that
 civill power, power common-wealth same
 thing; supremacy, power making canons, granting
 faculties, implyeth common-wealth; followeth, one is
 soveraign, another supreme; one can make lawes, another
 make canons; must needs two common-wealths, one & same
 subjects; kingdome divided selfe, stand. for
 notwithstanding insignificant distinction temporall, ghostly,
 still two kingdomes, every subject subject two
 masters. seeing ghostly power challengeth right declare
 sinne challengeth consequence declare law,
 (sinne nothing transgression law;) again, the
 civill power challenging declare law, every subject must
 obey two masters, bothe will commands observed law;
 impossible. or, one kingdome, either civill,
 power common-wealth, must subordinate the
 ghostly; ghostly must subordinate temporall then
 supremacy temporall. therefore two powers
 oppose one another, common-wealth great danger
 civill warre, dissolution. civill authority more
 visible, standing cleerer light naturall reason cannot
 choose draw times considerable part the
 people: spirituall, though stand darknesse schoole
 distinctions, hard words; yet fear darknesse, and
 ghosts, greater fears, want party sufficient to
 trouble, sometimes destroy common-wealth. disease
 unfitly may compared epilepsie, falling-sicknesse
 (which jewes took one kind possession spirits) the
 body naturall. disease, unnaturall spirit,
 wind head obstructeth roots nerves, moving
 violently, taketh away motion naturally have
 power soule brain, thereby causeth violent,
 irregular motions (which men call convulsions) parts;
 insomuch seized therewith, falleth sometimes the
 water, sometimes fire, man deprived senses;
 also body politique, spirituall power, moveth the
 members common-wealth, terrour punishments, hope of
 rewards (which nerves it,) otherwise civill power
 (which soule common-wealth) moved; by
 strange, hard words suffocates people, either overwhelm
 common-wealth oppression, cast fire civill
 warre.
 



mixt government
 
sometimes also meerly civill government, than
 one soule: power levying mony, (which nutritive
 faculty,) depended generall assembly; power conduct and
 command, (which motive faculty,) one man; power of
 making lawes, (which rationall faculty,) accidentall
 consent, onely two, also third; endangereth
 common-wealth, somtimes want consent good lawes; most
 often want nourishment, necessary life, motion.
 although perceive, government, government,
 division common-wealth three factions, call it
 mixt monarchy; yet truth is, one independent
 common-wealth, three independent factions; one representative
 person, three. kingdome god, may three persons
 independent, without breach unity god reigneth; men
 reigne, subject diversity opinions, so. and
 therefore king bear person people, generall
 assembly bear also person people, another assembly bear
 person part people, one person, one
 soveraign, three persons, three soveraigns.
 
disease naturall body man, may exactly compare this
 irregularity common-wealth, know not. seen man, that
 another man growing side, head, armes, breast,
 stomach, own: another man growing his
 side, comparison might exact.
 



want mony
 
hitherto named diseases common-wealth, the
 greatest, present danger. other, great; which
 neverthelesse unfit observed. first, difficulty of
 raising mony, necessary uses common-wealth; especially
 approach warre. difficulty ariseth opinion, that
 every subject hath propriety lands goods, exclusive of
 soveraigns right use same. whence commeth to
 passe, soveraign power, foreseeth necessities and
 dangers common-wealth, (finding passage mony the
 publique treasure obstructed, tenacity people,) whereas
 extend selfe, encounter, prevent dangers in
 beginnings, contracteth selfe long can, it
 longer, struggles people strategems law, obtain
 little summes, sufficing, fain last violently to
 open way present supply, perish; put often these
 extremities, last reduceth people due temper; else
 common-wealth must perish. insomuch may compare distemper
 aptly ague; wherein, fleshy parts congealed, or
 venomous matter obstructed; veins naturall course
 empty heart, (as be) supplyed
 arteries, whereby succeedeth first cold contraction,
 trembling limbes; afterwards hot, strong endeavour
 heart, force passage bloud; can do
 that, contenteth selfe small refreshments things as
 coole time, till (if nature strong enough) break last
 contumacy parts obstructed, dissipateth venome into
 sweat; (if nature weak) patient dyeth.
 



monopolies abuses publicans
 
again, sometimes common-wealth, disease, which
 resembleth pleurisie; is, treasure the
 common-wealth, flowing due course, gathered together in
 much abundance, one, private men, monopolies, by
 farmes publique revenues; manner blood a
 pleurisie, getting membrane breast, breedeth an
 inflammation, accompanied fever, painfull stitches.
 



popular men
 
also, popularity potent subject, (unlesse common-wealth
 good caution fidelity,) dangerous disease; because
 people (which receive motion authority the
 soveraign,) flattery, reputation ambitious man,
 drawn away obedience lawes, follow man, of
 whose vertues, designes knowledge. commonly
 danger popular government, monarchy; may
 easily made believe, people. means was, that
 julius caesar, set people senate, having
 won himselfe affections army, made himselfe master, both
 senate people. proceeding popular, ambitious men,
 plain rebellion; may resembled effects witchcraft.
 



excessive greatnesse town, multitude corporations
 
another infirmity common-wealth, immoderate greatnesse a
 town, able furnish circuit, number, and
 expence great army: also great number corporations; which
 many lesser common-wealths bowels greater,
 like wormes entrayles naturall man.
 



liberty disputing soveraign power
 
may added, liberty disputing absolute power,
 pretenders politicall prudence; though bred most
 part lees people; yet animated false doctrines, are
 perpetually medling fundamentall lawes, molestation
 common-wealth; like little wormes, physicians call
 ascarides.
 
may adde, insatiable appetite, bulimia, enlarging
 dominion; incurable wounds thereby many times received from
 enemy; wens, ununited conquests, many times a
 burthen, lesse danger lost, kept; also lethargy of
 ease, consumption riot vain expence.
 



dissolution common-wealth
 
lastly, warre (forraign, intestine,) enemies got a
 final victory; (the forces common-wealth keeping field
 longer) farther protection subjects loyalty;
 common-wealth dissolved, every man liberty protect
 himselfe courses discretion shall suggest unto him.
 soveraign, publique soule, giving life motion the
 common-wealth; expiring, members governed more,
 carcasse man, departed (though immortal) soule. for
 though right soveraign monarch extinguished the
 act another; yet obligation members may. that
 wants protection, may seek anywhere; hath it, obliged
 (without fraudulent pretence submitted himselfe fear,)
 protect protection long able. power of
 assembly suppressed, right perisheth utterly;
 assembly selfe extinct; consequently, no
 possibility soveraignty re-enter.

intended done, care applyed to

duty soveraign relinquish essentiall right of
 soveraignty see people taught grounds them
 
because, essentiall rights soveraignty (specified before

 essentiall rights; thereby men easie be

 use exercise.
 
grounds rights, rather need diligently,

 were, found place, other;
 whereas see, hitherto common-wealth, where

 time, industry, produce every day new knowledge. art
